1001 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Prosecutor of Middlesex County


A-229-90T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


255 N.J. Super. 333; 605 A.2d 265; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 141


January 14, 1992, Submitted  
April 8, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION APRIL 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Decision of the Public Employment Relations Commission.



DISPOSITION: The PERC decision is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecutor sought review of the decision of the Public Employment Relations Commission (New Jersey), in an action brought by appellee union and which held that appellant was in violation of the New Jersey Employer-Employee Relations Act, and ordered remedial action.


OVERVIEW: Appellee union filed an unfair practice charge against appellant prosecutor. The Public Employment Relations Commission (PERC) found that appellant violated the New Jersey Employer-Employee Relations Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 34:13A-5.4(a)(1), (a)(5), when it unilaterally stopped granting newly hired employees credit for prior governmental service. The PERC ordered appellant to reinstate the credit for prior employees represented by appellee, apply credit to all eligible members, and negotiate with appellee regarding any future attempts to rescind credit. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the PERC and held that rescinding the credit for prior governmental service was an illegal unilateral change, because appellant failed to negotiate any change in the existing agreement with appellee. The court held that appellant had the duty to maintain terms and conditions of employment and to bargain in good faith with appellee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Public Employment Relations Commission finding that appellant prosecutor violated the New Jersey Employer-Employee Relations Act. The court held that rescinding the credit for prior governmental service was an illegal unilateral change, because appellant failed to negotiate any change in the existing agreement with appellee union.

 

1002 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


N.M. v. J.G.


A-859-91T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


255 N.J. Super. 423; 605 A.2d 709; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 122


January 22, 1992, Argued  
March 30, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Chancery Division, Family Part, Monmouth County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant putative father challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Chancery Division, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which directed defendant to submit to a blood test to determine paternity of a child born during plaintiff mother's marriage to the presumed father in plaintiff's action for child support.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother received child support from the presumed father for a child born during their marriage. Later, plaintiff informed the child that defendant putative father was the child's biological father and sought child support payments from defendant. Defendant denied paternity. The trial court ordered plaintiff, defendant, the child, and the presumed father to submit to a blood test. The trial court dismissed plaintiff's claim, sua sponte, amended the complaint to include the child, and appointed an ad litem for the child. On appeal, the court held that plaintiff's claim was barred by the entire controversy doctrine because the paternity claim should have been joined with the divorce suit. Plaintiff's claim was also barred by judicial estoppel because her assertion of the presumed father's paternity was inconsistent with her assertion of defendant's paternity of the same child. Also, the child's claim was not barred by plaintiff's preclusion, collateral estoppel, or res judicata because there was no privity. The court held that requiring defendant to submit to a blood test was premature because the presumption of the presumed father's paternity had not been rebutted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff mother's action for child support against defendant putative father because it was barred by the entire controversy doctrine and judicial estoppel. The court reversed the order requiring defendant father to submit to a blood test because the presumption of the presumed father's paternity had not been rebutted.

 

1003 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Jones


A-3959-90T3G


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


255 N.J. Super. 213; 604 A.2d 970; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 100


January 8, 1992, Argued  
March 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey Law Division, Cumberland County.



DISPOSITION: The judgment appealed from is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow challenged the ruling by the Superior Court of New Jersey Law Division, Cumberland County, which denied plaintiff's application for disinterment of her late husband's remains and asserted that she had a right to disinterment over the objections of her estranged children.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff widow sought review of the trial court's denial of her request to disinter her deceased husband's body from a cemetery that was not properly maintained. Plaintiff asserted that N.J. Stat. Ann. 8A:5-20 authorized disinterment without a showing of good cause, the requirement that her children's' consent was inapplicable because she was estranged from them and their father, her deceased husband, had disinherited them, and the trial court erred when it applied "urgent necessity" instead of "good cause" as a condition for disinterment. The court affirmed the order and found that the statute permitted disinterment without recourse to a court when the requisite consents were forthcoming, but it did not preclude a court order for disinterment in an appropriate case even over the objection of a spouse or adult child. Plaintiff failed to establish good cause for her application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court denying plaintiff widow's required to disinter her deceased husband's body from a cemetery because based upon the facts of the case, plaintiff failed to establish good cause for her application to disinter.

 

1004 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Upper Deerfield Tp. v. Seabrook Housing Corp.


A-3580-90T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


255 N.J. Super. 218; 604 A.2d 972; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 119


December 16, 1991, Argued  
March 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 9, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cumberland County whose opinion is reported at     N.J. Super.    .



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff township challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Cumberland County, which held that Upper Deerfield Township, N.J., Township Code ch. 50, art. III, § 7 (1989) was unconstitutional and that defendant property owner did not have to obtain a certificate of occupancy prior to selling property that included a vacant house.


OVERVIEW: Defendant property owner transferred title to the purchaser without obtaining a certificate of occupancy as required by Upper Deerfield Township, N.J., Township Code ch. 50, art. III, § 7 (1989). The purchaser assumed the obligation of obtaining the certificate and making any required repairs to a vacant house on the property. Defendant was found guilty of violating the ordinance, fined, and ordered to comply with the ordinance within two weeks. On defendant's application for a de novo trial, the judge raised the issue of the constitutionality of the ordinance. The trial court held that § 7 was invalid, and the court affirmed and dismissed the complaint against defendant. The court held that the ordinance interfered with defendant's right to acquire, own, and dispose of real property, a right that was within the protections of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.J. Const. art. I, § 1. The reasonable exercise of police power was allowed; but the court held that the ordinance's regulatory reach was overbroad because in requiring an occupancy permit before an abandoned vacant structure could be sold the ordinance bore no real and substantial relationship to legitimate government purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that plaintiff township's ordinance requiring defendant property owner to obtain a certificate of occupancy prior to selling property that included a vacant house was unconstitutional and dismissed the complaint against defendant because the overbroad ordinance unconstitutionally interfered with defendant's right to acquire, own, and dispose of real property.

 

1005 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


GE Solid State, Inc. v. Director, Div. of Taxation


A-1530-90T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


254 N.J. Super. 653; 604 A.2d 189; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 96


January 27, 1992, Argued  
March 17, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication April 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Tax Court of New Jersey, whose opinion is reported at 11 N.J. Tax 320 (1990).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation challenged the decision of the Tax Court of New Jersey, which affirmed an assessment of a use tax deficiency against it, and asserted that the equipment in question was exempt from use tax pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:32B-32B-1 et seq., Sales and Use Tax Act.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporation sought review of the denial of its requested exemption of machinery and equipment it asserted was used directly in the manufacture of consumer products. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial and found that the assessment against plaintiff was proper. The court found that the equipment and machinery in question was not used directly in the manufacture of goods to be sold to the consumer. The equipment and machinery was used to manufacture goods that were sold to consumers on which sales taxes were collected. Under the N.J. Stat. Ann. 54:32B-1 et seq. Sales and Use Tax Act, exemptions required that the machinery was used "directly" and primarily" in the production process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court because the equipment plaintiff corporation sought to exempt from use taxes was not used directly in the production process therefore it was not exempt from use taxes.

 

1006 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


African Council v. Hadge


A-3894-90T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


255 N.J. Super. 4; 604 A.2d 604; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 106


February 18, 1992, Argued  
March 13, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant protestors challenge an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which denied appellants' application for counsel fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, contending that they were "prevailing parties" in an action to enforce their civil rights and that they were entitled to have their attorney's fees paid for obtaining an order directing respondent township and its manager issue a permit to march in the street.


OVERVIEW: Appellant protesters filed suit against respondent township and its manager arising out of respondents' failure to issue a special events permit to appellants for a protest march in a street. The trial court required respondents to issue a permit to appellants for a march to be conducted in the street, and it denied appellants' application for attorney's fees and costs, finding that the issue before the trial court was not a substantial, constitutional issue. The court reversed the trial court's order denying counsel fees and costs. The court held that when the trial judge concluded that the refusal to issue a permit to march in the street violated the federal Constitution, by implication there was also a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because defendants acted under color of the municipal code to deprive plaintiffs of their constitutional right to march peacefully in the street. The court held that appellants were prevailing parties within the contemplation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The court determined that the trial court's denial of counsel fees was a mistaken exercise of discretion because there were no special circumstances that would render award of counsel fees unjust.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that denied appellant protesters' application for attorney's fees and costs, finding that appellants were prevailing parties in an action to enforce their Constitutional right to protest under color of local law and that there existed no special circumstances to render an award of attorney's fees unjust.

 

1007 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gonzalez


A-2548-90T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


254 N.J. Super. 300; 603 A.2d 516; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 64


February 11, 1992, Submitted  
February 25, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County.



DISPOSITION: The convictions are affirmed and the matter is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her convictions from the Superior Court of Passaic County (New Jersey), for possession of heroin with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of school property, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7, and questioned the constitutionality of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-12, which permitted a court to waive a mandatory sentence only with the approval of the prosecutor. Defendant had entered a plea agreement, but tried to withdraw her pleas.


OVERVIEW: In reviewing defendant's drug convictions, the court found that the trial judge meticulously adhered to the rules in accepting defendant's guilty plea. The court found that defendant candidly acknowledged guilt and was questioned exhaustively concerning the plea agreement, and that the judge accepted her plea only after satisfying himself that her decision not to contest the charges was made voluntarily and with knowledge of her alternatives and options. Consequently, the court held that there was no abuse of discretion in denying defendant's motion to withdraw her pleas. The court also held that the judiciary was not deprived of its sentencing powers and that the statutes did not unlawfully delegate sentencing responsibility to the executive branch. However, the court recommended that guidelines and standards be adopted in conjunction with the prosecutor's statutory power to waive a mandatory sentence. Because the trial court did not have the benefit of a recent case, the court decided, in the interest of justice, to remand for reconsideration, so that defendant could challenge the prosecutor's exercise of discretion as arbitrary and capricious. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings, because in the interest of justice, the court gave defendant an opportunity to challenge the prosecutor's exercise of discretion as arbitrary and capricious and the trial court an opportunity to apply a recent case.

 

1008 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


O'Keefe v. Passaic Valley Water Com'n


A-1735-90T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


253 N.J. Super. 569; 602 A.2d 760; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 35; 7 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 354; 122 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P57,036


October 22, 1991, Argued  
February 7, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 24, 1992. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant water commission sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Passaic County, declaring that appellant's policy of pre-employment drug testing violated the Constitutions of both the United States and the state of New Jersey and respondent prospective employee cross-appealed the dismissal of his claim for relief under federal and state civil rights legislation, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-1.


OVERVIEW: Respondent prospective employee filed suit against appellant water commission, claiming relief under both state and federal civil rights legislation, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-1 et seq., contending that appellant refused to hire him as a water meter reader because he refused to submit to a pre-employment drug test. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment declaring that appellant's policy of pre-employment drug testing violated the U.S. Cons. amend. IV. The court also affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing respondent's claims for punitive damages and attorney's fees since the court determined that appellant's reasons for not hiring respondent were independent of his refusal of the drug testing. The court found that the record failed to support the required nexus between positive drug testing and the risk of meter reader criminality on the job, as such the risk to the public safety by reason of an employee's impaired judgment due to drug use was minimal and could not sustain a policy of involuntary drug testing by appellant. The court concluded that drug testing was not an indispensable screening device for achieving a trustworthy work force.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing respondent prospective employee's claims and declaring that appellant water commission's policy of pre-employment drug testing was unconstitutional. The court found that the record failed to support a nexus between positive drug testing and the risk of employee criminality on the job, as such, a policy of a drug-free workforce was not sufficient to overcome Fourth Amendment protection.

 

1009 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Wyzykowski v. Rizas


A-123-90T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


254 N.J. Super. 28; 603 A.2d 53; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 47


October 30, 1991, Argued  
February 3, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant objectors sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, which reversed in part the decision to approve respondent mayor's application concerning the development of a vacant property and remanded the matter to respondent planning board to conduct a new application process. Respondent mayor also sought review of the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The approval of respondent mayor's application for site plan approval and a bulk variance for a combination office and apartment building by respondent planning board, over the opposition of appellant objectors, was reversed in part and remanded for a new application process to be conducted. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court with one modification. The court concluded that respondent planning board should again consider the issue of whether respondent mayor's proposal required a use variance per N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-70(d) and zoning board approval. The court concluded that the peculiarity of the relevant ordinance and the particularized circumstances of the unique community required a complete reconsideration of the application. The highly discretionary nature of the many questions raised during the course of the application procedure, the rigorous contest of the issues at each level, and the pertinent legal authorities all counseled a new consideration of the issues, free from potential taint. The court determined that respondent mayor was under no necessity or compulsion to seize upon and promote development opportunities during his term of office.


OUTCOME: The judgment remanding the matter was affirmed with the modification that respondent planning board should also reconsider the issue of whether respondent mayor's proposal met the accessory use standard in the local ordinance or required a use variance as contended by appellant objectors. A complete reconsideration of the application was required. Respondent mayor was to submit an entirely new application to respondent planning board.

Byrd v. Manning


A-5911-89T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


253 N.J. Super. 307; 601 A.2d 770; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 26


December 10, 1991, Argued  
January 29, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 18, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrested party appealed the decision from the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which entered an order for summary judgment dismissing his action instituted against defendants, mayor and police department, under the federal Civil Rights Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff arrested party appealed from trial court's order for summary judgment dismissing his action instituted against defendants, mayor and police department, under the federal Civil Rights Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Defendant police officers arrested plaintiff outside a local tavern for using offensive language. Plaintiff was charged with disorderly conduct, resisting arrest, and aggravated assault upon a police officer. Plaintiff filed a cross-criminal complaint against defendants charging them with aggravated assault, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:12-1b(1) and official misconduct, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:30-2. The trial judge found the action was time-barred under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-2. Plaintiff was convicted of simple assault and acquitted on the resisting arrest charges. On appeal, the court held that there was no showing that the state's pursuit of the criminal complaint against plaintiff was for the purpose of deterring or inhibiting his civil action against defendants. Further, the court held that there had been no showing that plaintiff was deprived of his freedom of will to justify a tolling of the statute. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff arrested party's civil rights claim because there had been no showing that plaintiff was deprived of his freedom of will to justify a tolling of the statute.

 

1011 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moscato


A-6076-90T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


253 N.J. Super. 253; 601 A.2d 743; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 16


December 3, 1991, Argued  
January 21, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 14, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Passaic County, which dismissed the indictment charging that defendants commenced or continued operation of a sanitary landfill facility without having a tariff therefor filed with and approved by the board of public utilities, contrary to the provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:13A-6.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with commencing or continuing operation of a sanitary landfill facility without having a tariff therefor filed and approved by the board of public utilities, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:13A-6.1. The trial court entered an order dismissing the indictment on the basis that defendants disposed of solid waste on their own property, and the state appealed. The court affirmed the trial court's order, holding that § 48:13A-6.1 was inapplicable to defendants because the property upon which defendants disposed of solid waste was not a "permitted" sanitary landfill, and only "permitted" sanitary landfills were required to file tariffs. The court determined that the trial court should not have dismissed the indictment on the ground that defendants were disposing of waste on their own property because it was unclear whether disposal on one's own property required a certificate of public necessity and the filing of a tariff.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the indictment against defendants for failure to file a tariff for solid waste disposal, rejecting the trial court's reasoning that the indictment should be dismissed because defendants disposed of solid waste on their own property, and holding that because defendants were not operating a "permitted" solid waste disposal facility, they were not required to file a tariff.

 

1012 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Ragan v. Dukes


A-3971-90T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


253 N.J. Super. 246; 601 A.2d 739; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 13


October 29, 1991, Argued  
January 17, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the judgment under review is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, tractor trailer driver and his wife, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which dismissed their personal injury negligence action against defendants, truck driver and truck owner, on the ground that their action was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, tractor trailer driver and his wife, brought a personal injury action against defendants, truck driver and truck owner. The trial court dismissed the action on the ground that it was barred by the two-year statute of limitations, and plaintiffs appealed. The court found that plaintiffs' action was time-barred because the amended tolling statute extending limitations periods against nonresidents, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-22, was unconstitutional from the date on which the United States Supreme Court declared a similar statute of another state unconstitutional on commerce clause grounds. Consequently, since plaintiffs instituted this action more than two years after the accident and more than two years after the date when the amended tolling statute was considered unconstitutional, plaintiffs' claims were considered time-barred. The trial court's decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the personal injury action brought by plaintiffs, tractor trailer driver and his wife, against defendants, truck driver and truck owner, holding that the action was time-barred because plaintiffs brought their action after the tolling statute was considered unconstitutional.

 

1013 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sepulveda


A-1842-90T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


253 N.J. Super. 447; 602 A.2d 273; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 30


October 21, 1991, Submitted  
January 13, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.



DISPOSITION: The judgment under review is reversed and the matter is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a sentence by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Camden County, which imposed a five-year sentence with a three year period of parole ineligibility after defendant violated his probation for the offense of distribution of cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed a five-year sentence with a three-year period of parole ineligibility. Defendant pleaded guilty to distribution of cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school, and the state waived the mandatory period of parole ineligibility unless defendant committed a probation violation. The presumptive term would have been four years. Defendant violated probation, and the state argued that its waiver was for the initial plea only. The court reversed the sentence and held that the trial court was not bound by a plea agreement that attempted to bind it to revoke probation and impose a jail term simply because there was a violation of probation. The trial court had to determine whether defendant's violations warranted a revocation of his probation. Even if a revocation of probation was warranted, the trial court had to weigh the aggravating and mitigating factors at the time of the initial sentencing to determine whether to impose the presumptive sentence or one that was more appropriate. The trial judge could not have increased the presumptive term unless he found that the preponderance of aggravating factors weighed in favor of a higher term and the weighing process did not occur.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's five-year sentence with a three-year period of parole ineligibility for allegedly violating the conditions of his probation distribution of cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school. The trial court was unable to increase the presumptive term unless it found that the preponderance of aggravating factors weighed in favor of a higher term, and that weighing process did not occur.

 

1014 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


809-811 Washington Street Associates v. Grego


A-1533-90T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


253 N.J. Super. 34; 600 A.2d 1222; 1992 N.J. Super. LEXIS 3


October 8, 1991, Argued  
January 9, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 29, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Special Civil Part, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord challenged the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Special Civil Part, Hudson County which dismissed the complaints concluding that plaintiff failed to comply with various provisions of the Anti-Eviction Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.1 to 2A:18-61.12, and its implementing regulations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landlord appealed from the dismissal of the complaints for eviction against defendant tenants. The court reversed and held that plaintiff had complied in all respects with the requirements of the Anti-Eviction Act and its implementing regulations. The court was satisfied that plaintiff's notice of intention clearly informed defendants of their right to purchase their units. Service by mail was deemed complete upon mailing rather than upon receipt so 61 days elapsed between plaintiff's mailing of the notice of intention and the notice of eviction. Further, plaintiff clearly complied with the requirement of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.2(g) that three years' notice be given prior to the institution of the action. Although the trial court found that plaintiff failed to include a summary of tenants' rights approved by the Department of Community Affairs (DCA) with the notice of intention, the court disagreed and found that the regulation clearly indicated that if the notice of intention was accompanied by a copy of DCA's regulations governing condominium conversions, an approved summary of tenants' rights was not required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which dismissed plaintiff landlord's complaints for eviction against defendant tenants because plaintiff properly complied with the Anti-Eviction Act and its implementing regulations. The court remanded the case for further proceedings in conformity with the opinion.

 

1015 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Santiago


A-1855-90T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


253 N.J. Super. 197; 601 A.2d 714; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 439


December 2, 1991, Submitted  
December 24, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 21, 1992.
Certification granted by State v. Santiago, 130 N.J. 7, 611 A.2d 647, 1992 N.J. LEXIS 671 (1992)
Certification denied by State v. Santiago, 130 N.J. 396, 614 A.2d 618, 1992 N.J. LEXIS 952 (1992)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by, Sub nomine at State v. Shaw, 131 N.J. 1, 618 A.2d 294, 1993 N.J. LEXIS 19 (1993)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Camden County, which automatically imposed of a period of parole ineligibility due to defendant's failure to appear in court after he pleaded guilty to possession with intent to distribute cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession with intent to distribute cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7. The state recommended a three year probationary sentence with 364 days to be served in the county jail as a condition of probation contingent upon defendant appearing for sentencing. Defendant failed to appear for sentencing and was sentenced to four years in the custody imprisonment, with three years to be served before he was eligible for parole. The court remanded the case and held that the trial court was to give defendant the opportunity to renegotiate or withdraw his plea. The court held that the only authorized sentence for a § 2C:35-7 violation required a mandatory ineligibility term, except and only to the extent that the state recommended otherwise under N.J. Stat. Ann § 2C:35-12 and the trial judge accepted the recommendation. The court ruled that defendant was unable to obtain the benefit of his bargain after he dishonored his commitment to appear for sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court remanded defendant's sentence for possession with intent to distribute cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property to the trial court so as to give defendant the opportunity to renegotiate or withdraw his plea. The court held that because defendant failed to show for sentencing he was unable to obtain the benefit of his bargain after he dishonored his commitment to appear for sentencing.

 

1016 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shaw


A-0925-90T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


253 N.J. Super. 187; 601 A.2d 709; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 412


November 6, 1991, Submitted  
December 10, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which sentenced him to a four-year term of imprisonment with a mandatory three-year parole ineligibility after defendant failed to appear at his sentencing hearing. The state withdrew its recommendation of a one-year period of parole ineligibility pursuant to a plea agreement under which defendant was convicted of distribution of cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property.


OVERVIEW: Under a plea agreement, defendant was convicted of distribution of cocaine in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7, with a recommendation that he receive a one-year period of parole ineligibility rather than the mandated three-year period. Defendant violated a condition of the agreement when he failed to appear at his sentencing hearing and the state withdrew its recommendation. At sentencing, defendant received the mandated three-year period and the trial court announced it found no aggravating or mitigating factors for his nonappearance. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, but remanded so that the parole eligibility period could be reduced to one-year. The court held that the trial court erred in automatically applying the nonappearance condition to sentence defendant to the mandatory term in light of its specific finding that no aggravating factors applied. The court found that the nonappearance condition in the agreement, if enforceable, placed an additional limitation on the judiciary's already severely circumscribed sentencing authority. The court held that defendant's claim that the applicable statutes were unconstitutional was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the distribution of cocaine, but remanded for the entry of an amended judgment reflecting the reduction of the parole eligibility period from three years to one year. The court held that the trial court erred in automatically applying the nonappearance condition in the plea agreement to increase the period as no aggravating or mitigating factors applied.

 

1017 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Saldana v. City of Camden


A-5006-90T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


252 N.J. Super. 188; 599 A.2d 582; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 389


October 1, 1991, Argued  
December 2, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 19, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and city employees, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Camden County, which granted class certification to plaintiff property owners in their class action suit for property damage or anticipated damage from fires that were started in abandoned dwellings owned by defendants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners brought a class action suit against defendants, city and city employees, seeking damages and injunctive and declaratory relief for property damage that resulted from fires that originated in abandoned buildings owned by defendant city. Plaintiffs obtained class certification from the trial court, and defendants took issue. The court found that plaintiffs satisfied the threshold requirements for a class action, which were numerosity, commonality, typicality, and adequacy of representation. However, the court reversed because plaintiffs failed to meet any of three requirements under N.J. Ct. R. 4:32-1(b). First, the prosecution of separate actions would not have resulted in incompatible standards of conduct. Second, there was no showing that an adjudication of an individual case would, as a practical matter, dispose of other class members' claims, or that a single adjudication would have a dispositive impact involving a joint or common right. Third, the court found that questions of law or fact common to class members did not predominate over questions affecting individuals, or that a class action was superior to other means necessary for fair adjudication.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order, which granted class certification to plaintiff class members in their action for property damages against defendants, city and city employees, because, although plaintiffs met the threshold requirements to having the basis of a class action lawsuit, they failed to meet any of three further requirements for certification.

 

1018 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Allstate Ins. Co.


A-2465-90T3, A-2825-90T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


252 N.J. Super. 280; 599 A.2d 916; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 395


November 7, 1991, Argued  
November 27, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, whose opinion is reported at 246 N.J.Super. 42.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurers sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, ruling that N.J. Rev. Stat. § 39:6A-8.1 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff passengers filed suit seeking recovery under the no-fault insurance law. However, plaintiffs were not able to meet the verbal threshold to recover for non-economic loss as required by N.J. Rev. Stat. § 39:6A-8.1. Plaintiffs sought and were granted a summary judgment in the trial court. The trial court found that § 39:6A-8.1violated the equal protection clause because owners, operators, and their household members did not have to meet the threshold. On review, the court reversed, finding that the statute was not unconstitutional in that the goal of not raising premiums while expanding coverage was rationally related to a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding of the trial court that the statute requiring non-owners and operators of a vehicle to meet a verbal threshold to recover for non-economic loss was unconstitutional. Instead, the court found that the statute was rationally related to a state interest of expanding coverage without raising premiums.

 

1019 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


C.J. v. Vuinovich


A-1454-90T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


252 N.J. Super. 122; 599 A.2d 548; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 382; 2 Am. Disabilities Cas. (BNA) 1175


October 29, 1991, Submitted  
November 22, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 19, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a former member of the New Jersey National Guard, appealed an order by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which rendered summary judgment against him and in favor of defendants, the New Jersey Department of Defense, New Jersey Militia, Army National Guard, and a sergeant, in plaintiff's action under the New Jersey Tort Claims Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:9-2, for emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a former member of the New Jersey National Guard (Guard), was told by defendant sergeant in front of his company members that he had been discharged from the National Guard due to AIDS. Plaintiff filed suit under the New Jersey Tort Claims Act (NJTCA), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:9-2, and other statutes, and the trial court granted summary judgment for defendants, the New Jersey Department of Defense, New Jersey Militia, Army National Guard, and the sergeant. The court affirmed, and held that defendant sergeant's conduct was within the scope of his official duties, and that therefore he had immunity. Plaintiff did not have a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because his allegations were against defendant Army National Guard, which was not a "person" under the statute. He failed to make out a case under the New Jersey Law Against Discrimination (NJLAD), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-4.1, because plaintiff's discharge was compelled by Army regulations, and any state action to the contrary would have violated the Supremacy Clause of the U.S. Const. art. VI, cl. 2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment against plaintiff, a former member of the New Jersey National Guard, because defendant sergeant's comment, which was the basis for plaintiff's cause of action, was made within the course of official duties, so that the military immunity doctrine applied. Plaintiff could not maintain an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; defendant Army National Guard was not a covered "person."

 

1020 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Matter of Market Transition Facility of New Jersey


A-4634-90T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


252 N.J. Super. 260; 599 A.2d 906; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 381


October 28, 1991, Argued  
November 19, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Department of Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of an order of respondent Commissioner of the Department of Insurance (New Jersey), which denied appellant a role in the proceedings that lead to the order setting automobile insurance premiums of the Market Transition Facility, and set the rate order.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer applied for leave to intervene in respondent Commissioner of the Department of Insurance's ratemaking process, which set automobile insurance premiums of the Market Transition Facility (MTF). Respondent denied appellant's application. On appeal, the court reversed the order that excluded appellant from the ratemaking process and ordered respondent to take immediate action to set proper MTF rates. The court found that respondent, who set the rates at a loss-producing level, had a duty to set the rates on a break-even basis. The court additionally found that respondent had not adopted procedures for the filing and approval of changes in MTF rates as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-11c(3). The court ordered respondent to establish a brief timetable for preparation of a meeting with the interested parties, a forthcoming response to legitimate demand for relevant records of respondent, and a procedure suited to the protection of the rights of all interested parties. Respondent was to determine the manner of proceeding in the reconsideration of the MTF rates.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of respondent Commissioner of the Department of Insurance, which excluded appellant insurer from the ratemaking process of automobile insurance premiums of the Market Transition Facility (MTF), because respondent had not adopted procedures for the filing and approval of changes in MTF rates as required by statute. The court ordered respondent to take immediate action to set the proper MTF rates.

 

1021 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Am. Reliance Ins. Co.


No. A-27-90T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


251 N.J. Super. 541; 598 A.2d 1219; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 358


September 17, 1991, Argued  
October 24, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 15, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from State of New Jersey, Department of Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance companies sought review of a judgment of the Commissioner of Insurance, State of New Jersey, Department of Insurance, which held that assessments under the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 17:33B-1 to -63, applied to all Property Liability Insurance Guarantee Association members, and denied appellants' request for mandatory exemptions under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-55.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurance companies sought a declaration of the Commissioner of Insurance that they were not subject to the assessments imposed by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:30A-8a(9). The commissioner held that assessments under the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 17:33B-1 to -63, applied to all members of the Property Liability Insurance Guarantee Association members (PLIGA). On review, appellants contended that theses assessments were unfair, as appellants did not write automobile insurance, and were not servicing carriers of the New Jersey Full Insurance Underwriting Association (JUA). The court affirmed the decision of the Commissioner of Insurance and held that the impositions constituted a reasonable method of achieving an appropriate governmental objective, to relieve the JUA deficit. The fact that some members of the burdened class did not directly benefit from the JUA system was not sufficient to render the classification unreasonable or arbitrary. Also, it was not an unconstitutional taking of private property without compensation, because insurers were permitted a rate adjustment if necessary to assure a constitutionally adequate return.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Commissioner of Insurance, because the imposition of assessments by the Fair Automobile Insurance Reform Act of 1990 constituted a reasonable method of achieving an adequate governmental objective, and it did not constitute an unlawful taking, because the Commissioner of Insurance could permit a rate adjustment if necessary, though not a dollar for dollar pass-through of the assessments to the insurees.

Delta Chem. Corp. v. Ocean County Utils. Auth.


No. A-2405-89T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


250 N.J. Super. 395; 594 A.2d 1343; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 289


January 9, 1991, Argued  
August 12, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant public entity challenged the order from the Superior Court of Ocean County, New Jersey, which granted a money judgment to plaintiff high bidder for one bid, and plaintiff cross-appealed an order denying recovery on two other bids.


OVERVIEW: Defendant public entity appealed from a money judgment entered in favor of plaintiff high bidder in a public bidding case. Plaintiff filed a cross appeal of the denial of recovery concerning two additional bids. Defendant argued that the Buy-American provision in the Local Public Contracts law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:11-18, was unconstitutional. The court held that the monetary judgment must be reversed because plaintiff was not entitled to recover money damages even when its challenge to an award of a contract was successful. The court affirmed on the cross-appeal and reversed on the appeal because it did not need to address the statute's constitutionality once it reversed the money judgment and found that no equitable relief was feasible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted a money judgment against defendant to plaintiff high bidder. The court affirmed the denial of recovery on plaintiff's additional bids, because plaintiff could only attack the award of the contract and was not entitled to recover money damages.

 

1023 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Engel


Nos. A-5961-85T5, A-5963-85T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


249 N.J. Super. 336; 592 A.2d 572; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 232


November 27, 1990, Argued; November 29, 1990, Remanded; June 11, 1991, Reargued  
July 2, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 16, 1991. As Amended August 9, 1991.
Certification denied by State v. Engel, 130 N.J. 393, 614 A.2d 616, 1991 N.J. LEXIS 1286 (1991)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at State v. Engel, 2012 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 356 (App.Div., Feb. 21, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, which convicted defendants of conspiracy under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:5-2, and murder under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3(a)(1), (2), and sentenced them to life imprisonment rather than imposing the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of conspiracy under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:5-2, and murder under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3(a)(1), (2), and were sentenced to life imprisonment rather than the death penalty; the jury determined that the aggravating factors did not outweigh the mitigating factors, as required under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3(c)(3). Defendants argued that the indictment should have been vitiated due to prosecutorial interference, but the court found that evidence presented by the prosecutor was reasonable, and even if any statements had been erroneous, no prejudice had occurred. Defendants made a constitutional challenge to the death penalty statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3(4)(e), but the court held that since the death penalty was not imposed against defendants, it was questionable whether they had standing to raise a constitutional issue; the statute was nonetheless constitutional. Defendants raised a number of evidentiary arguments, but the court found no merit in the claims. The court affirmed defendants' convictions, holding that substantial evidence of guilt had been presented at trial, and no prejudicial error occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendants for conspiracy and murder, and it affirmed the sentence of life imprisonment, holding that there was no basis for a new trial, no error was committed by the trial court, and defendants' convictions were well deserved.

 

1024 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vasquez


A-4471-89T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


250 N.J. Super. 457; 595 A.2d 520; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 303


April 24, 1991, Argued  
June 21, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION August 28, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Camden County (New Jersey), which imposed a custodial term with three years of parole ineligibility, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7, based on defendant's probation violations. The state had waived the parole ineligibility term when defendant was initially sentenced for violating § 2C:35-7, on the condition that defendant would comply with the terms of his probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession of cocaine with intent to distribute within 1000 feet of school property, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7. As part of a plea agreement, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-12, the state agreed to waive the mandatory three-year parole ineligibility term fixed by § 2C:35-7. In the plea agreement, the state specified that it would not waive the parole ineligibility term if defendant had to be resentenced for violating a condition of his probation. Defendant appealed the trial court's judgment, which imposed the parole ineligibility term on defendant after defendant pleaded guilty to violating his probation. The court determined that after the state waived the parole ineligibility term, § 2C:35-12 could not be used to circumvent the sentencing guidelines established by case law. The court held that defendant was entitled to be resentenced on the probation violation in accordance with the standards set forth in the applicable case law without any mandatory period of parole ineligibility under § 2C:35-7.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter to the trial court so that defendant could be resentenced on the probation violation. The court held that the mandatory period of parole ineligibility could not applied against defendant where the state had waived the parole ineligibility period at the initial sentencing.

 

1025 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


N.J. Builders Ass'n v. Fenske


No. A-2367-89T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


249 N.J. Super. 60; 591 A.2d 1362; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 211


March 4, 1991, Argued  
June 18, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 8, 1991. As Amended September 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the final decision of New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the New Jersey Builders Association, challenged a decision by respondent, the New Jersey Department of Environmental Regulation, to adopt new water quality management planning rules. Appellant claimed that respondent exceeded its statutory grant of authority when it enacted the co-permittee requirement in N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7, §§ 15-4.1 and 14A-2.1(l),(m),(n) and (o).


OVERVIEW: Respondent, the New Jersey Department of Environmental Regulation, adopted new water quality management planning rules. Appellant, the New Jersey Builders Association, challenged N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7, §§ 15-4.1 and 14A-2.1(l),(m),(n) and (o), provided that applications for pollution discharge permits would not be issued unless a governmental body was either the sole or co-permittee. The court deleted the contested regulations, holding that respondent exceeded the scope of its authority. The court rejected respondent's argument that the regulations were necessary to insure proper oversight of the operations of domestic treatment works by experienced governmental bodies. The New Jersey Wastewater Treatment Privatization Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 58:27-1 et seq., had created the option to contract with private-sector firms for the operation of wastewater treatment systems. That the legislature had authorized reliance upon privatization was inconsistent with the co-permittee requirement, which sought to guarantee performance by private firms. The court stayed its deletion of the co-permittee requirements pending enactment of legislation that would implicitly ratify the regulations.


OUTCOME: The court held that respondent, the New Jersey Department of Environmental Regulation, exceeded its statutory authority when it enacted a co-permittee requirement as part of new water quality management planning rules. The requirement was invalid in the absence of legislative authorization. The court stayed its decision until a certain date because there was pending legislation that would provide authorization.

 

1026 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Powell


No. A-2418-90T2F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


250 N.J. Super. 1; 593 A.2d 342; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 264


May 28, 1991, Submitted  
June 12, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County (New Jersey), that suppressed cocaine evidence seized from defendant. Defendant had been driving a car, and a police officer heard loud music from the car and stopped the car for a violation of East Orange, N.J., Code § 184-1. The cocaine was seized when defendant exited the car. Defendant was charged per N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:35-10a(1), 2C:35-5b(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving in his car, and he was stopped by the police. The basis of the stop was an alleged violation of East Orange, N.J., Code § 184-1. Upon exiting the car, a police officer seized cocaine from defendant's pants. Defendant was charged for violations of N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:35-10a(1), 2C:35-5b(3). In the trial court, defendant moved to suppress the cocaine evidence on the basis that § 184-1 was void for vagueness. The trial court granted the motion. The state appealed. The court reversed. Section 184-1 outlawed unnecessary or unusually loud noise that either annoyed, injured, disturbed or endangered the comfort, health, repose, peace, or safety of others or which was so harsh, prolonged, or unusual in its use, time, and place as to annoy, disturb, or endanger the comfort, health, repose, peace, or safety of others. While temporarily on a roadway an electronic device could not be used to unreasonably annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort, peace, or repose of persons in public places. The court found that the terms of § 184-1 enabled persons of common intelligence, in light of ordinary experience, to understand whether or not contemplated conduct was lawful.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the state, the court reversed the trial court's order that suppressed the cocaine evidence found on defendant. The court rejected defendant's contention that the ordinance on which the police stop was based was unconstitutionally vague and therefore void. The court found that the challenged provision fairly apprised the public and defendant of what it proscribed, and it was not void for vagueness.

In re "plan for Orderly Withdrawal" of Twin City Fire Ins. Co.


No. A-114-90T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


248 N.J. Super. 616; 591 A.2d 1005; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 201


March 26, 1991, Argued  
June 11, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 1, 1991.
Certification granted In re "Plan for Orderly Withdrawal from New Jersey" etc., 127 N.J. 548, 606 A.2d 362, 1991 N.J. LEXIS 1049 (1991)
Affirmed by In re "Plan For Orderly Withdrawal from New Jersey" of Twin City Fire Ins. Co., 129 N.J. 389, 609 A.2d 1248, 1992 N.J. LEXIS 419 (1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from New Jersey Department of Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant auto insurance company sought review from a decision of the New Jersey Department of Insurance, which imposed various restrictions pertinent to appellant's attempt to leave the New Jersey private passenger auto insurance market. At issue on appeal was the constitutionality of Section 72 of the Reform Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-30.


OVERVIEW: Appellant auto insurance company wrote auto insurance but decided that it wanted to stop writing new insurance as well current policies. The Commissioner of Insurance attempted to control appellant's activities relative to the withdrawal and imposed restrictions. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-30 (the Act) was reviewed by the New Jersey Department of Insurance, and appellant was required to abide by restrictions including keeping insurance in place until insured's could find other insurance and not writing additional insurance. Appellant sought review and attacked the constitutionality of the Act. On review, the court concluded that the provisions of the Act authorized the Commissioner to require appellant to cease writing other lines of insurance if it chose to withdraw from the private auto insurance market. The court did note that the Commissioner did overstep his authority by imposing restrictions on the ability of appellant's parent company to write life or health insurance as this was not within the purview of the Act. The matter was remanded to permit the Commissioner to reconsider the application for withdrawal to correct to improper restrictions.


OUTCOME: The matter was remanded to permit the Commissioner of Insurance to reconsider appellant auto insurance company's application for withdrawal to correct improper restrictions against appellant's parent company to write life or health insurance, which did not come with the regulations of the Reform Act. The court did note that the provisions of the Act authorized the Commissioner to require appellant to cease writing other auto insurance.

 

1028 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wearing


No. A-3416-89T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


249 N.J. Super. 18; 591 A.2d 1350; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 188


March 6, 1991, Submitted  
June 10, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 25, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to various offenses, including a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7, and he was placed on probation. After violating his probation, defendant disputed the imposition of a sentence of five years in prison by the Superior Court, Camden County (New Jersey). He raised several issues, but the court only dealt with three constitutional issues and whether the mandatory ineligibility term under § 2C:35-7 had to be imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was placed on probation after he pled guilty to various offenses, including a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7. After violating probation, he disputed the imposition of a sentence of five years in prison. The court held that, because defendant was properly advised at the time of plea about his maximum exposure and the mandatory term of his ineligibility for parole upon violation of probation, he had to receive the ineligibility term. However, the length of the ineligibility term depended upon the propriety of the specific term and the quantity of marijuana involved in the violation of § 2C:35-7. That was not developed in the trial court when defendant entered his original guilty plea. Therefore, the court remanded for a determination of the specific term sentence based on consideration of the aggravating and mitigating factors and a determination of the appropriate ineligibility term based on that sentence and the quantity of marijuana involved. Also, on remand the trial court had to clarify the period of the suspension of defendant's driver's license. Defendant had waived any constitutional issues. The court remanded for proceedings consistent with the opinion.


OUTCOME: The court remanded. Defendant had waived the constitutional issues. Because defendant was advised at the time of his plea about his maximum exposure and the mandatory term of his ineligibility for parole upon violation of probation, he had to receive the ineligibility term. However, the terms depended upon the quantity of marijuana involved, which was not determined when he entered his original guilty plea. Therefore, the court remanded.

 

1029 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Aqn Assoc. v. Florence


Nos. A-4965-89T1, A-1346-90T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


248 N.J. Super. 597; 591 A.2d 995; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 202


May 15, 1991, Argued  
June 7, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporate property owner sought reversal of the judgment of the Superior Court, Burlington County (New Jersey), dismissing its complaint seeking to invalidate defendant township's bond ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporate property owner challenged a trial judge's order dismissing its complaint regarding defendant township's bond ordinances. The court affirmed. Defendant township had authorized the issuance of general obligation bonds to refinance its debt to another township. Plaintiff sought to block the issuance of those bonds, contending that defendant township had improperly issued them. The trial judge dismissed the complaint. In upholding the trial judge's decision, the court held that the debt payments made by defendant township, under a regional contribution agreement, were bondable under the Local Bond Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:2-1 et seq. In addition, the court held that a six-year period of repose was a proper useful life, not the 10-year period projected by defendant township; nevertheless, the proper remedy was to deem the maturation period for the bonds to be six years. Finally, the court held that the consideration paid by defendant township was related to a public purpose; thus, the bonds were valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court below was modified and then affirmed. The bond ordinance covered a subject for which bonds could be issued, and the bonds were for a valid public purpose. The maturation date, however, was changed to six years.

 

1030 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Durand Equip. Co. v. Superior Carbon Prods.


No. A-2-90T5F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


248 N.J. Super. 581; 591 A.2d 987; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 189


May 7, 1991, Argued  
June 4, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 25, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant witness appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, which denied his motion for partial summary judgment in action by plaintiff convict and plaintiff wife for defendant's false evidence that resulted in plaintiff convict's criminal conviction. Defendant contended that summary judgment should have been granted because the statements and evidence used in the criminal trial were subject to absolute immunity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant witness appealed the order that denied his motion for summary judgment on counts of plaintiff convict and plaintiff wife's complaint that alleged defendant's false and fraudulent testimony and documents resulted in defendant's conviction for defrauding the United States government. The court reversed the order. The court held that defendant's testimony and documents utilized in preparation of and for the criminal proceedings against plaintiff were absolutely privileged. Defendant was subject to the control of the trial judge and was subject to contempt citations for misbehavior and to prosecution for perjury if he knowingly gave false testimony. The court held that even if defendant gave false testimony and his documents were fabricated, the existence of federal avenues of judicial appeal was sufficient to cure any alleged infirmities in the criminal prosecution.


OUTCOME: The order that denied partial summary judgment was reversed because the statements by defendant witness were made in the course of a criminal judicial proceeding against plaintiff convict and were subject to absolute immunity.

 

1031 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


N.J. Dep't of Envtl. Prot. v. Duran


No. A-4437-89T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


251 N.J. Super. 55; 596 A.2d 1090; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 318


May 7, 1991, Submitted  
May 22, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant offenders sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Monmouth County (New Jersey), which denied appellants' motion to suppress evidence of detached American short lobster tails found in appellants' possession, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 23:5-9b, and which assessed civil penalties.


OVERVIEW: Appellant offenders challenged the judgment that denied their motion to suppress evidence of detached American short lobster tails found in their possession in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 23:5-9b. A confidential informant led state agents to a boat that was ascertained to be the source of the illegal tails. The agents requested and were granted permission to board and search for illegal lobsters. The tails were discovered in a wooden compartment. At trial, civil penalties were assessed against appellants. The court affirmed the judgment and held that one who was engaged in a regulated industry, such as the fishing industry, was on notice that periodic inspections would occur and had no reasonable expectation of privacy in the areas where he knew that inspections would occur. The court held that the search was authorized where there was reason to believe that a violation occurred within the meaning of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 23:10-20. The court also held that the search was valid under the exigent circumstances exception to the warrant requirement because there was cause to believe that the evidence might be destroyed if the boat had been allowed to proceed unimpeded.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the warrantless search of appellant offenders' fishing vessel was valid under the administrative search in a regulated industry exception to the warrant requirement and under the exigent circumstances exception to the warrant requirement.

In re Aetna Casualty & Sur. Co.


Nos. A-2628-90T5F, A-2631-90T5F, A-2783-90T5F (Consolidated)


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


248 N.J. Super. 367; 591 A.2d 631; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 171


March 6, 1991, Argued  
May 20, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication June 19, 1991.
Certification denied by In re Assignment of Exposures to Aetna Casualty & Surety Co., etc., 1991 N.J. LEXIS 931 (N.J., Sept. 18, 1991)
Certification denied by In re Assignment of Exposures to Aetna Cas. & Surety Co., 126 N.J. 385, 599 A.2d 162, 1991 N.J. LEXIS 1314 (1991)
Writ of certiorari denied Allstate Ins. Co. v. Fortunato, 502 U.S. 1121, 112 S. Ct. 1244, 117 L. Ed. 2d 476, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 991 (1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Department of Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurers sought review of the order of the Commissioner of Insurance (New Jersey), which ordered each of them to issue auto policies to thousands of "exposures" (private passenger cars requiring insurance) then insured in the "residual" market through the Joint Underwriting Association.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner of Insurance (commissioner) ordered appellants, insurers who did not meet their quotas, to issue auto insurance policies to those who were at a high risk and were insured under the residual market through the Joint Underwriting Association after the legislature passed statutes replacing it with the Market Transition Facility. The court affirmed and reversed some issues that had not been settled prior to trial. The court affirmed the commissioner's order that first distributed those in underserved geographical areas because it responded to legitimate legislative concerns in a reasonable way that did not unfairly prejudice the insurers. The court reversed the commissioner's order that assigned producers because it contravened N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:33B-9c. The court affirmed the commissioner's order requiring one-year coverage. The court found that appellants had not shown either that they relied on a previous plan or that such reliance was justified and detrimental such as to create a protectable interest against change. The court also found that appellants did not make a sufficient case of unconstitutionality because the results of the plan could not be predicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commissioner of Insurance's orders, except the order which provided for assignment of producers, because the orders responded to legitimate legislative concern in transitioning between two forms of auto insurance.

In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 7:26b


Nos. A-2403-87T1, A-2521-87T1, A-2522-87T1, A-2523-87T1, A-2524-87T1, A-364-89T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


250 N.J. Super. 189; 593 A.2d 1193; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 157


November 15, 1990, Argued  
May 6, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 28, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, chemical industry and environmental groups, challenged the regulations promulgated by respondent Department of Environmental Protection (New Jersey) to implement the Environmental Cleanup Responsibility Act (ECRA), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 13:1K-6 to -14. ECRA imposed on owners of industrial establishments a duty to clean up contamination as a precondition for the sale, transfer, or termination of operations at those facilities.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, industry and environmental groups, challenged regulations of respondent Department of Environmental Protection to enforce the Environmental Cleanup Responsibility Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 13:1K-6 to -14. The Act required industrial sites to clean up contamination as a precondition for the sale, transfer, or termination of operations at those facilities. Appellant industry groups claimed the regulations went beyond the Act and interfered with interstate commerce by regulating business transactions as opposed to dealing with the environment. The court held that protecting the public from contamination was a sufficiently compelling state interest to justify the minimal effect on interstate commerce. The court disallowed the regulations that dealt with certain issues, such as clean up of land adjacent to the industrial site, but as a whole conditionally approved all of the others if, on remand, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7, § 26B-1.9, was amended. The regulation, that permitted owners to seek waiver of the Act as too severe or unjust in their particular circumstances, was too vague. The court remanded for respondent to set appropriate standards within 90 days.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the regulations to enforce the Environmental Cleanup Responsibility Act set by respondent Department of Environmental Protection. The court held some regulations were overreaching, but as a whole conditionally approved them if the regulation regarding waiver of the Act on a case by case basis was amended. The cause was remanded to respondent to set less vague standards for waiver within 90 days.

 

1034 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lagares


No. A-5653-88T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


247 N.J. Super. 392; 589 A.2d 630; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 120


March 12, 1991, Argued  
April 19, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 2, 1991. As Amended June 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cumberland County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Cumberland County that convicted him of possession of a controlled substance, possession with intent to distribute cocaine, and distribution of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance, possession with intent to distribute cocaine, and distribution of cocaine. Pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-6f, the trial court sentenced defendant to seven years imprisonment with a three-year parole ineligibility period. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in allowing evidence of his prior drug convictions to be admitted at trial and that § 2C:43-6f was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. Defendant's prior drug convictions were properly admitted because they had a bearing on defendant's credibility and were not so remote in time to be prejudicial. Section 2C:43-6f did not violate the separation of powers doctrine because it did not transfer the court's sentencing power to the state. The state had to apply for application of such section, but it was within the court's discretion to apply the section. Section 2C:43-6f did not deny defendant due process because it reasonably related to a legitimate state interest and was neither arbitrary nor capricious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence for possession of a controlled substance, possession with intent to distribute cocaine, and distribution of cocaine. The trial court did not err in allowing evidence of his prior drug convictions to be admitted. The statute, which provided for an extended term of imprisonment with a mandatory parole ineligibility term, was constitutional.
