State v. Moore


No. A-6092-89T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


247 N.J. Super. 129; 588 A.2d 889; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 104


March 5, 1991, Argued  
April 4, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 18, 1991. As Amended June 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which, following a trial de novo on the record, found him guilty of consuming an alcoholic beverage while operating a motor vehicle in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-51a. A municipal court had previously found defendant guilty of the offense. Defendant was sentenced as a second offender to 10 days of community service and fined.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of consuming an alcoholic beverage while operating a motor vehicle in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-51a. A police officer came upon defendant's disabled car. During a conversation with defendant, the officer observed alcohol on defendant's breath and noted that defendant's eyes were somewhat red and watery. A passenger exited the car and the officer found two open, cold, beer cans that were half full inside the car. Defendant was sentenced to community service and fined pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-51a(c). On appeal, the court vacated the sentence, as it exceeded the maximum sentence under the statute. The court found that state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant violated § 39:4-51a, as each element required for the presumption of a violation was established. The court held that the presumption created by § 39:4-51a, that a person consumed an alcoholic beverage in violation of the statute where certain conditions were met, was legal. The court found that § 39:4-51a was not unconstitutionally vague, either on its face or as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was vacated and the matter was remanded for resentencing. State proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of consuming an alcoholic beverage while operating a motor vehicle. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague. However, because the imposition of both a fine and community service was in excess of the penalty authorized under the statute, defendant's sentence was illegal.

In re Borough of Roseland


Nos. A-1554-88T3, A-1563-88T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


247 N.J. Super. 203; 588 A.2d 1256; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 86


February 6, 1991, Submitted  
March 26, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication April 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Council on Affordable Housing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Council on Affordable Housing (New Jersey) granted substantive certification to a fair share plan for low income housing. Appellant public advocate challenged the downward adjustment based on insufficient vacant and developable land where a regional contribution agreement satisfied the obligation. Appellant Borough of Roseland contested respondent's interpretation of the occupancy preference under N. J. Admin Code tit. 5, § 92-15.1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant public advocate filed objections to the fair share plan proposed by appellant Borough of Roseland. Respondent Council on Affordable Housing determined the number of low housing units required by appellant borough to meet its fair share obligation and then made a downward adjustment based on the amount of vacant and developable land. On appeal of respondent's grant of substantive certification, appellant public advocate argued that because appellant borough had entered into a regional contribution agreement to satisfy its obligation, the downward adjustment was illegal. Noting statutory provisions that authorized several ways for the obligation to be met, the court held that once the share was determined, no recalculations were required regardless of the option selected. The court further held that the downward adjustment did not require an increase of units in other parts of the region. On appellant borough's proposed occupancy preference, the court held that N.J. Admin. Code tit. 5, § 92-15.1 required the preference to be extended to both local residents and workers. Rejecting appellants' challenge, the court affirmed respondent's grant of substantive certification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent affordable housing council's grant of substantive certification to appellant borough's fair share plan. The court rejected appellant public advocate's claim that the downward adjustment to the required number of units was not justified by appellant's borough choice of a regional contribution agreement to meet its obligation and affirmed respondent's interpretation of the occupancy preference statute.

In re Township of Warren

State v. Roberson


No. A-2601-89T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


246 N.J. Super. 597; 588 A.2d 434; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 89


January 29, 1991, Argued  
March 22, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Passaic County (New Jersey), for second-degree possession of cocaine and possession of cocaine near a school. Defendant challenged the admissibility of the certified laboratory report under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-19(c) and the failure to properly instruct the jury on the weight of the cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Police arrested defendant after observing a drug deal. An analysis of the contents of retrieved vials showed sufficient weight to charge defendant with a second-degree possession offense. Before jury selection, defendant requested the trial court to exclude the certified laboratory report because it did not detail how the vials were weighed. The prosecution responded that defendant failed to give timely notice of objection as required under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-19(c). The trial court admitted the report. On appeal of his convictions, defendant challenged the validity of § 2C:35-19(c) contending that the legislature was without power to enact a rule of evidence. The court held that § 2C:35-19(c) established a procedure for stipulating admission of the report, but was not a rule of evidence that interfered with judicial prerogatives. Because the jury was not instructed to determine whether the amount of cocaine defendant possessed included a sufficient amount of free base, the court affirmed only the three-degree possession near the school conviction and reversed the second-degree conviction remanding for new trial or new sentencing on a lesser third-degree conviction.


OUTCOME: The court held that the pretrial procedure for admitting analysis of controlled substances was valid and affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine near a school. Because the jury did not determine the weight of the cocaine, the court reversed the conviction for second-degree possession remanding for new trial and a new sentence for conviction of a lesser third-degree possession offense.

Lake Shore Estates, Inc. v. Denville Tp. Planning Bd.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


255 N.J. Super. 580; 605 A.2d 1106; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 518


November 26, 1990, Argued  
March 15, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 15, 1991.
Certification denied by Lake Shore Estates, Inc. v. Denville Township Planning Bd., 126 N.J. 335, 598 A.2d 892, 1991 N.J. LEXIS 609 (1991)
Affirmed by Lake Shore Estates, Inc. v. Denville Township Planning Bd., 127 N.J. 394, 605 A.2d 1073, 1992 N.J. LEXIS 36 (1992)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. Cluster issue moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a township, the township planning board, a mayor, and a municipal council, sought review of a decision of a trial court (New Jersey), which held that a "steep slope" ordinance and a zoning ordinance that imposed two-acre minimum lot size in a zone occupied by a tract of land could not be applied in reviewing a preliminary subdivision proposal submitted by respondent developer.


OVERVIEW: Appellants contended that the trial court incorrectly refused to apply the time of decision doctrine when it considered the municipal ordinance. Appellants had amended their zoning ordinance after the developer had set forth litigation against them. The trial court found that the amendments unfairly burdened the developer and rendered useless much of the judicial time that had been spent on the case. The trial court further found that the developer was not required to deal with changing rules which were at least in part a response to the developer's successful litigation. Thus, the trial judge relied upon the special equities exception. The court held that the trial court erred. The record did not show that appellants arbitrarily or capriciously changed the zoning ordinance to frustrate the express grant of a use or subdivision approval by a court in prior litigation. To the contrary, there were valid reasons for the zoning at issue. After weighing the issues, the court held that the zoning ordinance at the time of the decision should have been applied because it would not have undermined existing special equities without accomplishing any offsetting service to the public interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Alvarez

Defendant argued that the sentencing statute N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-6.2, was unconstitutional.

In re New Jersey Medical Malpractice Reinsurance Recovery Fund Surcharge, Adopted New Rules, N.J.A.C. 11:18


Nos. A-2225-89T5, A-2274-89T5, A-2492-89T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


246 N.J. Super. 109; 586 A.2d 1317; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 47


September 17, 1990, Argued  
February 13, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION March 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Department of Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a medical society and individual doctors, challenged the promulgation of a rule by appellee, Department of Insurance, in a dispute over the methodology employed to finance a deficit incurred by a legislatively-created fund to pay certain medical malpractice claims. Appellants contended that a surcharge regulation, N.J. Admin. Code. Tit. 11, § 18-1 et seq., was not valid, based on statutory, constitutional, and evidentiary challenges.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, the Department of Insurance, promulgated a surcharge regulation, N.J. Admin. Code. Tit. 11, § 18-1 et seq., to finance a deficit incurred by the New Jersey Property-Liability Insurance Guaranty Association Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §17:30A-1 et seq. (1974), to pay certain medical malpractice claims, pursuant to the Medical Malpractice Liability Insurance Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:30D-1 et seq., (1976). § 17:30D-1 et seq. Appellant, a medical society and individual doctors, challenged appellee's action, and the court affirmed appellee's adoption of the regulation. The court held that presumptions of validity and reasonableness had been rebutted, and therefore appellee's promulgated regulation was valid based on statutory, constitutional, and evidentiary grounds. Furthermore, the court held that appellee's regulation was accorded presumptions of validity and reasonableness, and appellants failed to meet their burden to establish that it was unreasonable or irrational. Finally, the court noted that where two or more reasonable permissible alternatives existed, the choice exercised by appellee, charged with implementing the regulation, would not be disturbed on appeal.

Tit. 11, § 18-1 et seq., by appellee, Department of Insurance, in an action by appellant, a medical society and individual doctors, over the methodology employed to finance a deficit incurred by a legislatively-created fund to pay certain medical malpractice claims. The court held that the constitutional presumptions of validity and reasonableness were not rebutted.

Aquino Colonial Funeral Home v. Pittari

Matter of Recycling & Salvage Corp.


No. A-2983-89T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


246 N.J. Super. 79; 586 A.2d 1300; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 36


November 20, 1990, Submitted  
February 1, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION February 21, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Board of Public Utilities.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant recycling centers challenged a final administrative action of the New Jersey Board of Public Utilities that found that appellants were without license to operate the business, ordered to cease operations, and imposed penalties for unlicensed operation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant recycling centers challenged an administrative action of the New Jersey Board of Public Utilities (board). The action ordered appellants not to resume operation of its solid waste transfer station, ordered a center without a certificate to cease collecting solid waste, ordered appellants to immediately comply with all waste order and rules, and imposed penalties for the unlicensed operation of a transfer station. Appellants argued that evidence did not support the decision. The court affirmed the decision of the board and held such order would be upheld in the absence of evidence that the board was arbitrary, capricious or unreasonable, that it was supported by the evidence, and that it did not violate legislative policies expressed or fairly implied in the statutory scheme administered by the board. The court found that appellants were transfer stations, not recycling centers, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:13A-6(a) did not violate the Commerce Clause because waste disposal was a matter or state concern and the statute imposed only incidental effects on interstate commerce, and the penalties provide for in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:13A-12(b) did not constitute criminal punishment.


OUTCOME: The order of the New Jersey Board of Public Utilities against appellant recycling centers was affirmed because it was not arbitrary or capricious. The statute regulating appellants was constitutional because it was not ex post facto and its affect on interstate commerce was only incidental. The court also held that the statute regulating appellants did not constitute criminal punishment.

Phillips v. Curiale


No. A-224-89T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


245 N.J. Super. 418; 586 A.2d 245; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 26


December 3, 1990, Argued  
January 16, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION February 20, 1991. As Corrected February 25, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Passaic County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Passaic County (New Jersey), which granted summary judgment to defendant national guardsmen, on plaintiff's claim for injuries sustained to her decedent while riding in an armored personnel carrier during a national guard training exercise.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff administratrix sought review of a decision which granted summary judgment to defendant national guardsmen, on plaintiff's claim for injuries sustained to her husband while riding in an armored personnel carrier during a national guard training exercise. Plaintiff's husband was injured in 1978 and committed suicide in 1987. During the pendency of the litigation, the legislature enacted N.J. Stat. Ann. § 38A:13-1.2, which eliminated the liability of the state, national guard, and its members for injury or death that occurred in the line of duty, except as provided under the military compensation law and except for injury or death that was due to an intentionally wrongful act by a national guardsman. The statute applied to all actions and proceedings that accrued, were pending, or were filed after June 1, 1986. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to defendant guardsmen and held that the legislature had the power to wipe out a claim that existed under a prior statute at any time prior to entry of a final judgment. The court held that it did not violate due process to apply the statute retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of defendant national guardsmen, on plaintiff administratrix's claim for injuries sustained to her husband while riding in an armored personnel carrier during a national guard training exercise. Defendants had statutory immunity from the action, and the legislation that created the immunity was retroactive to plaintiff's action.

Miller v. Mitchell


No. A-4403-89T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


245 N.J. Super. 290; 585 A.2d 414; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 11


December 5, 1990, Argued

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for publication January 31, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Union County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mayor challenged the order of the Superior Court, Union County (New Jersey), which concluded that the provisions of the charter controlled appointment of members to the planning board.


OVERVIEW: The municipal charter established a mayor-council-administrator form of government. It provided that non-elected municipal officials were generally to be appointed by the mayor with the advice and consent of the city council. Plaintiffs, three members of the city council, filed a verified complaint in lieu of prerogative writs challenging defendant mayor's appointments to the planning board which were in the absence of the city council's advice and consent. The trial court enjoined the defendant from appointing class IV and alternate members without the advice and consent of the city council and invalidated the three class IV members and two alternates appointed by the defendant. The court affirmed because it found no basis for finding any legislative language, policy or history sufficient to evidence an intent to repeal the charter provisions. The court concluded that the stable and efficient operation of municipal government depended upon the predictability of interpretation and clarity of its governing laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order, which concluded that the provisions of the municipal charter controlled appointment of members to the planning board because the municipal ordinance required appointment of class IV members by defendant mayor with the advice and consent of the city council.

 

1046 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Graham


No. A-4707-88T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


245 N.J. Super. 257; 584 A.2d 878; 1991 N.J. Super. LEXIS 14


December 19, 1990, Submitted  
January 14, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 31, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court, Law Division, Union County (New Jersey), which found him guilty of counts of drug possession or distribution. Defendant asserted that statements he made were inadmissible and that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled dangerous substance, possession of a controlled dangerous substance with intent to distribute, and possession of a controlled dangerous substance with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of school property, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:35-10(a)(1), 2C:35-5(a)(1), 2C:35-7. At sentencing two counts were merged, and on the third count defendant received a concurrent five year sentence. Defendant challenged the conviction and asserted that statements he made were inadmissible and that § 2C:35-7 was unconstitutional. On appeal the court affirmed the conviction and held that § 2C:35-7 did not violate double jeopardy provisions because § 2C:35-7 was specifically prohibited from merging with § 2C:35-5(a)(1). The court concluded that the double jeopardy argument was not applicable because it prohibited retrials after an acquittal. Defendant's statements were properly admitted because the trial judge's determination regarding the credibility of conflicting testimony, which was supported by the evidence of record, was not subject to reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's drug convictions and held that prohibition on the merging of his convictions did not violate the double jeopardy clause because it was statutorily mandated. His statements were properly admitted because he failed to show with credible evidence that his admission was coerced or not voluntary.

 

1047 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gadsden


No. A-2912-88T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


245 N.J. Super. 93; 584 A.2d 265; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 457


November 27, 1990, Submitted  
December 26, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] Approved for Publication January 22, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Union County, where he was found guilty by a jury of the crime of third-degree unlawful possession of cocaine with intent to distribute within 1,000 yards of a school, a violation of N. J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:35-5a(1), 2C:35-7, after the prosecution used an allegedly ex post facto amendment to enter evidence against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and convicted by a jury for the crime of third-degree unlawful possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, a violation of N. J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5a(1), which was enhanced by the finding that he committed this crime within 1,000 yards of a school, N. J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7. At trial, the prosecution used a map drawn up by city engineers, to show that the situs of the crime was within the required distance to a school. The court received the map as prima facie evidence, after it had been properly authenticated, because an amendment to N. J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7 authorized such an action. After he was convicted, he appealed based upon ex post facto constitutional violations because the amendment was not in place at the time he committed the crime. The court affirmed his conviction, finding that the amendment was only a change to the evidentiary rules. Because the amendment did not create the crime of which defendant was convicted, nor did it increase the punishment for the crime or deprive defendant of a defense that was available when he committed it, it passed constitutional muster in not violating ex post facto prohibitions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of third-degree unlawful possession of cocaine with intent to distribute within 1,000 yards of a school, finding the amendment to be only an evidentiary rule. Because the amendment did not create the crime of which defendant was convicted, nor did it increase the punishment for the crime or deprive him of a defense that was available when he committed it, it did not violate the ex post facto clause.

County of Essex v. Waldman


No. A-6258-88T1F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


244 N.J. Super. 647; 583 A.2d 384; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 431


September 19, 1990, Argued  
December 6, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]  Approved for Publication December 21, 1990. As Amended January 7, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Commissioner of Human Services and state officials, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, which entered a summary judgment in favor of plaintiff county that enjoined defendants' long-standing practice of retaining 50 percent of maintenance payments received from social security benefits on behalf of indigent patients residing in state institutions in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-60.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county brought an action against defendants, Commissioner of Human Services and state officials, alleging that defendants' long-standing practice of retaining 50 percent of social security benefits received by defendants on behalf of indigent patients residing in state institutions with county settlements violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-60. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff and awarded reimbursement and prejudgment interest from 1980. The court affirmed in part, finding that plaintiff was entitled to the full amount of social security benefits paid on behalf of indigent patients with county settlements up to its 50 percent obligatory share of the costs as provided by § 30:4-60. The court modified the judgment to reflect a limited retrospective application from the date of the filing of the complaint because the trial court failed to apply the appropriate balancing test in that regard. As the court found no abuse of discretion in permitting prejudgment interest, the court modified the judgment to allow interest from the date of filing the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the grant of summary judgment in favor of plaintiff county because plaintiff was entitled to all social security payments made to defendants, Commissioner of Human Services and state officials, on behalf of plaintiff's indigent patients. The court modified the judgment to the extent that it had limited retrospective effect from the date of filing of the complaint with interest from that date.

DiFalco v. Subaru of America, Inc.


No. A-6247-89T3F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


244 N.J. Super. 530; 582 A.2d 1284; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 419; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,682


November 7, 1990, Argued  
December 4, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]  Approved for Publication December 13, 1990. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant seatbelt manufacturer appealed an order of the Superior Court, Passaic County (New Jersey), which denied its motion for summary judgment under the statute of limitations, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-2, and sustained the constitutionality of the tolling statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-22, which was defended on appeal by the attorney general, not plaintiff driver.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff driver filed suit against defendant seatbelt manufacturer and others for injuries she suffered in an automobile accident when her seatbelt broke. Defendant filed a motion for summary judgment under the statute of limitations, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-2. The trial court denied that motion, holding that the tolling provision of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-22, applicable to foreign defendants, was constitutional and applied. On interlocutory appeal, the attorney general rather than plaintiff defended, and asked the court to interpret § 2A:14-22 so as to satisfy the requirements of the Commerce Clause. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment that § 2A:14-22, as amended, was constitutional, holding that it violated the Commerce Clause. However, the court held that because its determination of unconstitutionality was prospective only as of the date of a United States Supreme Court decision, the statute of limitations did not commence running against defendant until June 17, 1988. Therefore, the two-year statute of limitations had not run when the amended complaint naming defendant was filed. Therefore, the court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant seatbelt manufacturer's summary judgment motion because the court's determination that the tolling statute was unconstitutional was prospective only as of the date of a United States Supreme Court decision, and thus the statute of limitations did not expire before the amended complaint naming defendant was filed.

State v. L.K.


No. A-5632-89T1F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


244 N.J. Super. 261; 582 A.2d 297; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 386


October 1, 1990, Argued  
October 29, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION November 14, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought an interlocutory appeal of a decision by the trial judge of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, when the trial judge refused its motion for further discovery regarding hypnosis evidence to be presented by defendant regarding multiple personality disorder in an insanity defense. The trial judge based his decision on the fact that the state had not yet conducted its psychiatric examination of defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant intended to introduce evidence of multiple personalities in an insanity defense case using testimony under hypnosis. The state filed a motion with the court requesting further discovery of the hypnosis methods used by defendant and the trial court denied the motion, finding that the state had not yet done its own psychiatric examination of defendant. The state appealed the denial of the motion and the court affirmed the denial. The court found that the procedural safeguards regarding the use of hypnotically enhanced evidence should apply to defendant, but that the taped evidence requested by the state should not be given because the state's psychiatric examination was not yet performed. However, the state was entitled to other psychiatric and medical records.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court regarding further discovery by the state of the hypnosis testimony of defendant, finding that the state must first complete its psychiatric examination of defendant, and remanded the case. The court further found that the state was entitled to other medical and psychiatric records of defendant and defendant's counsel was ordered to turn over such to the state.

State v. Davis


No. A-2415-88T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


244 N.J. Super. 180; 581 A.2d 1333; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 387


October 3, 1990, Argued  
October 25, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]  APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION November 13, 1990. As Corrected January 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cape May County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the denial of his application for Pretrial Intervention (PTI) by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cape May County. Defendant had been accepted into the program pending the satisfaction of certain conditions and while he was working on satisfying them, the state indicated that its approval for PTI was withdrawn and defendant was then convicted at trial on an indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on one count of third-degree conspiracy, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:5-2, three counts of third-degree receiving stolen property valued in excess of $ 500, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-7(a) and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:2-6, three counts of third-degree possession of a motor vehicle valued in excess of $ 500 with removed or altered identification marks, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:17-6(b), and one count of fourth degree unlawful purchase of a firearm, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-10(a). Defendant sought entry into Pretrial Intervention (PTI) and it was eventually granted. While working on satisfying the conditions of entry, the acceptance into the program was withdrawn by the prosecutor and defendant went to trial and was convicted of more charges under a new indictment. Defendant sought review of the prosecutor's withdrawal of acceptance. The court reversed the convictions and remanded the case with the order to allow defendant to participate in PTI. The court found that it was erroneous for the prosecutor to withdraw the acceptance because of a change in prosecutor, as defendant had relied upon the acceptance into the program.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were vacated by the court and the case was remanded with the order that defendant be permitted to participate in Pretrial Intervention. It was error for the new prosecutor to deny defendant entry into the program because of a change in view when defendant had already been accepted.

Darmetko v. Electron Technology


No. A-960-89T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


243 N.J. Super. 536; 580 A.2d 1087; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 357


September 18, 1990, Argued  
October 2, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]  APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION October 25, 1990. As Corrected October 29, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from New Jersey Department of Labor, Division of Workers' Compensation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of the judgment of the New Jersey Department of Labor, Division of Workers' Compensation, which awarded petitioner a 55 percent partial permanent disability in regard to an injury sustained while working for respondent employer, where petitioner challenged the constitutionality of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-36.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee was injured while working for respondent employer. Thereafter, the New Jersey Department of Labor, Division of Workers' Compensation, awarded petitioner a 55 percent partial permanent disability. The compensation judge noted that he would have awarded petitioner total disability payments but for the restriction of the definition of permanent total disability under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-36, which provided that injured workers must be 75 percent disabled before factors other than physical or neuropsychiatric impairments were considered in the determination of permanent total disability. Subsequently, petitioner sought review, contending that § 34:15-36 was unconstitutional. On review, the court affirmed respondent's award. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional in that the statutory limitation placed upon application of the odd lot doctrine bore a reasonable and just relationship to the general object of the legislation, that is, cost containment. The court found that the statutory restriction was not unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious, and that the restriction did not discriminate against the elderly because it was not predicated upon age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the New Jersey Department of Labor, Division of Workers' Compensation, which awarded petitioner employee a 55 percent partial permanent disability. The court held that the applicable statute was not unconstitutional in that the restriction at issue bore a reasonable and just relationship to the general object of the legislation, that is, cost containment, and because the restriction was not predicated upon age.

 

1054 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Budis


No. A-3313-88T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


243 N.J. Super. 498; 580 A.2d 283; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 351


October 24, 1989, Argued  
September 14, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]  Reargued December 19, 1989. APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION October 2, 1990.
Certification granted State v. Budis, 127 N.J. 324, 604 A.2d 599, 1990 N.J. LEXIS 1560 (1990)
Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Budis, 125 N.J. 519, 593 A.2d 784, 1991 N.J. LEXIS 91 (1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Somerset County (New Jersey), which convicted defendant of two counts of sexual penetration on a child of less than thirteen years of age, contrary to N.J. Stat. Ann. 2C:14-2(a)(1), on the ground that exclusion of evidence of child's statutory rape by another person violated defendant's right to confrontation and cross-examination.


OVERVIEW: The 10-year old victim used sexually explicit language in the presence of her father. Upon investigation, the victim indicated that her former stepfather and defendant had raped her on different occasions. At defendant's trial, the trial court excluded any evidence of the victim's prior sexual abuse under the rape shield statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:14-7. Defendant was convicted of two counts of sexual penetration on a child of less than thirteen years of age, contrary to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:14-2(a)(1). Defendant appealed on the ground that exclusion of the evidence of the prior rape violated his constitutional rights to confrontation and cross-examination. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial. The court held that the rape shield statute could not be used to deny defendant a right to a fair trial and the evidence of the victim's prior sexual abused should have been admitted to rebut the inference that she could not have known of the sexual experiences she described unless they occurred in connection with the incident being prosecuted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial. Evidence of the child victim's prior sexual abuse should have been admitted to rebut the jury's inference that she was a sexual innocent and that she would not have known of the sexual experiences she described unless defendant had committed the acts charged.

Small v. Department of Corrections


No. A-5574-88T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


243 N.J. Super. 439; 579 A.2d 1263; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 344


May 22, 1990, Submitted  
August 30, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION September 27, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County (New Jersey), which dismissed his complaint under the Tort Claims Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:1-1 et seq., against respondent Department of Corrections on the ground that his complaint was not timely filed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate challenged the trial court's dismissal of his complaint for personal injuries against respondent department of corrections on the ground that his complaint was filed outside the two year limitations period of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:8-8. Appellant argued that the date of accrual of his cause of action should be on the repeal date of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:5-3, which formerly prohibited an inmate's cause of action against a public entity prior to release, rather than on an earlier date, on which case precedent rendered the statute invalid. The court determined that appellant's right to file an action against the appellee was restored on the date that the repealer statute was enacted, and as such appellant's cause of action was effective upon the date of the repeal of § 59:5-3. The court also held that respondent had ample notice of circumstances surrounding the accident and of the medical aspects of the claim within 90 days of the accident as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:8-8. Accordingly the dismissal was reversed and the cause remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of appellant inmate's cause of action was reversed and the cause remanded for further proceedings because respondent department of corrections had ample notice of circumstances and medical aspects of the claim within 90 days of the accident and because appellant's cause of action was effective upon the date of the repeal of a statutory provision prohibiting inmates from filing a cause of action against public entities.

Alexander's Dept. Stores of New Jersey, Inc. v. Paramus


Nos. A-5098-88T5F, A-5103-88T5F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


243 N.J. Super. 157; 578 A.2d 1241; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 348


April 3, 1990, Argued  
August 8, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] Approved for Publication September 9, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants Borough of Paramus and New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing sought review from the Superior Court, Bergen County in which their motions to dismiss claims asserted by plaintiff commercial landowner were denied, in actions against defendants involving zoning ordinance amendments and certification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant borough made an agreement with defendant developer to amend a zoning ordinance to allow commercial development more intensive than otherwise permitted in exchange for $ 2.5 million and certain land from developer to the borough. The land and money was to be used to help satisfy the borough's obligation to provide low and moderate income housing and was conditioned on certification and enactment by the borough of zoning ordinance amendments. The court dismissed the claim that certification did not provide a realistic opportunity for construction of affordable housing, holding that plaintiffs did not have standing as neighboring landowners and taxpayers to make such a claim; housing rights of low and moderate income persons could only be asserted by the persons themselves. The court also allowed other charges against the borough holding that the Fair Housing Act did not diminish the constitutionally protected right to challenge municipal conduct by actions in lieu of prerogative writs. The Council on Affordable Housing was not granted power by legislature to hear actions challenging municipal action and the action should properly be heard in the Law Division.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings because plaintiffs as neighbors could not assert rights of low income persons. However, claims against defendant borough for spotting and illegal concessions, among other claims, was to be heard in the Law Division of the court, and Council on Affordable Housing was without legislative authority to hear claims against municipalities.

Ran-Dav's County Kosher, Inc. v. State


No. A-5420-88T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners and operators of a Kosher food store, sought review of the order of the trial court, Chancery Division (New Jersey), which dismissed plaintiffs' counterclaim in an enforcement action challenging the constitutionality of the New Jersey Kosher regulations, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13, § 45A-21.1 et seq. on the grounds that it was a matter to be heard by the appellate division.


OVERVIEW: Attorney general filed a complaint against plaintiffs, owners and operators of a Kosher food store, alleging violation of the New Jersey Kosher regulations, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13, § 45A-21.1 et seq. arising from plaintiffs' possession of non-Kosher meat and improper handling or packaging of purportedly Kosher meats. Plaintiffs filed a counterclaim seeking a declaration of the unconstitutionality of the regulations, an injunction against enforcement, and damages. The trial court denied the attorney general's motion to dismiss the counterclaims, retained jurisdiction of the enforcement actions against plaintiffs, and dismissed the counterclaim as a matter properly to be heard by the appellate division. Plaintiffs appealed, and the court found that the regulations were constitutional and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. The court applied a three-pronged test to determine whether the regulations violated the U.S. Const. amend. I establishment clause and found that Kosher food regulations served a legitimate secular purpose by protecting consumers from fraud where food was falsely represented to be Kosher.


OUTCOME: The court found that the state Kosher food regulations served a legitimate secular purpose by protecting consumers from fraud where food was misrepresented as Kosher and that the regulations did not violate the First Amendment establishment clause. The court remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Town of Morristown v. Woman's Club of Morristown


No. A-5127-88T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


242 N.J. Super. 654; 577 A.2d 1309; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 315


April 23, 1990, Argued  
July 18, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION August 13, 1990.
Certification granted Morristown v. Woman's Club of Morristown, 122 N.J. 392, 585 A.2d 392, 1990 N.J. LEXIS 1265 (1990)
Affirmed by Morristown v. Woman's Club of Morristown, 124 N.J. 605, 592 A.2d 216, 1991 N.J. LEXIS 73 (1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, whose opinion is repeated at 10 N.J. Tax, 309 (1989).
Morristown v. Womans Club of Morristown, 10 N.J. Tax 309, 1989 N.J. Tax LEXIS 2 (Tax Ct., 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant woman's club appealed a judgment from the Tax Court of New Jersey in favor of plaintiff town in plaintiff's suit to tax defendant's property used for commercial purposes under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-3.52.


OVERVIEW: Defendant woman's club appealed a ruling of the tax court in favor of plaintiff town denying a local property tax exemption under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-3.52. On appeal, the court reversed the tax court ruling because it found § 54:4-3.52 was constitutional as written by the legislature. The statute had only two requirements for exemption: ownership by a non-profit corporation and certification as an historical cite. The tax court added a use requirement not embodied in the statute. The court wrestled with whether the tax court allowed for the possibility that an exemption could be achieved without constitutional amendment when the statute advanced purposes generally beneficial to society as a whole. The court concluded that the exemption made a substantial distinction that had a logical and reasonable basis premised on the public purpose and works of a non-profit corporation.


OUTCOME: The judgment that defendant's property did not qualify for exemption from local property tax was reversed because the challenged statute was constitutional.

S.S. v. E.S.


No. A-4160-89T1F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


243 N.J. Super. 1; 578 A.2d 381; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 305


June 13, 1990, Argued  
July 17, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]  APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION August 16, 1990. As Amended September 10, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant alleged father appealed an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Camden County, incarcerating him for refusing to submit to a court-ordered blood test under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 9:17-51 to determine whether he was the father of plaintiff's child.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother alleged defendant was the father of her eight-year-old child. The trial court ordered defendant to take Human Leucocyte Antigen (HLA) blood test under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 9:17-51. Defendant refused, challenging the statute's constitutionality. The trial court admitted defendant's refusal into evidence and ordered him imprisoned. On appeal, the court determined the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, but that the court-ordered blood test was a search under U.S. Const. amend. IV and remanded to determine whether there was an articulable suspicion that defendant was the father. The court never reached the question of whether defendant was properly imprisoned, but held that the lower court could incarcerate a litigant who refused to submit to a court-ordered blood test and that such refusal gave rise to a presumption the results would have been unfavorable to him.


OUTCOME: The order incarcerating defendant for refusing to submit to a court-ordered blood test was reversed and remanded because the record was inadequate to establish whether plaintiff had an articulable suspicion that defendant was the father of her child.

State v. Varona


No. A-156-89T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


242 N.J. Super. 474; 577 A.2d 524; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 266


May 8, 1990, Argued  
July 12, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 26, 1990. As Amended September 25, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, which convicted defendant of conspiracy to distribute five or more ounces of cocaine and possession of five or more ounces of cocaine with at least three and one-half grams of free base with intent to distribute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:5-2 and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5(a)(1), (b)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to distribute five or more ounces of cocaine and possession of five or more ounces of cocaine with at least three and one-half grams of free base with intent to distribute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:5-2 and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5(a)(1), (b)(1). The trial court merged the convictions for a sentence of 20 years with a 10-year parole ineligibility. Defendant argued that he was a victim of entrapment, but the court found that the informant had not furnished drugs to defendant. Defendant argued that he was not able to properly cross-examine witnesses, but the court found that he had ample opportunity. The court found that statements made by a co-conspirator were admissible under N.J. R. Evid. 63(9). Defendant argued that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-12, regarding mandatory minimum sentences, was unconstitutional, but the court found that defendant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute because defendant was not injured by the statute. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, holding that substantial evidence existed to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for conspiracy to distribute and possession with intent to distribute five or more ounces of cocaine, holding that defendant was not prejudiced by the trial court, and substantial evidence existed to support the conviction.

Coldwell Banker Residential Real Estate Services, Inc. v. New Jersey Real Estate Com'n


No. A-3960-88T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division

March 27, 1990, Argued  
July 11, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 26, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Real Estate Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, real estate broker and associated individual, sought review of the judgment of defendant Real Estate Commission (New Jersey), which held that plaintiffs' proposed discount coupon promotion was not legally permissible, because it violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:15-17g.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, real estate broker and associated individual, brought suit against defendants, real estate commission and associated individual, to bar enforcement of regulations that prohibit brokers from making free promotional offerings and to declare the underlying statutory provisions unconstitutional. Defendant Real Estate Commission ruled that plaintiffs' proposed discount coupon promotion program was not legally permissible. The court held that the coupon program would violate N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:15-17g, which prohibited using any plan, scheme, or method for the sale or promotion of the sale of real estate which involved a lottery, a contest, a game, a prize, a drawing, or the offering of a lot or parcel or lots or parcels for advertising purposes. The court held that defendant real estate commission properly concluded that the coupons constituted a prize prohibited by § 45:15-17g. The court further held that plaintiffs' constitutional arguments had no merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that plaintiff real estate broker and plaintiff related individual's coupon program would violate the applicable statute because it constituted a prohibited prize.

Tocco v. New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing


No. A-6301-88T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


242 N.J. Super. 218; 576 A.2d 328; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 229


May 1, 1990, Argued  
July 3, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION July 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a summary judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County (New Jersey), granted in favor of respondent Council on Affordable Housing in appellant's suit. Appellant sought just compensation from respondent Cherry Hill Township after respondent council issued an order restraining respondent township from granting any type of development approval for lands of a certain size.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner sued respondent Council on Affordable Housing. Respondent council joined respondent Cherry Hill Township to the suit. Appellant had acres in respondent township. Respondent council, using the power given to it under Fair Housing Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:27D-301 et seq. and N.J. Admin. Code tit. 5, § 91-11.1, issued an order stopping respondent township from giving any approval for development of lots of two acres or more. This freeze on development lasted 18 months and affected appellant's property. Appellant's suit was for damages for an unconstitutional taking of his affected property. Appellant relied on U.S. Const. amend. V, XIV; N.J. Const. art. I, § 20. The trial court granted summary judgment to respondent council. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed. The court held that the imposing of a moratorium for a reasonable time on land development based on environmental and other public interest considerations did not equal a temporary taking. Without extraordinary delay, there was no taking because of decreases in the value of property while government deliberated; the decreases were incidents of ownership. The court found no unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment. The court found that the development moratorium imposed by respondent Council on Affordable Housing on respondent Cherry Hill Township lasted 18 months, and, per the court, the ordering of a moratorium for a reasonable time period on land development for environmental reasons and other public interest reasons was not a temporary taking of appellant property owner's land.

 

1063 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Childs


No. A-712-89T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


242 N.J. Super. 121; 576 A.2d 42; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 230


May 7, 1990, Argued  
July 3, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION JULY 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County that dismissed a three-count grand jury indictment against respondent corporation and owner with deceptive fund raising activities which constituted theft, on the basis that the state infringed on the grand jury's independent judgment and because one of the counts was duplicitous.


OVERVIEW: The state challenged the trial court's order that dismissed a three-count indictment against respondent corporation and owner for theft from deceptive fund raising. The state asserted that the trial court erred when it found that the state infringed on the grand jury's independent judgment and that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-2b(4) permitted the aggregation of amounts in thefts committed pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct. The court reversed, remanded, and noted that an indictment could not be dismissed except on the clearest ground. The court found that the state's comments to the grand jury that explained expected testimony of a witness and how it fit in a complicated case did not infringe on the grand jury's independent judgment because the grand jury was admonished not to take the state's comments as evidence. The court found that the offenses that were allegedly committed by respondents were multiple thefts that were the result of one common scheme and the amounts could have been aggregated pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-2b(4), and that in the continuing course of respondents' conduct, the statute of limitations started to run on the day of respondents' last theft.


OUTCOME: An order that dismissed a three-count indictment was reversed and remanded because an indictment could only be dismissed on the clearest of grounds, because the state's comments and explanations did not infringe on the grand jury's independent judgment, because the amounts of the alleged thefts could be aggregated by statute, and because the statute of limitations began to run on the date of the last theft.

 

1064 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Hopkins v. Fox & Lazo Realtors


No. A-2796-89T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


242 N.J. Super. 320; 576 A.2d 921; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 233


April 4, 1990, Argued  
June 29, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION July 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant architect sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, that granted summary judgment in respondent homebuyer's complaint for negligent performance of architectural services against appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant architect challenged the trial court's order that granted summary judgment in favor of respondent homebuyer in her complaint of negligent performance of architectural services against appellant, and asserted that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-1.1 provided appellant with repose from liability claims ten years after the completion of his design work. The court reversed and found that appellant performed only an architectural function and presented them to an independent contractor. The court noted that appellant did not engage in any supervisory functions associated with the construction of the building in which respondent was injured. The court held that the period of repose provided by the statute began when appellant submitted his designs and provided no supervision on a project, ten years and one day after the delivery of his plans to an independent contractor-developer. The court found that the statute was based on a desire not to subject appellant to potential liability throughout his professional life, and because the passage of time handicapped appellant's defense of such actions.


OUTCOME: An order that granted summary judgment in favor of respondent homebuyer was reversed because respondent architect only performed design services and did not engage in any supervisory functions in the construction of the dwelling in which appellant was injured, and because respondent should not be subject to liability for a design throughout his professional life when as time passed it was difficult to defend against the actions.

State v. Ervin


No. A-1192-89T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


242 N.J. Super. 584; 577 A.2d 1273; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 238


June 5, 1990, Argued  
June 29, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION July 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County that was entered upon his plea bargain for causing the drug induced death of his girlfriend in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-9 and his sentence to 10 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction in the trial court that was entered upon his plea bargain of causing the drug induced death of his girlfriend in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-9 and his sentence of 10 year's imprisonment, and asserted that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated appellant's due process rights and exceeded the legislature's power to create a strict liability statute. The court affirmed and determined that the transferred intent of the statute was modeled on the felony murder law. The court noted that all reported challenges to the constitutionality of a felony murder statute have been rejected. The court held that the legislature found that the manufacture, distribution, and dispensing of cocaine were inherently dangerous criminal activities that posed dangers to others, and appellant failed to show any basis that the legislature's determination was irrational. The court held that the statute applied only to deaths that were proximate consequences of dangerous illegal activities and did not violate due process of law. The court held that appellant's sentence conformed to contemporary standards of decency and was not cruel or unusual.


OUTCOME: A conviction for causing the drug induced death of another was affirmed because the statute was modeled on the felony murder statute, because the constitutionality of the felony murder statute had been upheld, because the statute's strict liability provisions applied only to activities that were proximate consequences of dangerous illegal activities, and because appellant's sentence conformed to contemporary standards.

Matter of State Grand Jury Investigation re Acceturo


Nos. A-809-89T2, A-1157-89T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


242 N.J. Super. 281; 576 A.2d 900; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 228


May 31, 1990, Argued  
June 27, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION July 11, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County and from the Department of Corrections.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contemnor sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, that denied appellant's motion for an evidentiary hearing to determine the effectiveness of appellant's continued incarceration for civil contempt. The appeal was consolidated with appellant's challenge to the decision of respondent correctional facility superintendent to place appellant in protective custody.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contemnor was brought before the lower court after he refused to testify in grand jury proceedings where appellant had been granted immunity. The lower court held appellant in civil contempt and ordered appellant to remain in custody until such time as appellant agreed to purge himself of the contempt by testifying. A few weeks into the incarceration, appellant filed a motion for an evidentiary hearing, which the lower court denied. Appellant also sought review of the type of protective custody he was placed under, complaining that it was punishment. The court affirmed the lower court's order denying appellant's request for an evidentiary hearing and approved of the protective custody afforded to appellant. The court held that in the early phase of a civil contempt commitment, it would defer to the lower court's assessment of whether a hearing was necessary to determine if the incarceration was being used to coerce the desired action or whether the incarceration was punishment. The court held that the method of protective custody used was appropriate. The conditions complained of were those normally incidental to confinement and were not purposely designed to punish.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court that denied appellant contemnor an evidentiary hearing on his civil contempt action a few weeks after the incarceration was affirmed. The lower court had discretion to determine if the hearing was necessary at that point in the incarceration. The court affirmed the conditions of appellant's custody and held that they were not designed to punish.

State v. Todaro


No. A-3439-88T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


242 N.J. Super. 177; 576 A.2d 307; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 231


April 10, 1990, Submitted  
June 27, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION July 11, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver appealed from the decision of the Superior Court, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which found him guilty of refusing to submit to a breathalyzer test under N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 39:4-50.2, 39:4-50.4a, imposed a fine, and revoked his driver's license for six months.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty, by a municipal court, of refusing to submit to a breathalyzer test pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 39:4-50.2, 39:4-50.4a. He was fined, and his license was revoked for six months. On de novo review, a superior court also found him guilty of refusing to take a breathalyzer test, imposed a fine, and revoked his driver's license for six months. Defendant appealed from the decision, arguing that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50 was unconstitutional because it required that the state need only prove by a preponderance of the evidence that he refused to submit to a breathalyzer test. The court affirmed, holding that there was no error, constitutional or otherwise, in utilizing a preponderance standard of proof because a breathalyzer refusal hearing had always been treated as a civil matter, even though drunk driving was a quasi-criminal offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's finding that defendant refused a breathalyzer test. The court held that an error did not occur in using a preponderance of the evidence standard of proof because a breathalyzer refusal hearing was a civil matter.

Gurski v. New Jersey State Police Dept.


No. A-1901-89T3F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


242 N.J. Super. 148; 576 A.2d 292; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 208


May 8, 1990, Argued  
June 4, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 19, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants police officers and superintendent challenged the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Union County, which denied their motions for summary judgment in an action by appellee family under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the New Jersey Tort Claims Act. In this action, appellee alleged that appellants acted maliciously and tortiously during the execution of a search warrant on appellee's home.


OVERVIEW: Appellee family filed suit against appellants police officers and superintendent under the Federal Civil Rights Act, 42 U.S.C.S.§ 1983 and the New Jersey Tort Claims Act, after appellants allegedly conducted an unreasonable search pursuant to a search warrant. Appellee contended that during the execution of the search warrant appellants intentionally inflicted emotional distress and maliciously converted property. Appellants moved for summary judgment, and the trial court denied appellants' motions because appellee's version of facts constituted enough evidence that appellants' conduct was not reasonable. Appellants challenged the trial court's order. The court affirmed the denial of summary judgment, as to appellants police officers, because there were outstanding issues of fact as to whether or not appellants police officers acted unreasonably during their search, which had to be determined by a plenary hearing. The court reversed the trial court's order denying appellant superintendent summary judgment, however, because he was not present during the search and was entitled to immunity as a matter of law with respect to the seizure of appellee's property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting appellant superintendent summary judgment because he was entitled to immunity with respect to claims arising out the execution of the search warrant and retention of appellee family's property. The court affirmed the trial court's order denying appellants police officers summary judgment based on immunity because their conduct in executing the search warrant was objectively unreasonable.

State v. Soto


No. A-3336-88T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


241 N.J. Super. 476; 575 A.2d 501; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 198


February 13, 1990, Submitted  
May 31, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]  APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION June 19, 1990. As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court, Middlesex County (New Jersey), which entered judgment convicting defendant of three drug-related offenses in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:35-5a(1), 2C:35-5b(3), 2C:35-5a, 2C:35-7, and 2C:35-10a(1). The superior court merged the first and third count of defendant's indictment for sentencing purposes and sentenced him to a consecutive sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in a three-count indictment with third degree possession of a controlled dangerous substance, cocaine, with intent to distribute, contrary to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:35-5a(1) and 2C:35-5b(3); third-degree possession of a controlled dangerous substance, cocaine, with intent to distribute within 1000 feet of school property, contrary to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5a and § 2C:35-7; and third degree possession of a controlled dangerous substance, cocaine, contrary to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-10a(1). The lower court convicted defendant on all three counts. For sentencing purposes, count three and count one were merged and defendant was given concurrent sentences. Defendant challenged the judgment and sentence. The appellate court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The appellate court agreed with defendant that his conviction under §§ 2C:35-5a(1) and b(3) should have merged into his conviction under § 2C:35-7 and that anti-merger language in § 2C:35-7 did not bar such a result. The appellate court held that any scheme of multiple punishments for a single crime violated deeply imbedded notions of substantive due process and fundamental fairness.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of three drug-related offenses was affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded. The appellate court held that the lower court's failure to merge defendant's the first and third counts of defendant's indictment was error and that remand was necessary for the entry of an amended judgment reflecting the vacation of defendant's conviction and sentence for violating the first count of the indictment.

Somers Associates, Inc. v. Gloucester Tp.


No. A-2892-88T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


241 N.J. Super. 323; 575 A.2d 20; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 191


January 24, 1990, Argued  
May 18, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] Approved for Publication June 14, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipality challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Camden County (New Jersey), which held that portions of a rent control ordinance were unconstitutional after plaintiff landlord challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landlord was the managing agent of an apartment complex. After fire destroyed some of the units in the complex, plaintiff totally reconstructed them. Plaintiff applied for a periodic increase in rents for the apartment complex. After conducting hearings on the application, an administrative board granted plaintiff the increase. Defendant township reversed the board's decision on the ground that plaintiff's renovated or reconstructed units could not, as a matter of law, qualify as initial rentals under a rent control ordinance. Thereafter, plaintiff filed an action against defendant seeking a judgment declaring that several sections of the ordinance were unconstitutional. The trial court granted summary judgment to plaintiff. On appeal, the court held that the ordinance met the legitimate goals of safeguarding tenants against excessive rent increases. The ordinance satisfied federal and state equal protection guarantees. There was no evidence presented that the ordinance impaired plaintiff's ability to recover a fair return. Hence, the judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment holding that sections of a rent control ordinance were unconstitutional was reversed, because the ordinance did not the violate due process or equal protection provisions of the federal and state constitutions, and plaintiff landlord did not establish impairment.

State v. Gonzalez


No. A-5841-87T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


241 N.J. Super. 92; 574 A.2d 487; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 153


February 20, 1990, Submitted  
May 8, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] Approved for Publication May 22, 1990.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of various drug charges and for engaging in prohibited conduct near a school. He challenged his conviction on the ground that the non-merger provision of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7 violated the prohibitions against double jeopardy under U.S. Const. amend V, and N.J. Const. art. I, para. II. He also argued that the fines assessed against him violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-15.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed a sentence he received in connection with his drug related conviction. He challenged the sentence, among other reasons, on the ground that the non-merger provision of N.Y. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-7 violated U.S. Const. amend. V, and N.J. Const. art. I, para. II. He also argued that the fines assessed against him violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-15. The appellate court reduced the amount of the fine and otherwise affirmed the judgment. The court observed that an element of the § 2C:35-7 crime was prohibited conduct near a school, which was not an element of the N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5 of which defendant was convicted. Moreover, the § 2C:35-5 crimes did not include as an element prohibited conduct near a school. The non-merger provision was therefore not offensive and, in fact, the non-merger provision of § 2C:35-7 was not necessary to prevent merger anyway. The court agreed with defendant that the fines assessed by the trial court did not comply with N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-15, and remanded the case for an appropriate reduction.


OUTCOME: The court modified the fine defendant was assessed but otherwise affirmed defendant's drug charge conviction. The court rejected defendant's argument that the non-merger provision of one of the statutes under which he was convicted subjected him to double jeopardy. The court found that since the crime it defined had a different element from the others there would have been no merger in any event.

Slocum v. Hospital Rate Setting Com'n, N.J. Dept. of Health


Nos. A-1461-88T1, A-2761-88T1, A-541-89T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


240 N.J. Super. 566; 573 A.2d 971; 1990 N.J. Super. LEXIS 137


February 22, 1990, Argued  
May 1, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication May 10, 1990. As Amended May 16, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey State Department of Health Hospital Rate Setting Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision from respondent New Jersey State Department of Health Hospital Rate Setting Commission that set the allowable hospital rates for the state pursuant to the Health Care Facilities Planning Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 26:2H-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Health Care Facilities Planning Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 26:2H-1 et seq., respondent New Jersey State Department of Health Hospital Rate Setting Commission set the allowable hospital rates in the state. Petitioner claimed respondent erroneously considered the labor component when it set the rates. Petitioner contended that respondent's decision violated the Administrative Procedures Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:14B-2(e), and respondent did not have the authority to grant statewide increases in the labor component. On appeal, the court modified the decision, then affirmed. Respondent was required to take the Bureau of Labor Statistics' rate of inflation in force at the time respondent took final action under N.J. Admin. Code tit. 8, § 31B-3.72(a)(1), so the court modified the order to reflect such rate. Respondent had the authority to grant statewide increases under the Act because the Act allowed respondent to consider common issues and consolidate cases involving common issues. Respondent did not violate the Administrative Procedures Act because it did not reduce the deadline in which appeals could be taken.


OUTCOME: The court modified the decision because respondent New Jersey State Department of Health Hospital Rate Setting Commission should have taken the Bureau of Labor Statistics' rate of inflation in force at the time respondent took final action. The affirmed the decision as modified because respondent commission did not violate the Administrative Procedures Act and properly set the rates under the Health Care Facilities Planning Act.
