State v. Cacamis


No. A-2330-87T8


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


230 N.J. Super. 1; 552 A.2d 616; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 458


October 25, 1988, Argued  
November 22, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] Approved for Publication December 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession with intent to distribute controlled substances and was sentenced to 25 years. Defendant appealed, and his sentence was affirmed. He then filed a petition for post-conviction relief in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County. The trial court denied the petition, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession with intent to distribute controlled substances and was sentenced to 25 years. On appeal, his sentence was affirmed. Defendant then petitioned for post-conviction relief, arguing that at the time of his guilty plea, the prosecutor misrepresented to him that he was facing 25 years without parole, violating his rights under U.S. Const. amends. VI and XIV. The trial court denied the petition, and defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that because defendant had not raised these issues in his appeal and they did not present exceptional circumstances of fundamental injustice, the issues should not be considered. The court held that the alleged error was without merit, because defendant could have been sentenced to life imprisonment, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 24:21-19b(2), with a parole disqualifier of up to half that time. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-6b. Although the statute did not state how long half of a life sentence was, it was not unconstitutionally vague, because when read with N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-123.51b, it was clear that defendant could have received a 25-year parole disqualifier.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's petition, holding that the issues raised were not raised in defendant's direct appeal and did not present exceptional circumstances of fundamental injustice. The court held that representations at defendant's guilty plea hearing that he was facing 25 years without parole were not inaccurate, and so his contention based on misrepresentation was without merit.

State v. Cuccurullo

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant convicted of driving a motor vehicle during a period when his driver's license was suspended (DWS) under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-40, appealed that judgment, which was entered in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County. Defendant contended that the judge erred in ruling that the DWS statute subjected him to enhanced penalties.


OVERVIEW: Defendant who was convicted of driving a motor vehicle during a period when his driver's license was suspended (DWS) pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-40, sought review of that judgment. Defendant contended that the enhanced penalties provision of the DWS statute did not apply because when he committed the offense in question, his driving while intoxicated (DWI) suspension period had not begun and therefore he was not a person under suspension issued pursuant to N.J. Rev. Stat. § 39:4-50, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-40. The court affirmed the judgment entered in the court below. The court held that a person is under suspension from the time that the suspension is imposed even though the period of suspension may not begin until later.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgement of the trial court. The court held that a driver's license suspension commences when it is imposed, even though the period of suspension may not begin until a later date.

State v. Nemesh


No. A-5939-86T8


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


228 N.J. Super. 597; 550 A.2d 757; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 415


September 27, 1988, Argued  
October 31, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] Approved for Publication November 14, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from the Superior Court of New Jersey, in which he was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and operating a motor vehicle during a period when his New Jersey license was suspended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving a car which collided with another vehicle, causing injuries to the driver and passenger. At the scene, defendant presented a Maryland driver's license to the officer. Defendant acknowledged to the officer that he was the driver of the vehicle. Upon noticing an odor of alcohol, swaying, and bloodshot eyes, defendant was charged with driving while impaired. Defendant had prior charges of driving while impaired in New Jersey, and his New Jersey license had been suspended for the previous charges. The municipal judge found defendant guilty of driving while impaired and operating a vehicle with a suspended license without admission of the breathalyzer test. The court affirmed the convictions and denied defendant's motion to vacate the judgment, holding that the state had proven defendant was under the influence at the time he operated the vehicle and defendant was not prejudiced by false testimony of state trooper as to his education. Defendant's Miranda rights were not violated; an officer's inquiry as to who was operating the vehicle was not a custodial interrogation. Defendant was not entitled to jury trial for driving while impaired charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions because the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was driving under the influence and operating his motor vehicle with a suspended license. The defendant was not entitled to a jury trial and his Miranda rights were not violated because he was not under custodial interrogation.

Matter of Association of Trial Lawyers of America


No. A-5576-87T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


228 N.J. Super. 180; 549 A.2d 446; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 380


September 19, 1988, Argued  
October 13, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 31, 1988. As amended November 17, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Attorney General sought interlocutory review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Middlesex County, which ruled that respondent American Trial Lawyer's Association had the requisite standing to attack the Products Liability Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:58C-1 et seq., under the New Jersey Declaratory Judgment Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:16-50 et seq., and the federal constitution.


OVERVIEW: Respondent American Trial Lawyer's Association filed an action attacking the Products Liability Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:58C-1 et seq., under the New Jersey Declaratory Judgment Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:16-50 et seq., and the federal constitution. The Products Liability Act contained substantive provisions setting forth rules of liability and defenses, procedural requirements, and mandated bifurcated proceedings for the determination of compensatory and punitive damages. Appellant Attorney General sought interlocutory review of the trial court which ruled that respondent had the requisite standing to maintain the action and that its complaint presented a justiciable controversy. The court reversed and dismissed the complaint. The court found that the Products Liability Act did not regulate or purport to regulate respondent in any way, nor could the court determine how it effected respondent's members in a way that gave them standing to maintain their action. The court held that although respondent sought to raise issues on behalf of the consuming public, it could not depart from the traditional rule that one may not claim standing to vindicate the rights of a third party.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and dismissed respondent American Trial Lawyer's Association's complaint in favor of appellant Attorney General. The court held that although respondent sought to raise issues on behalf of the consuming public, it could not grant respondent standing to vindicate the rights of a third party, where respondent sought to attack the Product Liability Act.

Clean Capital County Committee v. Driver


No. A-16-88T3F


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


228 N.J. Super. 506; 550 A.2d 494; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 401


September 19, 1988, Argued  
September 21, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]  Approved for Publication October 12, 1988. As Amended December 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county clerk and county bottle bill committee, sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Mercer County (New Jersey), which granted respondents', beverage distributors and retailer, injunction against appellants from placing on the general election ballot a question proposed by initiative petition as to whether the county should adopt an ordinance requiring deposits on certain bottles and cans.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, beverage distributors and retailer, brought suit opposing an initiative by appellant county bottle bill committee to place a bottle deposit bill on the general election ballot. The trial court enjoined appellants, county clerk and committee, from placing the question on the ballot. The trial court held that a deposit program must be enacted as part of the county's comprehensive solid waste management plan and that the bottle bill was preempted by the Clean Communities and Recycling Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:1E-99.1 et seq. The court reversed the order, discharged the injunction, and directed appellant county clerk to include the proposed ordinance on the ballot. The court found no clear or facial invalidity in the proposed ordinance or conflict with state law or policy. Further, there was no clear intention by the state to preempt counties from entering the field and there was no indication of a requirement for uniformity of handling anti-litter regulations. The court concluded that the initiative was not necessarily invalidated by the fact that the county had not yet adopted a comprehensive recycling plan.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that enjoined appellants, county clerk and county bottle bill committee, from placing on the general election ballot a question as to whether the county should adopt a bottle deposit ordinance where there was no clear or facial invalidity in the proposed ordinance, no conflict with state law, and no clear preemption. The court discharged the injunction and directed the proposed ordinance to be placed on the ballot.

New Jersey Ass'n of Ticket Brokers v. Ticketron


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


226 N.J. Super. 155; 543 A.2d 997; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 227


January 12, 1988, Argued  
June 30, 1988, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ticket brokers appealed the order of the superior court (New Jersey) which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, the state of New Jersey, and dismissed portions of plaintiffs' complaints challenging the constitutionality of New Jersey's anti-ticket-scalping law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:8-26 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff ticket brokers brought suit against defendant, the state of New Jersey, challenging New Jersey's anti-ticket-scalping law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:8-26 et seq. The lower court granted summary judgment in favor of defendant and dismissed those portions of plaintiffs' complaints which attacked the constitutionality of the statute. On appeal, the court noted that legislative enactments regulating prices were subject to a narrow scope of review in accordance with the due process clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court held that due process was satisfied because the statute was reasonably related to a proper legislative purpose and promoted the public welfare without discrimination or arbitrariness. Plaintiff's argument that the statute violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, the commerce clause, was also held to be without merit in the absence of evidence that the commerce clause was implicated, and in light of the fact that the statute promoted a legitimate governmental interest. After ruling that plaintiffs' further constitutional claims lacked substance, and finding no remaining issues of fact, the court affirmed the order which granted summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment to defendant state of New Jersey, holding that the state's anti-ticket-scalping statute was reasonably related to a proper legislative purpose and did not violate plaintiff ticket brokers' constitutional rights.

 

1120 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pratt


No. A-4615-85T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


226 N.J. Super. 307; 544 A.2d 392; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 263


May 31, 1988, Argued  
June 28, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 2, 1988.
Certification denied by State v. Pratt, 114 N.J. 314, 554 A.2d 864, 1988 N.J. LEXIS 1289 (1988)
Motion denied by State v. Pratt, 2008 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1954 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of murder and firearm possession convictions under N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:11-3 and 2C:39-4a, in favor of respondent state in the Atlantic County Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile sought review of murder and firearm convictions in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:11-3 and 2C:39-4a, based on contended error in refusing to permit the jury to consider his age in determining whether the homicide was committed in heat of passion resulting from reasonable provocation and in restricting evidence regarding the victim's assaultive acts against others. The court rejected appellant's urged errors and affirmed the conviction in respondent state's favor. The court explained the standard for provocation sufficient to reduce murder to manslaughter was based upon provocation calculated to produce passion in an average man of ordinary self control. The court further noted this did not mean that an actor's age could never be considered in determining the issue of reasonable provocation under an objective standard. Instead, the court concluded that in the present case, appellant's age had no particular relevance on the issue of whether the deceased's conduct would have prompted a homicidal rage in a reasonable person. The court also explained absent proof of appellant's knowledge of a deceased's reputation, evidence thereof was inadmissible.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed appellant's murder and firearm convictions in appellee state's favor because jury's consideration of appellant's age in determining whether actions were the result of heat of passion based on reasonable provocation was properly denied when such provocation was an objective standard and age was irrelevant to deceased's conduct while deceased's aggressive reputation was inadmissible absent proof of appellant's knowledge thereof.

State v. Fiorilla


No. A-4747-87T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


226 N.J. Super. 81; 543 A.2d 958; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 232


June 10, 1988, Submitted; June 14, 1988, Submitted  
June 21, 1988, Decided  
June 14, 1988, Supplementing Order entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplementing Order Entered June 14, 1988. Approved for Publication July 12, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, nursing home operators and principals, challenged the order of the Superior Court, Bergen County (New Jersey), which denied their N.J. Ct. R. 1:8-1(a) request to waive a jury trial. In this action, appellants were charged with multiple crimes including falsification of records, conspiracy, and failures of duty, and sought to have a non-jury trial due to their concern over widespread publicity.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, nursing home operators and principals, requested a waiver of a jury trial pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 1:8-1(a) in an action brought against them by the state for falsification of records, conspiracy, failures of duty, and other crimes that victimized their elderly residents and public bodies. In support of their request, appellants agreed to provide intelligent waivers and stated that the reasons for the request were to shorten the trial time for a complicated case, limit publicity, and because of the emotional issues. The state urged a trial and the trial court rejected appellants' request, stating that because it was a high profile case, it should appear to the public that a jury of appellants' peers had reached a verdict. Appellants challenged the trial court's order. The court reversed the trial court's order and stated that even though a request for waiver of a jury trial was not a constitutional or unconditional right, it should not be denied without good reason. The court then held that appellants supported their request with good reasons and that the trial judge's refusal due to the perception of public expectation was an improper basis for denial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying the request of appellants, nursing home operators and principals, for a waiver of a jury trial. The court held that while appellants had no constitutional right or unconditional right to waiver of a jury trial, their request set forth good faith reasons for the waiver and should not have been denied by the trial court because of its concern over public perception.

 

1122 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Bethany Baptist Church v. Deptford Tp.


No. A-1028-86T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


225 N.J. Super. 355; 542 A.2d 505; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 201


May 9, 1988, Submitted  
June 7, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 15, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Tax Court, Gloucester County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff church appealed an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Tax Court, Gloucester County (New Jersey), that upheld the levy of taxes on plaintiff's property for a particular tax year.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff church purchased property after the assessment date for the 1984 tax year. Prior to plaintiff's purchase, the property had been used for a nonexempt purpose. Plaintiff was assessed taxes for the 1984 tax year. The assessment was affirmed by the trial court, and plaintiff appealed. The court held that pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 54:4-23, 4-35, the status of property as exempt or nonexempt was determined by its ownership and use on October 1 of the pre-tax year. Because the property plaintiff purchased was non-exempt as of October 1, 1983, taxes were assessable on the property for the 1984 tax year. The court found that the denial of exempt status for plaintiff did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I or N.J. Const. art. I, par. 3. Nothing required that religious property be exempt from taxation from the moment of its acquisition. Further, there was a compelling state interest in not cancelling the tax liability on land mid-way through a tax year because such a cancellation would unfairly burden other taxpayers. Plaintiff's tenet against the payment of taxes provided no basis for resisting the tax. The order upholding the tax assessment was thus affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order that upheld the levy of taxes on plaintiff church's property for a particular tax year was affirmed because, pursuant to statute, the property was non-exempt as of the tax assessment date. Further, neither constitutional nor statutory law precluded taxation of plaintiff's property and the state had a compelling interest in not changing the tax status of property mid-way through a particular tax year.

 

1123 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bolte


No. A-2276-87T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


225 N.J. Super. 335; 542 A.2d 494; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 220


April 20, 1988, Argued  
May 31, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 15, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Burlington County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, Burlington County (New Jersey), which denied his motion to suppress evidence in the action against him for numerous motor vehicle and disorderly persons violations.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed defendant erratically driving prior to pulling into his garage, and then followed defendant into his home. Defendant was arrested and charged with numerous motor vehicle and disorderly persons violations. The officer had entered the garage just as the automatic door started to close and had advised defendant that he was under arrest, but defendant proceeded to the bedroom and locked the door. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence against him. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the cause for the entry of an order of suppression, holding that the warrantless intrusion by the police officer into defendant's home failed to meet the U.S. Const. amend. IV standard of reasonableness. The court found that the officer had probable cause only as to certain motor vehicle offenses, and those relatively minor offenses did not justify the kind of warrantless intrusion that occurred. The court concluded that the officer could not justify his warrantless intrusion based on the need to avoid the dissipation of blood alcohol, because blood alcohol was not evidential as to any offense with respect to which he had probable cause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment denying defendant's motion to suppress for the entry by the trial court of an order of suppression, holding that the warrantless intrusion by the police officer into defendant's home failed to meet the Fourth Amendment standard of reasonableness.

 

1124 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Levinson


No. A-3312-86T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


225 N.J. Super. 135; 541 A.2d 1110; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 186


February 10, 1988, Argued  
May 19, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 6, 1988.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an out of state motorist, challenged the judgment from the Municipal Court (New Jersey), which convicted him of taking pictures on the New Jersey turnpike in violation of N.J. Admin. Code tit. 19, § 9-1.9(a)(1). Defendant argued that the regulation promulgated by plaintiff New Jersey Turnpike Authority was arbitrary, vague and overbroad, unconstitutional, and exceeded the powers granted to it by the legislature.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an out of state motorist, stopped his car on the New Jersey turnpike and took pictures of an accident after he witnessed a collision between a state police car and two other vehicles. Defendant was charged with taking photos on the turnpike in violation of N.J. Admin. Code tit. 19, § 9-1.9(a)(1). Defendant testified that he took the photographs to prevent a police cover-up. On review of his conviction, defendant argued that § 9-1.9(a)(1) was arbitrary, vague and overbroad, unconstitutional, and exceeded the authority granted by the legislature. The court reversed and held the regulation that established a blanket ban against all photography regardless of circumstances or context exceeded the powers delegated to plaintiff New Jersey Turnpike Authority under the enabling act. The court reasoned that the regulation did not contribute to the stated objectives of traffic flow and safety and concluded that any special risks to traffic flow and safety posed by photography should be defined and incorporated into traffic security regulations. The court also refused to usurp the function of the legislature and declined to limit the breadth of the photography regulation.


OUTCOME: Defendant out of state motorist's conviction for taking pictures on the New Jersey turnpike in violation of N.J. Admin. Code tit. 19, § 9-1.9(a)(1) was reversed. A regulation that established a blanket ban against all photography regardless of circumstances or context exceeded the powers delegated to plaintiff, the New Jersey Turnpike Authority, under the enabling act.

 

1125 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Sykes v. Propane Power Corp.


No. A-416-87T8


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


224 N.J. Super. 686; 541 A.2d 271; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 166


April 12, 1988, Argued  
May 6, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 25, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, one opinion of which is reported as Sykes v. Zook Enterprises, Inc., 215 N.J. Super. 461 (Law Div. 1987).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order from the Superior Court of Essex County (New Jersey), denying her motion for reconsideration and granting the summary judgment motions of defendants, chemical plant, engineer, and engineering firm. Plaintiff claimed she was entitled to recover under the Wrongful Death Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:31-1 et seq., as the purported "wife" of defendant plant's deceased employee.


OVERVIEW: Defendant company operated a chemical plant. Defendant engineer prepared a plan to bring the plant into compliance with state environmental laws. A chemical distillation unit in the plant exploded and killed an employee. Plaintiff, who cohabited with the employee, brought a suit against the employer and the engineer and his firm, alleging wrongful death, negligence, and strict liability. The court dismissed the suits. On appeal, the court affirmed. Plaintiff's individual claim was barred under the Wrongful Death Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:31-4 et seq., because she was not the decedent's spouse. Since damages under the Act did not depend upon the a survivor's needs, it was immaterial that plaintiff's children might have to provide for her future medical care with funds from their award. No equal protection claim existed because illegitimacy did not bar the children's recovery. Because defendant engineer and his firm were retained simply to prepare generalized drawings of the processing system components in order to show how the chemicals were carried, stored and discharged, and their work did not involve safety processes, dismissal against these defendants was upheld.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of a wrongful death suit against defendants, employer, engineer, and engineering firm. Because plaintiff was not married to a deceased employee, she could not recover for wrongful death against the employer. Because defendant engineer and defendant engineering firm were not hired as safety engineers, they could not be held liable for an explosion at the employer's chemical plant.

Matter of Wayne, CVS Pharmacy


No. A-3440-86T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


224 N.J. Super. 631; 541 A.2d 242; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 160


January 12, 1988, Argued  
April 28, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 16, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the State of New Jersey, Department of Law and Public Safety, Division of Consumer Affairs, State Board of Pharmacy.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pharmacist sought review of an order of the State Board of Pharmacy (New Jersey) that found that petitioner had committed an act of grossly unprofessional conduct in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:14-12(f), on the ground that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:14-12(f) was unconstitutional for failure to satisfy due process requirements.


OVERVIEW: Pharmacy store advertised that all prescriptions for a one-week period would be offered for a flat fee of $ 3. Petitioner was charged with violating N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:14-12(f). At a hearing before the State Board of Pharmacy, petitioner testified that he was the pharmacist in charge of the store and that the decision to run the advertisement was not his but a corporate level decision. The Board found petitioner guilty of grossly unprofessional conduct in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:14-12(f) and found him responsible under N.J. Admin. Code § 13:39-8.14b14. Petitioner sought review claiming that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:14-12(f) was unconstitutional for failure to satisfy due process requirements. The Superior Court held that the statute did not fulfill the purpose of serving the public health, safety or welfare because it did not bear any relationship to the legislative objective sought to be obtained by the statute, the banning of practices which would lower standards of professional service by a pharmacist. The court determined that the statute was void for vagueness because there was no fixed or otherwise identifiable price from which the discount could be calculated.


OUTCOME: The final decision of the State Board of Pharmacy that found petitioner pharmacist guilty of grossly unprofessional conduct in violation of the statute was reversed, and the penalty imposed was vacated. The court held that the statute was unconstitutional because it did not fulfill the purpose of serving the public health, safety or welfare and was void for vagueness.

 

1127 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Bluvias v. Winfield Mut. Hous. Corp.


Nos. A-3881-86T1, A-4018-86T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


224 N.J. Super. 515; 540 A.2d 1324; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 128


March 7, 1988, Argued  
April 13, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 20, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Union County, which held that appellee housing corporation had not unfairly restricted appellant's rights to alienation by having refused to allow them to sell or give their unit to anyone not approved of by appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee housing corporation owned a municipality incorporated as a township. Appellee managed, operated, acquired, and owned, on a nonprofit basis, a federal housing project, and defined appellant members as those persons housed in the project. Appellee required appellants to execute mutual ownership contracts, required that a signatory member occupy units, and held that units could not be subleased without express permission. Appellants argued that that placed an unfair restriction on alienation. The court affirmed the judgment for appellee. The court held that appellee was a cooperative and that appellants had the rights of a tenant because the occupancy terms in the mutual ownership contract constituted the basis of a leasehold. The court held that the units were rented for a perpetual term, included the right of inheritance and devise subject only to reasonable approval by appellee, and that the lease was subject to termination only for violation of the agreement's terms, which included that appellants occupy the premises. The court held that appellee's means of preserving family use of the project had not constituted an unwarranted restriction on alienation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment for appellant housing corporation because their means of upholding the purpose of preserving family use by having retained a right of first refusal had not constituted an unwarranted restriction on alienation.

 

1128 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crescenzi


No. A-1259-86T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


224 N.J. Super. 142; 539 A.2d 1250; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 117


December 8, 1987, Argued  
March 30, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 19, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Onappeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court, Mercer County (New Jersey), which convicted him on two counts of witness tampering in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:28-5 a(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on two counts of witness tampering. On appeal, he alleged the statute was unconstitutional because it was overbroad and void for vagueness. The court affirmed his conviction and found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it was sufficiently definite to give notice that no one could undermine enforcement of criminal justice by attempting to coerce or induce witnesses or informants not to cooperate with law enforcement. It also held that the statute was not overbroad because it furthered the important governmental interest of preventing intimidation of, and interference with, potential witnesses or informers in criminal matters, and held that it easily met the test of weighing the importance of the exercise of speech against the gravity and probability of harm therefrom. The court found that when the public interest in discovering the truth in official proceedings was balanced against a party's right to speak to a particular witness with the intent of tampering, that party's right was minuscule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on two counts of witness tampering because the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad as it gave sufficient notice that no one could coerce witnesses not to cooperate with law enforcement and furthered the important governmental interest of preventing intimidation of witnesses.

State v. Gonzalez


No. A-4406-84T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


223 N.J. Super. 377; 538 A.2d 1261; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 88


February 2, 1988, Argued  
March 2, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 23, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Passaic County (New Jersey), which convicted defendant of first degree robbery following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first degree robbery when he and two accomplices stopped a victim, aimed a shotgun at him and demanded money, and then stole his automobile when the victim got away to call police. Prior to trial, defendant's counsel informed the trial court that there would be no alibi defense. After the state presented its case, defendant testified that he was somewhere else when the robbery occurred. The trial court instructed the jury to disregard defendant's alibi statement and the jury convicted defendant of robbery. The court affirmed the conviction. The court applied a three-factor balancing test on the trial court's preclusion of defendant's alibi defense. The court held that the trial court's jury instruction was proper because defendant's alibi statement was highly prejudicial to the state, which was not given notice of the alibi defense and who had completed its case in chief before the statement was made, and because it was likely that the withholding of the alibi defense was deliberate and a fragrant violation of N.J. Ct. R. 3:11, which would have been rewarded by delaying and confounding the prosecution in the midst of trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of first degree robbery was affirmed, because defendant's alibi statement made after the state had presented its case in chief was likely a flagrant violation of notice requirement of such a defense and because there could be no lesser sanction against defendant than the charge to the jury to disregard defendant's alibi statement.

In re Robert L. Mitchell Technical Center


No. A-5451-86T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


223 N.J. Super. 166; 538 A.2d 410; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 63; 18 ELR 20847


February 9, 1988, Argued  
March 1, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 11, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Final Decision of the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation sought review of the decision of respondent New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection, which denied its request for a determination that its research and development facility was not subject to the provisions of the New Jersey Environmental Cleanup Responsibility Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:1K-6 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner corporation requested a determination that its research and development facility was not subject to the provisions of the New Jersey Environmental Cleanup Responsibility Act (ECRA), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:1K-6 et seq., from respondent New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection. Respondent denied petitioner's request. The court affirmed respondent's determination. It concluded that an examination of ECRA and the Standard Industrial Classification Manual (SICM), which ECRA incorporated by reference, disclosed the correctness of respondent's position. The court reasoned that the legislature had dictated that the SICM be consulted and if it classified an operation within the designated classifications, the place of business which conducted that operation was covered by ECRA. It concluded that the interpretation of respondent, the agency to which the legislature had given responsibility for administration of ECRA, was entitled to great weight and that respondent's construction of the statute resulted from its plain meaning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination of respondent New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection that the research and development facility of petitioner corporation was subject to the provisions of the New Jersey Environmental Cleanup Responsibility Act (ECRA). It concluded that respondent's interpretation of ECRA was entitled to great weight and that respondent's construction of the statute resulted from its plain meaning.

Jehovah's Witnesses Assembly Hall of Southern New Jersey v. Woolwich Tp. of New Jersey


No. A-4894-86T8


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


223 N.J. Super. 55; 537 A.2d 1336; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 50


December 2, 1987, Argued  
February 19, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 4, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Gloucester County, whose opinion is reported at 220 N.J.Super. 381 (1987).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, municipality and planning board, challenged the ruling of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Gloucester County, which decided that defendant planning board was required to reconsider the site plan application of plaintiff religious group. The trial court held that a zoning change that prohibited churches in a residential area violated plaintiff's state constitutional right to freedom of religion.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff religious group had title to a piece of land in defendant municipality and wanted to build a place of worship and other buildings. The land zoning permitted churches and other places of worship. Defendant planning board rezoned the land and prohibited churches and places of worship on the land. Plaintiffs filed suit and contended that the new zoning deprived them of their state constitutional right to free religion. The trial court concluded that defendants had completely excluded plaintiffs and violated their rights to freedom of religion. On appeal, the court remanded the case to the trial court for findings of fact and conclusions of law. The court stated that the record had no relevant facts about the religious nature and significance of plaintiff's planned activities, whether there was other property available in the municipality that would have served plaintiff's needs, and the kind and extent of disruption to defendant municipality's zoning plan plaintiff's church would have created. The court believed that these facts were needed to properly consider the zoning restrictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that found that defendants, municipality and planning board, had violated plaintiff religious group's freedom of religion rights by excluding from zoning all places of worship in a particular area. The court found that the record had not addressed relevant facts and remanded the case for further findings.

State v. Helewa

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed from an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Middlesex County, which denied his motion to suppress his statement to a Division of Youth and Family Services caseworker during an interview conducted after he was arrested on charges of sexually abusing his two teenage daughters.


OVERVIEW: Defendant father was indicted and charged with two counts of aggravated sexual assault, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:14-2a, and two counts of endangering the welfare of a child, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:24-4a. Following his not guilty plea to the indictment, defendant moved to suppress the statement given to the Division of Youth and Family Services (DYFS) caseworker pursuant to N.J. R. State v. Kocen


No. A-4371-86T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


222 N.J. Super. 517; 537 A.2d 731; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 35


January 20, 1988, Argued  
February 5, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 4, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment entered by the Superior Court, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which convicted him for unlawfully and purposefully obtaining natural gas without compensation, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-8(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant purchased a house that was supplied with natural gas without the gas company's knowledge. The gas company had installed gas service for defendant's predecessor in interest, but the company mistakenly recorded the address of the house and never corrected the error. Defendant knew that normally one paid for gas, and that he was not doing so, but continued to receive the gas. After a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of unlawfully and purposefully obtaining natural gas without compensation, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-8(a). On appeal, the court reversed the judgment because defendant's conduct was not criminalized by the statute. The court held that a person who knowingly accepted services without payment which the person knew were available only for compensation did not violate § 2C:20-8(a) unless there was a verbal or physical act of deception, fraud or threat, or false token, slug, mechanical or electronic device, or like means employed to avoid payment for the service. Because defendant did not engage in any affirmative act, the court remanded the case with instructions to enter judgment dismissing the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for unlawfully and purposefully obtaining natural gas without compensation because his conduct was not prohibited by the applicable statute. The court held that the statute was not violated unless there was a verbal or physical act of deception, fraud or threat, or false token, slug, mechanical or electronic device, or like means employed to avoid payment for the service.

 

1134 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Exec. Com. on Ethical Stds. Etc


No. A-2991-86T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


222 N.J. Super. 482; 537 A.2d 713; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 26


November 30, 1987, Submitted  
February 3, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 18, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from an Advisory Opinion of the Executive Commission on Ethical Standards.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonprofit organization sought review of the advisory opinion of the Executive Commission on Ethical Standards (New Jersey), which determined that professors and attorneys at the state law school were subject to the Conflicts of Interest Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:13D-12 et seq., and therefore, they could not have represented plaintiff in affordable housing litigation before the Council on Affordable Housing.


OVERVIEW: Law professors and staff attorneys employed at the state law school represented plaintiff nonprofit organization in affordable housing litigation before the Council on Affordable Housing (COAH), a state agency. At plaintiff's request, the Executive Commission on Ethical Standards (Commission) issued an advisory opinion, which determined that employees of the state law school could not represent plaintiff before COAH without violating the Conflicts of Interest Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:13D-12 et seq. The court affirmed the determination of the Commission, holding that employees of the state law school were covered by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:13D-16(b), as they were state employees. The court held that the very fact that the law school provided public higher education made it a full-fledged state agency that performed a governmental function. The fact that the law school had no personal or pecuniary interest in the outcome of plaintiff's litigation was irrelevant, as the legislature had not intended to preclude only those types of conflicts. The court held that the law school employees' representation of a party other than the state before a state agency contravened § 52:13D-16(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination of the Executive Commission on Ethical Standards (Commission), holding that the Commission had correctly determined that the employees of the state law school were state employees that were subject to the Conflicts of Interest Law, and that they could not have represented plaintiff nonprofit organization before the Council on Affordable Housing without violating the statute.

Grant v. Wright

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff cohabitant girlfriend filed a complaint against defendant cohabitant boyfriend pursuant to the Prevention of Domestic Violence Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:25-1 et seq. Plaintiff sought a restraining order and exclusive possession of the parties' residence because of defendant's asserted harassment of her. 1136 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Boylan v. State


Nos. A-4578-86T5, A-5124-86T5, A-4833-86T5, A-4503-86T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


222 N.J. Super. 313; 536 A.2d 1283; 1988 N.J. Super. LEXIS 15; 9 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2092


November 2, 1987, Argued and Submitted  
January 20, 1988, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for Publication February 9, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Determination of Division of Pensions, Department of Treasury.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, police and fire department personnel, appealed from a final determination by the Division of Pensions, Department of Treasury (New Jersey), which advised plaintiffs that they were required to retire from their positions because they were over the age of 65. Plaintiffs' actions for injunctive relief against the enforcement of their mandatory retirement were transferred to the appellate court by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The court remanded the appeals by plaintiffs, the police and fire personnel, from their notifications of mandatory retirement to determine the duties of each of the individual plaintiffs. The court held that if an individual plaintiff was not primarily and directly involved in the duties outlined in 29 U.S.C.S. §§ 630(j) and (k) that plaintiff was not subject to mandatory early retirement. The 1986 federal amendments to the Age Discrimination in Employment Act exempted police and fire personnel from mandatory retirement restrictions. The court agreed that the 1986 amendments served to reinstate New Jersey's public employee pension laws, which included mandatory retirement ages for police and fire personnel, as they existed in 1983. The court held, however, that those mandatory retirement ages applied only to police and fire personnel whose duties came within the definitions found in §§ 630(j) and (k). Language in §§ 630(j) and (k) regarding personnel transferred to supervisory positions did not apply to bona fide promotions to those positions. Thus, where bona fide promotions placed a plaintiff outside the parameters of §§ 630(j) and (k), mandatory retirement was not applicable.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the appeals of plaintiffs, the police and fire department personnel, from their notifications of mandatory retirement. The court found that mandatory retirement did not apply to personnel who had bona fide promotions to supervisory or administrative positions and who were not directly involved in the day to day duties of police and fire personnel as defined by federal regulations.

 

1137 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Urban League of Greater N.B. v. Twp. Comm. of Cranbury


No. A-3416-86T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


222 N.J. Super. 131; 536 A.2d 287; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1429


November 2, 1987, Argued  
December 29, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 22, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Middlesex County, denying their application for attorney fees and costs in their action attacking defendant cities' zoning ordinances as unconstitutionally exclusionary and discriminatory.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, a corporation and three minorities, sued defendant cities to invalidate exclusionary zoning and to make possible the construction of housing that was affordable by low and moderate income people. Due to a complex procedural history involving appeals and remands, plaintiffs prevailed on their state constitutional nonfee claims, but were improperly precluded from presenting evidence calculated to establish racial and ethic discrimination in violation of their asserted federal claims before the trial court. The court reversed the order denying plaintiffs' application for attorney fees and costs. Because of the unique procedural history, plaintiffs were entitled to establish on the record that they were entitled to counsel fees if their evidence established an unrebutted prima facie violation of the Fair Housing Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 3601 et seq. On remand, the trial court was directed to determine this issue using only the record, expert reports based on that record, and matters that could be judicially noticed. Plaintiffs waived an evidentiary trial on the issue where appellate counsel stated that they did not want an evidentiary trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying plaintiffs fees and costs, and remanded the case for a redetermination of fees using only the record in the case, expert reports based on that record, and matters which could be judicially noticed. Plaintiffs were entitled to a decision on their unresolved fee claim based on the common nucleus of operative facts doctrine where they prevailed only on their nonfee claims.

Phila. Outdoor v. N.J. Expressway Auth.


No. A-671-86T6


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


221 N.J. Super. 207; 534 A.2d 77; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1374


October 13, 1987, Submitted  
November 23, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 7, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Administrative Decision of the Commissioner of Transportation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant expressway authority challenged an order from the Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Transportation, which granted respondent advertiser an outdoor advertising permit that was to be placed on property adjacent to the right-of-way of a city expressway.


OVERVIEW: Respondent advertiser filed an application for an outdoor advertising permit with the New Jersey Department of Transportation (DOT). The Commissioner of the DOT granted the permit, and appellant expressway authority sought review of the DOT's decision. The court reversed and remanded for the entry of an order denying respondent's application. The court found that the Commissioner failed to apply the proper legal standard, instead of applying the language of the Outdoor Advertising Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:40-60(1) and (2), and N.J. Admin. Code tit. 16, § 41A-3.2(a)2 and 3i. The court concluded that the Commissioner's decision was not supported by the record because she gave no weight to appellant's experts. The court ruled that the Outdoor Advertising Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:40-50 et seq., did not contravene the U.S. Const. amend. I right to free speech.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a decision to grant respondent advertiser an outdoor advertising permit because the Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Transportation did not apply the Outdoor Advertising Act and its attendant regulation, which were not violative of the First Amendment.

 

1139 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Salzman


No. A-528-85T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


228 N.J. Super. 109; 549 A.2d 46; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1477


September 28, 1987, Argued  
October 27, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 6, 1988.
Certification denied by State v. Salzman, 110 N.J. 314, 540 A.2d 1291, 1988 N.J. LEXIS 774 (1988)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant dog owner sought review of a his conviction from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County of permitting his dogs to bark late at night and early in the morning in violation of Montclair Township, N.J., Ordinance Art. III, § 166-11 (1947).


OVERVIEW: Defendant dog owner was convicted of permitting his dogs to bark late at night and early in the morning in violation of Montclair Township, N.J., Ordinance Art. III, § 166-11 (1947). On appeal, the first summons, and four of the five convictions from the second summons were reversed. The court held that the form of complaint required the officer to sign and swear to the complaint in the presence of a person authorized to make a probable cause determination. On the face of the complaint filed in connection with the first summons, the officer did not sign or swear to the complaint as required by N.J. R. Civ. P. 3:3-1(a) and N.J. R. Civ. P. 3:3-2. Because there was no determination of probable cause, the summons and complaint were fatally defective. In addition, the second summons and the complaint were sworn to by the deputy court clerk who also made a determination of probable cause. However, defendant was put on trial without knowing how many charges he was facing. He learned he was facing multiple charges only after he was shown a copy of complainant's trial notes. Because there has been a violation of a defendant's constitutional right to due process, prejudice was presumed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant dog owner's judgment of conviction, holding there was no determination of probable cause respecting the first complaint, therefore the summons and complaint were fatally defective. Regarding the second summons, the court ruled that the complaint did not inform defendant that he was facing five charges, which violated defendant's constitutional right to due process.

In re Daniels


No. A-3243-85T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


219 N.J. Super. 550; 530 A.2d 1260; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1279


March 24, 1987, Argued  
July 30, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 14, 1987.
Certification granted In re Daniels, 109 N.J. 496, 537 A.2d 1287, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 1833 (1987)
Affirmed by In re Daniels, 118 N.J. 51, 570 A.2d 416, 1990 N.J. LEXIS 17 (1990)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney, a public defender, challenged an order from the Superior Court of Union County (New Jersey), which found him in criminal contempt of court, imposed a fine, and ordered that he serve two days in county jail. Appellant argued that his statements and conduct were not contemptuous and that he was denied his right to be heard because the trial court found him in contempt before he had a chance to speak.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney, a public defender, who was found in criminal contempt, challenged his conviction and sentence. After being held in contempt, the trial court gave appellant an opportunity to be heard. The trial court then fined him and ordered that he serve two days in county jail. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in finding that his statements and conduct were disrespectful and contemptuous. Appellant also argued that the trial court violated his rights by failing to order an evidentiary hearing in which witnesses could be called to support his case. The appellate court affirmed the finding of criminal contempt because the contempt power could be invoked in the state courts for any conduct that tended to obstruct the course of justice. The appellate court held that appellant was not denied his right to be heard merely because the lower court announced that it found him in contempt before appellant had a chance to speak. The appellate court held that the crucial consideration was whether appellant was afforded an opportunity to address the court. The appellate court, however, reversed the jail term imposed because imprisonment was not an appropriate punishment.


OUTCOME: In a de novo review of the conviction for criminal contempt, the court determined that appellant attorney's behavior was properly punished as contempt. The court held that an evidentiary hearing was not needed because the contumacious conduct occurred entirely in the lower court's presence. The court, however, vacated the jail term imposed because being fined and rebuked in open court was appropriate punishment.

State v. Hurtado


No. A-4764-84T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


219 N.J. Super. 12; 529 A.2d 1000; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1255


May 19, 1987, Argued  
July 9, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 25, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Union County (New Jersey), which denied his motion to suppress evidence seized in an inventory search of defendant's belongings.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant littering in violation of a municipal ordinance. When the police officer asked defendant for identification so that he could write out a summons, defendant could not produce any identification. Defendant was taken to the police station. At the station, identification procedures established that defendant had a record, including incidents of failure to answer other municipal summonses. Defendant's bail was set at $ 100 to secure his attendance for the summons. Defendant could not make bail and was placed in a holding cell. Pursuant to an inventory search, cocaine was discovered on defendant's person. At the trial, defendant's motion to suppress the evidence was denied and defendant pled guilty to unlawful possession of cocaine. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of the motion to suppress. The court found that the officer acted reasonably in taking defendant down to the station for identification purposes. It was reasonable for the officer to set a modest bail as collateral to insure defendant's appearance at the trial. The court found that the inventory of defendant prior to his temporary incarceration was lawful and constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized as the result of an inventory search. The court found that the inventory search, conducted of defendant prior to placing him in a jail cell, was lawful and constitutional.

Cumberland Farms v. Moffett


Nos. A-1917-84T7, A-2427-84T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


218 N.J. Super. 331; 527 A.2d 913; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1211


September 9, 1986, Argued  
June 24, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 7, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Docket No. A-1917-84T7, On appeal from Regulations Promulgated by the Division of Dairy Industry. Docket No. A-2427-84T7, On appeal from a Decision of the Director of Dairy Industry.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant milk dealer challenged rules promulgated by respondent Director, Division of Dairy Industry (New Jersey), which prohibited sales below cost and imposed prior notice requirements upon changes in source of supply by dealers and stores respectively. Appellant milk seller sought review of respondent's final decision revoking his license to sell milk for violation of the sales below cost regulations.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Director, Division of Dairy Industry issued an order revoking appellant milk seller's milk license on the ground that he was selling milk at a price below his cost contrary to N.J. Admin. Code tit. 2, § 53-3.1. Respondent also denied appellant milk dealer's license application due to its continued failure to provide respondent with records to enable it to determine whether appellant dealer was selling at a price below its cost. Appellants sought review of respondent's actions and challenged the validity of respondent's below-cost and notice regulations, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 2, §§ 52-6.1, 53-3.1. The court affirmed, holding that appellant milk dealer failed to exhaust its administrative remedies. The court held that the below cost regulations were within the scope of delegation reasonably contemplated by the enabling statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 4:12A-21, and the regulations were valid on their face as a proper exercise of respondent's wide powers legislatively delegated by § 4:12A-21. The court held that the administrative law judge's findings adopted by respondent were not arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent Director, Division of Dairy Industry, revoking appellant's milk seller's license because the administrative law judge's findings adopted by respondent were are not arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable. Respondent's milk sales below cost and prior notice requirement regulations were a proper exercise of respondent's powers delegated by the legislature.

State v. Ojo Trucking Corp.


Nos. A-4512-85T4, A-4855-85T4, A-4869-85T4 Consolidated


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


217 N.J. Super. 307; 525 A.2d 1125; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1158


May 4, 1987, Argued  
May 18, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 1, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Burlington and Camden Counties (A-4855-85T4 and A-4869-85T4) and from the Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County (A-4512-85T4).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state challenged decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which dismissed of judgments against defendant trucking corporations finding that defendants violated state motor vehicle laws by operating trucks weighing more than their registrations permitted and more than permitted by law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant trucking companies were charged with operating vehicles in excess of its registration, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-20, and exceeding the vehicles' axle weight limitations or the maximum gross weight statutory limitations, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-84(b). Defendant appealed from the judgments against them and the trial court dismissed the complaints. Plaintiff state appealed and the court reversed. The court held that defendants' argument that the registration laws were merely revenue-producing laws was meritless. The court found that the revenue-producing character of the laws was no reason not to apply the laws. The court also found that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-20 was constitutional. The court did not decide whether the defendants could be charged with both registration and weight violations because defendants failed to argue the point in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the judgements against defendant trucking corporations, holding that the registration laws were constitutional, defendants had no basis to argue that the laws should not be applied as written, and defendants waived the argument that it was unconstitutional to charge them with both weight and registration violations.

Graham v. N.J. Real Estate Com


Nos. A-4867-85T6, A-654-86T6


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


217 N.J. Super. 130; 524 A.2d 1321; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1145


March 31, 1987, Argued  
April 27, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 7, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Real Estate Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former licensed realtors sought review of the decision of respondent New Jersey Real Estate Commission, which denied their respective applications for relicensure as real estate salespersons after they allowed their licenses to expire, pursuant to the amended N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:15-9 which required satisfaction of educational and examinational requirements if more than two years had passed since the license expiration.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former licensed realtors allowed their real estate licenses to expire at a time when the law allowed a five-year period for renewing the licenses without having to undergo re-education or re-examination. They sought to renew their licenses five years and three years later, respectively; however, in the interim, the legislature had amended N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:15-9 to allow only a two-year relicensure period. Appellants' applications were denied by respondent New Jersey Real Estate Commission, and they were advised that they had to satisfy the statutory educational and examination requirements. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that ample notice of the amendment to § 45:15-9 was mandated and provided, even if appellants never received it. The federal and state constitutions did not require actual and individual notice. Neither, the court concluded, were appellants' rights violated, because at the time the law was changed they had no vested right that was adversely affected. If they had had protected property interests in their expired licenses, the mandated published notice constituted due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant former licensed realtors' application for relicensure by respondent New Jersey Real Estate Commission, because the statutory amendment that limited their time to renew their licenses without examination or additional courses was not rendered unconstitutional by their lack of actual notice or the fact that their rights under the former statute were adversely affected or diminished.

Mkt. St. Mission v. Bureau of Rooming & Boarding House Stds.


No. A-401-85T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


217 N.J. Super. 56; 524 A.2d 1283; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1143


November 19, 1986, Submitted  
April 23, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 1, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a final decision of the Commissioner, Department of Community Affairs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonprofit religious organization sought review of the order of the Commissioner, Department of Community Affairs (New Jersey), adopting the decision of an administrative law judge, which upheld the assessment of a penalty against appellant for failure to abate fire hazards, in violation of the Rooming and Boarding Housing Act of 1979, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 55:13B-1 et. seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant nonprofit religious organization, a rescue mission, operated a shelter for recovering alcoholics and drug addicts without charge. The Commissioner, Department of Community Affairs, adopted the decision of an administrative law judge, which upheld the assessment of a penalty against appellant for failure to abate fire hazards, in violation of Rooming and Boarding Housing Act of 1979 (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 55:13B-1 et. seq. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the Act was restricted solely to commercial enterprises operating board houses, and that the Act was inapplicable to charitable nonprofit organizations offering their services without charge to homeless and socially handicapped persons. The court found that the Act imposed standards other than those relating to general fire and safety requirements, and that the standards were incompatible with the expressed purpose of a nonprofit religious organization, such as appellant. In addition, the court held that the fire safety provisions of the Act were adequately regulated by existing statutes and ordinances relating to fire, building, and health regulations and requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the Commissioner, Department of Community Affairs and vacated the penalty that was imposed against appellant nonprofit religious organization. The court held that the Rooming and Boarding Housing Act did not apply to appellant because its focus was upon commercial enterprises, not religious missions where the beneficiaries did not pay for the services.

N.J. Div. of Alcoholic Beverage Control v. H & H Wine & Spirit Shop


No. A-3121-85T6


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


216 N.J. Super. 532; 524 A.2d 466; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1127


March 10, 1987, Submitted  
April 13, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 28, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from New Jersey Division of Alcoholic Beverage Control.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee challenged the decision of respondent New Jersey Division of Alcoholic Beverage Control, which suspended appellant's liquor license for 17 days for the sale or delivery of beer to a person under the legal age to purchase and consume alcoholic beverages. Appellant disagreed with respondent's interpretation of N.J. Admin. Code § 13:2-23.1(a), as well as its findings.


OVERVIEW: A state police inspector observed appellant licensee's employee make a sale of alcoholic beverages to a minor and an of-age individual. In the ensuing disciplinary proceeding, respondent New Jersey Division of Alcoholic Beverage Control found three violations of N.J. Admin. Code § 13:2-23.1(a). Respondent suspended appellant's plenary retail distribution license for 17 days. Appellant sought review of the 15-day suspension imposed for the sale or delivery of beer to a person under the legal age to purchase and consume alcoholic beverages. Respondent rejected the initial decision of an administrative law judge, who had dismissed the charge. Appellant challenged respondent's interpretation of the regulation and its findings. The court affirmed the suspension. Although there was conflicting evidence of who actually purchased the alcohol, the state's interest in protecting young people against the dangers resulting from consuming alcoholic beverages was advanced by prohibiting a retail distribution licensee from selling or delivering packaged alcoholic beverages to a person under age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent New Jersey Division of Alcoholic Beverage Control against appellant licensee. The court found that although the facts as to whom the alcohol was sold were in dispute, unless respondent could prohibit delivery to a person under age, who is accompanied by a person of age, violators could falsely claim that sale was made to the person of age when in fact it was to the person under age.

 

1147 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Somerset Cent. Corp.


No. A-1131-86T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


216 N.J. Super. 716; 524 A.2d 893; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1128


March 18, 1987, Argued  
April 13, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 28, 1987.
Certification denied by State v. Somerset Cent. Corp., 108 N.J. 207, 528 A.2d 28, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 940 (1987)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State appealed from the judgment of Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, which denied forfeiture of a boat owned by a bona fide purchaser for value in the state's suit against respondents, the boat, its current owner, and certain others under the forfeiture statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-1a(2).


OVERVIEW: An individual was convicted of theft by deception as the result of an insurance fraud scheme in which he falsely reported to the insurer that his boat was lost at sea. In the meantime, the boat had been sold to a series of bona fide purchasers who were unaware of the fraud. The state filed suit against respondents, the boat, its current owner, and certain others under the forfeiture statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-1a(2). The trial court denied forfeiture of the boat. The court affirmed. The New Jersey Supreme Court had previously held that the forfeiture statute was required to be read to exempt innocent owners and to apply only to owners who used their property for criminal purposes and to those who knowingly allowed others to use their property for such purposes. The statute could also apply to innocent owners who did not use due care to prevent the unlawful use of their property by third parties. None of these circumstances applied here. The state in this case stipulated that the current owner played no part in, nor had any knowledge of, the theft by deception from the insurer regarding the boat.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed the denial of forfeiture because boat's owner had no knowledge of previous owner's insurance fraud. Forfeiture statute was required to be read to exclude innocent owners who did not consent to or know of illegal use of their property and who used due care to prevent that use.

 

1148 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shipp


No. A-4475-84T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


216 N.J. Super. 662; 524 A.2d 864; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1136


March 3, 1987, Submitted  
April 8, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 22, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Warren County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of Superior Court of New Jersey, Warren County, which convicted him of possession of controlled dangerous substance with intent to distribute and sentenced him to 10 years in prison, contending the evidence was insufficient to support the jury's finding of a knowing and intentional possession.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for possession of a controlled dangerous substance with intent to distribute. The evidence at trial showed that he was a front seat passenger in a car driven by a co-defendant, which was stopped for speeding. Defendant's stepmother, another co-defendant, was a passenger in the rear seat. The occupants were ordered out of the car. Defendant's stepmother suggested that she might be able to find some identification in a bag that was next to her in the car. The trooper saw her take two large business envelopes out of the bag and drop them through a storm grate. The envelopes were recovered and found to contain heroin. The court reversed defendant's conviction. Criminal possession signified intentional control and dominion. It could not be inferred from defendant's mere presence at the location where the contraband was found. Here, the heroin was contained in two envelopes which, in turn, were secreted in a bag resting next to defendant's stepmother. To all appearances, it was her bag. Defendant's presence in the car under these circumstances did not suffice to authorize an inference that he was sharing in the intentional control and dominion over the contraband.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction. The contraband was contained in a bag resting on the back seat of a car next to defendant's co-defendant, and defendant's mere presence in the car did not suffice to authorize an inference that he was sharing intentional control and dominion over the contraband.

 

1149 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Private Truck Council v. State


Nos. A-1145-85T1, A-1559-85T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


221 N.J. Super. 89; 534 A.2d 13; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1379


March 16, 1987, Argued  
March 31, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 2, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, plaintiffs, motor carrier trade organization and motor carriers, appealed decisions of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County in favor of defendants, state and officials, which upheld the constitutionality of the Counterpart Fee Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-6.


OVERVIEW: In two separate cases, plaintiffs, motor carrier trade organization and motor carriers, filed suit against defendants, state and officials, arguing that the Counterpart Fee Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39.3-6, which imposed a tax on trucks operating in New Jersey that are registered in one of 18 states that imposed taxes for highway use on trucks registered in New Jersey, was unconstitutional. The trial court upheld the Act, granting summary judgment for defendants. Plaintiffs appealed. The court held that the purpose of the Act was retaliatory in nature because it was designed to induce other states not to impose highway use taxes on New Jersey registered vehicles. Because retaliation was not a legitimate local public interest and the tax discriminated against interstate vehicles, the Act violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The court reversed the decisions and awarded refunds to plaintiffs for fees paid after the filing of their complaints. Plaintiffs were not entitled to counsel fees because 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 did not apply to this type of action. The ruling denying class certification in one of the cases was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions and remanded the case for further proceedings because the Counterpart Fee Act violated the Commerce Clause as retaliation against other states was not a legitimate local public interest and the tax discriminated against interstate vehicles. Plaintiffs were awarded refunds of fees paid after their complaints were filed. The court affirmed the order denying class certification in one of these consolidated actions.
