FOP v. Newark


No. A-4788-85T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


216 N.J. Super. 461; 524 A.2d 430; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1092; 2 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 437; 44 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P37,374


October 15, 1986, Argued  
March 26, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 3, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fraternal order of police appealed the order of the Superior Court, Essex County (New Jersey), which sustained defendant city's directive mandating that all members of the police narcotics bureau be subjected to urine testing for drug abuse both upon transfer into the bureau and at least twice a year afterwards, on the grounds that the directive required an unconstitutional search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff fraternal order of police filed an action to invalidate a directive issued by defendant city police director mandating that all members of the narcotic bureau be subjected to urine testing for drug abuse both upon transfer into the bureau and at least twice a year afterwards. The trial court sustained the directive, and plaintiffs appealed. The court found that drug testing without probable cause or reasonable individualized suspicion was unreasonable and constitutionally invalid. The court found that such testing constituted a significant interference with personal privacy and autonomy, and it involved an intrusion upon a most private kind of conduct. Both in concept and in practice, the intrusion was profoundly demeaning. Drug testing also had serious pragmatic implications including loss of employment and possible criminal prosecution. The protectable privacy interests of plaintiffs were thus very substantial. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for the entry of judgment invalidating defendant's directive and for the trial court to address plaintiff's claim for damages under 42 U.S.C.A. § 1983 arising from the urine tests already taken.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for entry of a judgment in favor of plaintiff fraternal order of police. Defendant city's drug testing of police in the absence of probable cause or a reasonable individualized suspicion was unreasonable and unconstitutional. The court also remanded to the trial court for consideration of plaintiff's claim for damages arising from urine tests already taken.

Beaudoin v. Belmar Tavern Owners Asso


No. A-828-86T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


216 N.J. Super. 177; 523 A.2d 256; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1096


February 25, 1987, Argued  
March 24, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 3, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff resident challenged the order from the Superior Court, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which granted summary judgment dismissing plaintiff's complaint to enjoin defendant county clerk from placing two referendum questions on the election ballot pursuant to defendant tavern association's petition. Plaintiff maintained that placing the referendum questions on the ballot violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 33:1-47.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant tavern owners association petitioned the Board of Commissioners to place on the 1986 ballot two questions to expand the hours of sale of alcoholic beverages. Plaintiff resident claimed that placing the questions on the ballot violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 33:1-47.1, which stated that after there had been a referendum, no further referendum on the same question could be held for another five years. Plaintiff sought to enjoin defendant county clerk from placing the questions on the ballot. The trial court entered summary judgment against plaintiff and held that there was no violation of § 33:1-47.1. Plaintiff appealed. While his appeal was pending, both questions were approved at the 1986 election. Plaintiff sought to enjoin defendant county clerk from certifying the election results and to accelerate the appeal. The court denied injunctive relief but granted the acceleration. On appeal, the court held that the 1985 ballot questions, which limited the hours of sale for alcoholic beverages, were the same substantive questions as those placed on the 1986 ballot. As § 33:1-47.1 was mandatory, the violation of the statute invalidated the election.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment entered in favor of defendant tavern owners association (Association) and defendant county clerk, and directed the entry of judgment in plaintiff resident's favor. Placing the referendum questions submitted by defendant Association on the 1986 election ballot violated the five-year rule and, as the five-year rule was mandatory, not directory, the violation invalidated the election.

 

1152 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Scioscia


No. A-1240-85T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


216 N.J. Super. 644; 524 A.2d 855; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1123; 1987-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P67,562


December 9, 1986, Argued  
March 23, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 22, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from New Jersey Board of Public Utilities.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a garbage collection service and its manager and part owner, sought review of an order of the New Jersey Board of Public Utilities (BPU), which prohibited the manager from participating in the solid waste business after appellants were convicted of conspiracy in restraint of trade in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:9-3.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were convicted of conspiracy in restraint of trade in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:9-3. In a separate administrative proceeding, the BPU concluded that appellant manager had violated the Solid Waste Utility Control Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:13A-1 et seq. (Act) and prohibited appellant manager from participating in the solid waste business. The court affirmed, rejecting appellant manager's argument that a criminal conviction under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:9-3 for restraint of trade was insufficient to prove a violation under the Act for monopolization, stating that monopolization was closely related to, if not synonymous with, restraint of trade. The court also disagreed with appellant manager's claim that the BPU exceeded its statutory authority by prohibiting him from participating in the solid waste business, holding that authority to exclude individuals could reasonably be implied from the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the BPU, holding that appellant manager's conviction for conspiracy in restraint of trade was a sufficient basis to conclude that appellant manager had violated the Solid Waste Utility Control Act.

 

1153 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Kim Real Estate Enters. v. N. Bergen


No. A-2394-85T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


215 N.J. Super. 255; 521 A.2d 900; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1045


January 7, 1987, Argued  
February 23, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 12, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners of multi-family units, sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Hudson County, New Jersey, which was entered in favor of defendants, township and some of its officials, and concluded that an amendment to a rent leveling ordinance clearly intended to refer only to the immediate preceding calendar year.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, owners of multi-family units, instituted an action against defendant, township and some of its officials, and sought judgment declaring that the term "previous year" in the last amendment was intended to refer to the year previous to the enactment of the ordinance. In the alternative, plaintiffs sought a declaration that the amendment was unconstitutional as applied. The trial judge entered judgment in favor of defendant and concluded that the amendment clearly intended to refer to the immediate preceding calendar year. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the amendment intended to permit a tax pass-through only for increases from the preceding calendar year. The court held that the language of the amendment could not have been any clearer. By adding the term "previous year" and deleting reference to a previous year's tax, there was no doubt that the governing body intended to amend the provision to limit tax pass-throughs to increases from the preceding year. The court held that under the circumstances, it was bound by that clear legislative expression.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which held that an amendment to a rent-leveling ordinance clearly intended to refer only to the immediate preceding calendar year. The court held that there was a clear legislative history that expressed the governing body's intent to modify the surcharge to permit plaintiffs, owners of multi-family units, to pass through tax increases to tenants from the preceding year.

N.J. Hous. & Mortg. Fin. Agency v. Moses

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state agency appealed orders of the Superior Court of Essex County (New Jersey), which dismissed plaintiff's complaints in condemnation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff state agency brought various complaints in condemnation. The trial court dismissed the complaints, holding that plaintiff did not have the authority to condemn the properties and that there was a lack of legislated standards as to when plaintiff's condemnation power could be exercised constitutionally. The appellate court consolidated the cases for review. It disagreed with the trial court, holding that plaintiff had the power to condemn the properties and that the grant of power, under the New Jersey Housing and Mortgage Finance Agency Law of 1983, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 55:14K-1 et seq., was accompanied by standards sufficiently clear and definite to sustain its constitutionality. However, the court affirmed the dismissals because it found that plaintiff had failed to disclose its appraisals of defendant owners' properties during pre-litigation negotiations. The court held that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 20:3-6 required such disclosure and that plaintiff's willful violation of § 20:3-6 warranted the remedy of dismissal.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed orders that dismissed various complaints in condemnation. The court held that plaintiff state agency willfully failed to disclose its appraisals of defendant owners' properties during pre-litigation negotiations.

In re Njpdes Permit No. NJ 0055247


Nos. A-2512-85T7, A-2516-85T7, A-2518-85T7, A-2521-85T7

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from final orders of the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, public interest group, challenged the order of the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection that granted air pollution control and solid waste permits to respondent applicant for the construction of a resource recovery facility.


OVERVIEW: Respondent applicant sought air pollution and solid waste permits from the department of environmental protection for the construction of a resource recovery facility. The department approved the permits, but they were contingent upon acceptance of several revisions, modifications, and additions in the emission data. Appellants, public interest group, challenged the issuance of the permits, asserting that the emissions limitations were not stringent enough, that the solid waste permit was issued in error because it was without a disclosure statement, and respondent failed to designate a residual landfill. The court affirmed the grant of the permits because there was no merit in appellants' arguments. The court held that respondent's application, which included the lowest available emission rate, was proper because the county was a nonattainment area. The court held that the department was without the authority to require a disclosure statement and, therefore, issuance of the solid waste permit was not error. The court also held that respondent's permits were already conditioned upon the identification of a residual landfill.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the issuance of air pollution and solid waste permits in favor of respondent applicant for the construction of the resource recovery facility because application of the lowest available emission rate was proper, as the county was a nonattainment area. The court also noted that the permits were conditioned upon respondent's identifying a residual landfill.

 

1156 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zalta


No. A-1859-85T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


217 N.J. Super. 209; 525 A.2d 328; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1153


December 10, 1986, Argued  
January 22, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 13, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which convicted defendant of driving while on the revoked list, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-40. Defendant had not sought restoration of his license.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of driving while on the revoked list, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-40. Defendant challenged his conviction, asserting that the prohibition against driving applied only to the period of suspension. In affirming the conviction, the court held that the prohibition against driving with a suspended licensed continued past the suspension period. According to the court, a reasonable interpretation of section 39:3-40 meant that the suspension continued until actual restoration of the license by the director. The court stated that implicit in the director of motor vehicle's pervasive power over the licensing and suspending of driving privileges was a right to keep a license in suspension until it was restored after appropriate application for restoration by the licensee. Thus, the court concluded that defendant was in violation of the statute because he never sought restoration of his license.


OUTCOME: The judgment that convicted defendant for driving while on the revoked list was affirmed because defendant's license suspension continued until his license was restored by the director of motor vehicle.

Cooper Medical Ctr. v. Camden


No. A-1238-85T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


214 N.J. Super. 493; 520 A.2d 413; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1000


November 25, 1986, Submitted  
January 15, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 5, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospital appealed an order from the Superior Court, Camden County (New Jersey), which dismissed plaintiff's complaint for payment of medical services rendered to two suspects injured during a police apprehension.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff hospital brought suit against defendant city and county seeking payment for medical services rendered to two suspects that were injured during a police apprehension. The trial court entered summary judgment in defendants' favor and an appeal ensued. The court affirmed the judgment. According to the court, the obligation to provide necessary medical care and treatment to persons injured during the course of apprehension by municipal police was required by the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court held defendants' obligation was met when they transported the suspects to the hospital for treatment. The court stated that there was no obligation on the part of defendants to pay for medical care and treatment where police injured the patient during apprehension. Next, the court held that there was no taking of property by defendants' failure to pay for the cost of medical treatment because Diagnostic Recovery Group (DRG) System of New Jersey reimbursed plaintiff.


OUTCOME: Judgment dismissing plaintiff hospital's claim for payment for medical services rendered to two suspects injured during a police apprehension was affirmed because defendants had no obligation to pay for medical care and treatment where the patient was injured by police during apprehension. The court held that defendants met their obligation when they delivered the suspects to the hospital for treatment.

State, Dep't of Law & Public Safety, Div. of Gaming Enforcement v. Merlino


Nos. A-937-85T1, A-938-85T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


216 N.J. Super. 579; 524 A.2d 821; 1987 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1130


November 17, 1986, Argued  
January 15, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 5, 1987.
Certification granted State, Dep't of Law & Public Safety, Div. of Gaming Enforcement v. Leonetti, 107 N.J. 657, 527 A.2d 475, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 1777 (1987)
Certification granted State, Dep't of Law & Public Safety, Div. of Gaming Enforcement v. Merlino, 107 N.J. 658, 527 A.2d 475, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 1789 (1987)
Affirmed by State, Dep't of Law & Public Safety, Div. of Gaming Enforcement v. Merlino, 109 N.J. 134, 535 A.2d 968, 1988 N.J. LEXIS 2 (1988)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a final decision of the New Jersey Casino Control Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gamblers sought review of an order of the New Jersey Casino Control Commission, which placed them on a list and excluded them from the premises of any licensed gambling casino in New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: Respondent state division of gaming enforcement filed petitions to place appellant gamblers on the casino control commission's list of persons to be excluded from licensed casinos. Each petition alleged that appellants were associates of a known career offender. The administrative law judge (ALJ) found that respondent did not meet its burden. The casino control commission remanded for a new hearing. On remand, the ALJ reversed. Appellants sought review. No live witnesses appeared at the hearings before the ALJ, except appellants, who invoked their U.S. Const. amend. V. privilege against self-incrimination. The court affirmed because the findings grounded in hearsay evidence did not have to be supported by a residuum of competent evidence. The statute was not void for vagueness because a person of ordinary intelligence would understand that a person who possessed appellants' characteristics would be deemed "inimical" to the state's interests within the meaning of N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 5:12-71(a) and N.J. Admin. Code tit. 19, § 48-1.3(a). The commission was allowed to draw adverse inferences from appellants' plea of a U.S. Const. amend. V privilege.


OUTCOME: The order of the Casino Control Commission that placed appellant gamblers on a list and excluded them from the premises of any licensed gambling casino in New Jersey was affirmed because a person of ordinary intelligence would understand that a person who possessed appellants' characteristics would be deemed "inimical" to the state's interests.

Harrison Assocs. v. Rent Leveling Bd.


No. A-3067-85T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


215 N.J. Super. 1; 520 A.2d 1150; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1561


November 26, 1986, Submitted  
December 29, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 3, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff apartment owner challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Somerset County (New Jersey), which affirmed the rent leveling board's decision concluding that plaintiff was bound by the 3 1/2 percent maximum rental increase cap prescribed by local ordinance as it applied to defendant tenants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff apartment owner challenged the constitutionality of a local rent leveling ordinance that capped rental increases at 3 1/2 percent. Although the trial court found for plaintiff, the appellate division reversed and ordered plaintiff to reimburse tenants by the difference between that which was collected and the 3 1/2 percent cap. Defendant tenants complained to the rent leveling board, alleging that plaintiff had violated the local ordinance capping rental increases by raising defendants' rent by 4.8 percent. Plaintiff argued that, because the maximum cap rate had since been modified to 6 1/2 percent, it was entitled to apply this rate to the new lease with defendants. The board concluded that plaintiffs were bound by the 3 1/2 percent cap rate in place when it resigned the lease with defendants. On appeal to the superior court, the trial court affirmed the board's determination. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that plaintiff was subject to the 3 1/2 percent cap because it was in effect at the time that the new lease was signed. The court ruled that the local ordinance was not preempted by the Anti-Eviction Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2A:18-61.1 and 2A:18-61.2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had upheld the decision of the rent leveling board. The court ruled that plaintiff apartment owner was bound to the 3 1/2 percent rental rate increase with respect to the lease with defendant tenants, because this cap rate had been in place at the time that the new lease was signed.

Thanasoulis v. Winston Tower 200 Asso


No. A-2003-85T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


214 N.J. Super. 408; 519 A.2d 911; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1549


October 27, 1986, Submitted  
December 24, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 16, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a nonresident owner, challenged the decision from the Superior Court, Bergen County (New Jersey), which granted defendant condominium owners' association's motion for summary judgment, contending that the rule adopted by defendant, which increased the parking fee for tenants of nonresident owners while leaving untouched the fee charged to resident owners, was unreasonable and unconstitutionally discriminatory.


OVERVIEW: Defendant condominium owners' association increased the parking fee for tenants of non-resident owners but did not change the fee charged to resident owners. Plaintiff, a nonresident owner, attacked the rule as being unreasonable and unconstitutionally discriminatory. The trial court held that the fee structure was not unconstitutional because there was no state action and that the rule did not burden nonresident owners any more than resident owners because the tenant dealt directly with defendant and not the owner. On appeal the court held that, to determine whether defendant breached its fiduciary duty, it had to be determined whether its action was authorized by its own by-laws, and, if so, whether the action was fraudulent, self-dealing, or unconscionable. The court found that the action was authorized and that it was not fraudulent, self-dealing, or unconscionable because it benefitted all owners. The court therefore affirmed the granting of the summary judgment to defendant.


OUTCOME: The granting of defendant condominium owners' association summary judgment motion that upheld its revised fee schedule was affirmed because the action to raise the fees was authorized by the by-laws and was not fraudulent, self-dealing, or unconscionable.

Piscopo v. Lemi Excavating Co.


No. A-643-85T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


215 N.J. Super. 149; 521 A.2d 846; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1567


November 18, 1986, Submitted  
December 10, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 11, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Judgment of the Division of Workers' Compensation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, 29-year old son of deceased, challenged denial of his claim to workers' compensation benefits, by the Division of Workers' Compensation (New Jersey), arguing that he was improperly denied benefits, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-13, because the benefit-related definition of dependent was arbitrary and capricious and violated equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, 29-year-old son of deceased, sought review of denial of his claim to workers' compensation benefits for his father's compensable accident, contending that the Division of Workers' Compensation erred in finding that while he was dependent upon deceased, within the meaning of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-13, he was denied compensations benefits because the statute provided that in computing compensation only those under 18 and over 40 were included. Petitioner argued that such statute violated the equal protection clause, was arbitrary and capricious, unconstitutional, and served no legitimate government function. On appeal, the lower court judgment was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that dependency for workers' compensation purposes was determined not by actual dependency but by qualification under the strict terms of the statute. The court further held that as the age parameters defining dependency in the statute were at least rationally based, the court had no discretion to enlarge the class of eligible dependents.


OUTCOME: The denial of benefits was affirmed as the age parameters defining dependency contained in the statute were rationally based, and could not be altered by the courts without the action of the legislature.

Henningsen v. Randolph


No. A-2592-85T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


214 N.J. Super. 82; 518 A.2d 503; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1495


September 17, 1986, Argued  
November 24, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 15, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, which upheld the grant of a use variance by respondent board of adjustment to respondent business partnership for a two-story office building in a residential zone.


OVERVIEW: Appellant residents brought an action that challenged the grant of a use variance by respondent board of adjustment to respondent business partnership for a two-story office building in a residential zone. The trial court upheld the variance on the basis that a special reason existed for a use variance under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-70(d), that the subject property was not realistically developable for residential use, and that an office would relate well to the area's development. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that there had not been a sufficient showing of a special reason for a use variance. The court stated that a use other than one inherently promoting the general welfare could provide a special reason for a variance under § 40:55D-70(d) if it promoted the public health, safety, or welfare and was particularly suited to the location. The court found, however, that the proposed use would be a commercial enterprise for profit, not per se contributing to the public health or safety or otherwise serving a public need. The fact that the proposed office would fit well into the area was not a special reason for a variance under § 40:55D-70(d).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision to uphold the grant of a use variance by respondent board of adjustment to respondent business partnership for a two-story office building in a residential zone that was challenged by appellant residents. The court held that construction of an office building was not a special reason for a use variance under the statute.

Nyt Cable Tv v. Homestead at Mansfield


Nos. A-4251-84T1, A-4734-84T1, A-5102-84T1 (Consolidated)

Certification granted NYT Cable TV v. Homestead at Mansfield, Inc., 107 N.J. 154, 526 A.2d 213, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 1578 (1987)
Affirmed by NYT Cable TV v. Homestead at Mansfield, Inc., 111 N.J. 21, 543 A.2d 10, 1988 N.J. LEXIS 54 (1988)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Chancery Division, Burlington County, and the Board of Public Utility Commissioners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Homeowners' association and state board of public utilities appellants sought review of judgment in favor of cable television company respondent's favor on consolidated appeals in a suit under the Planned Real Estate Development Full Disclosure Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:22A-21 et seq., and the Cable Television Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:5A-1 et seq., in the Burlington County Superior Court, Chancery Division.


OVERVIEW: Appellants homeowners' association and state board of utilities sought review of judgment in favor of cable television company respondent in connection with a suit challenging validity of an application of the provision enabling installation of cable facilities and administratively delegating the compensation that had to be paid for such exercise. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding the administrative regulation prescribing rules for the use of eminent domain power, N.J. Admin. Code § 48:5A-2, was valid. The court determined the regulation was incidental to the broad overall powers delegated to the administrative agency charged with administering the Cable Television Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:5A-49. The court explained there was a strong presumption in favor of administrative rule making authority and in finding rules thereby adopted valid. The court found the provision establishing just compensation was not unreasonable by reason of a presumption of what qualified as "just." The court further found restriction to the before and after method was also appropriate in view of the fact installation did not result in any "taking" in fee based on physical occupation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment in favor of cable television company respondent because appellants homeowners association and state board of utilities' challenge to Cable Television Act and legislative delegation of a determination of just compensation in connection with enabling cable television facilities installation failed because legislation was constitutional and constituted a valid delegation of authority to administrative agency.

 

1164 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


No. A-4969-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


213 N.J. Super. 426; 517 A.2d 513; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1465


September 17, 1986, Argued  
November 10, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 21, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior court, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision by the Superior Court of Monmouth County (New Jersey) that convicted and sentenced defendant for purposeful or knowing murder, felony murder, aggravated arson, contrary and arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for purposeful or knowing murder, felony murder, aggravated arson, contrary and arson. Defendant appealed, contending that defendant's actions did not constitute purposeful or knowing conduct sufficient to sustain a murder conviction. Defendant argued that, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:2-2b(2), defendant had to be practically certain that defendant's conduct would result in death. The reviewing court disagreed, stating that a murder conviction based on knowing conduct could result from conduct that was practically certain to cause serious bodily injury when death was a result of the injury caused. Therefore, the state had to show only that defendant wanted to cause serious bodily injury which ended up resulting in death. Defendant also argued that, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3b, there was no minimum term of 30 years imprisonment without parole eligibility. However, the court looked to the legislative history and found that the legislature's intent was to have a mandatory minimum sentence of 30 years upon conviction for murder. The decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for purposeful or knowing murder was affirmed because a murder conviction based on knowing conduct could result from conduct that was practically certain to cause serious bodily injury when death was a result of the injury caused.

 

1165 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Serrano


No. A-346-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


213 N.J. Super. 419; 517 A.2d 509; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1472


October 7, 1986, Submitted  
November 7, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 21, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division,Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Middlesex County (New Jersey), which convicted him, upon a jury trial, of terroristic threats, kidnapping, possession of a rifle for an unlawful purpose, possession of weapons with purpose to use unlawfully, aggravated assault, and murder. Appellant contended it was error to deny his request for a jury instruction on diminished capacity under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:4-2.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted in a jury trial of terroristic threats, kidnapping, possession of a rifle for an unlawful purpose, possession of weapons with purpose to use unlawfully, aggravated assault, and murder. He sought review, claiming that it was error for the trial court to deny his request for a jury instruction on diminished capacity pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:4-2. The court affirmed the convictions for terroristic threats and kidnapping but reversed the remaining convictions, finding that it was reversible error to deny appellant's requested jury instruction. The court concluded that the instruction could have affected the jury's determination on appellant's ability to act purposely or knowingly, which were elements of the offenses for the reversed convictions. The court determined that the testimony of witnesses from both sides indicated that a question existed on appellant's ability to form the requisite state of mind that was an element of the offenses. The court concluded that consideration of the diminished capacity defense might well have led the jury to conclude that defendant acted only recklessly or without any culpable state of mind at all.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for terroristic threats and kidnapping but reversed the convictions for possession of a rifle for an unlawful purpose, possession of weapons with purpose to use unlawfully, aggravated assault, and murder, finding it was reversible error to deny his request for a jury instruction on diminished capacity that could have affected the determination on his ability to act purposely or knowingly.

Ciccolello v. Middlesex County Bd. of Freeholders


No. A-1180-85T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


214 N.J. Super. 1; 518 A.2d 228; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1504


October 7, 1986, Submitted  
November 5, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 3, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, Middlesex County (New Jersey), which granted summary judgment to defendants, the county director of corrections and the county board of freeholders, on the ground that a two year statute of limitations had expired on plaintiff's action for an alleged beating while plaintiff was incarcerated in a county correctional center.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff prisoner sought review of the lower court's decision to grant defendants, the county director of corrections and the county board of freeholders, summary judgment based on the expiration of a two-year statute of limitations on plaintiff's action. Plaintiff filed an action alleging that he was beaten while incarcerated in a county facility. After his release from the county facility, plaintiff was later incarcerated in a state institution. The appellate court found that, contrary to plaintiff's assertion that the statute of limitations was tolled for the pendency of plaintiff's incarceration, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:8-8 required plaintiff to file a claim during a 90-day limitations period. That period started and expired after plaintiff's release from the county facility and prior to his incarceration in a state institution. As such, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's summary judgment decision. The court found that although the relevant statute was tolled during the period of a prisoner's incarceration, plaintiff had been released from custody for a period. During that time, he was required to file a claims notification but failed to do so.

 

1167 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hughes


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


215 N.J. Super. 295; 521 A.2d 1295; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1571


October 7, 1986, Argued  
October 24, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by State v. Hughes, 107 N.J. 55, 526 A.2d 142, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 1304 (1986)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Camden County (New Jersey), which convicted appellant, upon jury verdict, of conspiracy to rob. Appellant raised several points of error on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of conspiracy to rob upon jury verdict. On appeal, he asserted several points of alleged error, including claims that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on the affirmative defense of renunciation of purpose, and that the prosecution improperly used its peremptory challenges. Appellant allegedly told a police officer of a planned robbery approximately a month before the robbery took place. However, appellant never revealed that he had agreed to participate in the robbery. The appellate court found that the defense of renunciation required that appellant reveal his participation in the conspiracy. The court also found that the prosecution did not improperly strike jurors of a certain race because, although the appellate court found no adequate reason for the strike of two jurors, it would rely on the fair and impartial decision making of the trial court. Finally, the appellate court rejected appellant's contention that the jury's verdict was in error because the jury rendered an inconsistent verdict by failing to convict appellant for actual robbery, but convicting him for conspiracy to rob. As such, the lower court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant for conspiracy to rob was affirmed, because the court rejected appellant's claim that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury as to the defense of renunciation of purpose where appellant claimed he was never involved in the conspiracy, and therefore could not have renounced his participation.

Ocean Pines v. Point Pleasant


No. A-2912-85T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


213 N.J. Super. 351; 517 A.2d 472; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1477


September 24, 1986, Argued  
October 22, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 14, 1986.
Certification granted Ocean Pines, Ltd. v. Point Pleasant, 107 N.J. 112, 526 A.2d 183, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 1783 (1987)
Certification granted Ocean Pines, Ltd. v. Edwards, 107 N.J. 112, 526 A.2d 183, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 1765 (1987)
Certification granted Ocean Pines, Ltd. v. Point Pleasant, 107 N.J. 113, 526 A.2d 183, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 1852 (1987)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Ocean Pines, Ltd. v. Point Pleasant, 112 N.J. 1, 547 A.2d 691, 1988 N.J. LEXIS 100 (1988)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from final order of Tax Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of the Tax Court (New Jersey), which dismissed appellant's complaint for failure to comply with N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-34 in appellant's action against respondents, a borough and the state Attorney General, seeking reassessment of appellant's property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer purchased an apartment complex in respondent borough and after failing to provide the principal tax assessor the requested income and expense data for the complex, appellant filed a petition with the board of taxation requesting the reduction of its assessment. The lower court dismissed appellant's action finding that appellant failed to satisfy the "good cause" provision of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-34. The court reversed the lower court's dismissal and remanded the cause for the consideration of the claim of unreasonableness. The court determined that it could not say whether appellant was discriminated against and whether there was an improper "spot assessment" because the assessor reassessed at approximately 87 percent of its sale price. The court found that appellant's due process rights were not violated by a strict enforcement of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-34. Appellant was still able to appeal the reasonableness of the assessment based upon the data available to the assessor, and appellant could assert that the data used did not reasonably justify the results reached, but appellant could not supply new income or expense data or expert interpretations thereof.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing appellant taxpayer's action against respondents, a borough and the state Attorney General, for reassessment of his real property, and the cause was remanded for consideration of the claim of unreasonableness, because the court could not determine whether appellant was discriminated against and whether there was an improper "spot assessment."

State v. Reevey


No. A-3840-84T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


213 N.J. Super. 37; 516 A.2d 269; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1437


September 9, 1986, Submitted  
October 7, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 22, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, that convicted defendant of heroin and cocaine distribution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the offenses of heroin and cocaine distribution in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 24:21-19a(1). Defendant sought review of the trial court judgment, arguing that the recent amendment to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-6b, as applied to Title 24 offenses was unconstitutional as being ambiguous and vague. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-6b was not unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the words in the statute, when given their ordinary and popular meaning, have a sufficient popular connotation to apprise men of common intelligence, with a reasonable degree of certainty, as to the possibility of the imposition of a parole ineligibility term. The court further held that the overwhelming evidence indicated that defendant was specifically aware of the possibility of imposition of a parole ineligibility term when he entered his guilty pleas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of drug distribution offenses. The court held that the statute permitting parole ineligibility term was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1170 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Kirk v. Newark


No. A-3930-84T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


212 N.J. Super. 201; 514 A.2d 839; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1371


May 20, 1986, Submitted  
August 4, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 18, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accused appealed a judgment non obstante verdicto from the Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County (New Jersey), that dismissed plaintiff's action brought under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against defendant detective for filing a criminal complaint without probable cause.


OVERVIEW: Based upon a prosecutor's advice after reviewing a caseworker's report and plaintiff accused's exculpatory statement, defendant detective filed a criminal complaint against plaintiff for aggravated assault. Because a subsequent medical report was consistent with plaintiff's exculpatory statement, defendant administratively dismissed the criminal complaint. Plaintiff filed suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, claiming that defendant violated his civil rights by initiating the complaint without probable cause. The court reversed the judgment non obstante verdicto (n.o.v.) in favor of defendant. The court held that the determination whether probable cause existed was for the jury to determine, because questions existed regarding the reasonableness of defendant's investigation which formed the basis of her belief that plaintiff committed a crime. Because there were also disputed facts with respect to the objective reasonableness of defendant's knowledge at the time of instituting the criminal complaint, with respect to a qualified immunity defense of reliance on counsel advice, this issue too was for a jury to determine. Thus entry of judgment n.o.v. was inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment non obstante verdicto that dismissed plaintiff accused's complaint for civil rights violation by defendant detective. Whether there was probable cause to initiate a criminal complaint against plaintiff was for a jury to determine. Further, the factual dispute regarding defendant's defenses also required resolution by a jury.

 

1171 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Meyer


No. A-3057-85T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


212 N.J. Super. 1; 512 A.2d 1139; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1342


May 28, 1986, Argued  
July 16, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the municipal court for selling obscene material in public, Paramus, N.J., Ordinances No. 77-6, for failure to cover two allegedly obscene magazines. On appeal, the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County (New Jersey) remanded for trial. The court granted defendant's motion for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty in municipal court for violating an obscenity ordinance, Paramus, N.J., Ordinances No. 77-6, prohibiting the sale of obscene material exposed to public view. Defendant failed to cover two allegedly obscene magazines. The superior court denied defendant's motion to dismiss. The court granted defendant's motion for leave to appeal. The court reversed, holding that the ordinance was unenforceable; N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:1-5d prohibited the enactment of local ordinances that conflicted with or were preempted by the New Jersey Code of Criminal Justice; the issue of obscenity was largely preempted by state law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:34-2; while state law allowed municipalities to enact zoning ordinances regulating the sale of obscene material, the ordinance at issue controlled not the location of the sale of obscene material, but the manner of sale; and the ordinance's definition of obscenity was unconstitutional for failure to comply with the three-part test applying contemporary community standards and a determination whether the work depicted sexual conduct defined by state law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's judgment which remanded defendant's case for trial in the municipal court following his conviction for the public sale of obscene magazines. The court held that the city's ordinance was unenforceable because the regulation of the manner of sale of obscene material was preempted by the state.

Clark v. New Jersey Div. of Motor Vehicles


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


211 N.J. Super. 708; 512 A.2d 588; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1463


June 3, 1986, Submitted  
July 16, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from a final decision of Robert S. Kline, Acting Director of the Division of Motor Vehicles.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a determination by respondent, Acting Director of the Division of Motor Vehicles (New Jersey), that assessed insurance surcharge penalties pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:29A-33 based on petitioner's convictions for speeding, driving while intoxicated, and failing to take a breathalyzer test, on the ground that the imposition was unconstitutionally applied to him ex post facto and the surcharges were penal in nature.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was assessed insurance surcharge penalties based upon convictions for speeding,, driving while intoxicated, and failing to take a breathalyzer test. An administrative law judge determined petitioner was subject to the Merit Rating Plan surcharge. Respondent Acting Director of the Division of Motor Vehicles affirmed. Petitioner contended the imposition of the surcharge pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:29A-33, et seq. had been unconstitutionally applied to him on an ex post facto basis and that the surcharges were penal in nature. The appellate court affirmed and determined to be without merit petitioner's claim that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:29A-33, et seq. as applied to him violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws. The prohibition applied only when the legislation was retrospective in operation and the Merit Rating Plan surcharge was approved prior to petitioner's arrest. The court ruled petitioner's claim that the statute was punitive in nature also failed because the prohibition against ex post facto law only applied to punitive legislation and did not apply to retrospective legislation involving a statutory system of civil penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that assessed insurance surcharge penalties against petitioner and held that the statute allowing the imposition of such penalties was not punitive in nature and that the penalties were not proscribed under the ex post facto provision of the state or federal constitutions.

Riggs v. Township of Long Beach


No. A-5799-82T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


212 N.J. Super. 69; 514 A.2d 45; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1645


May 27, 1986, Reargued  
July 16, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 18, 1986.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted by Riggs v. Long Beach, 107 N.J. 81, 526 A.2d 160, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 1793 (1987)
Reversed by Riggs v. Long Beach, 109 N.J. 601, 538 A.2d 808, 1988 N.J. LEXIS 22 (1988)


PRIOR HISTORY: Argued October 16, 1984. Decided November 1, 1984. On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.
Riggs v. Long Beach, 101 N.J. 515, 503 A.2d 284, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 863 (1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant township sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Ocean County, which declared that Long Beach Township, N.J., Ordinance No. 81-1C was invalid and had no effect, in favor of plaintiff landowners.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowners challenged Long Beach Township, N.J., Ordinance No. 81-1C, which rezoned plaintiffs' property and restricted its use. Plaintiffs alleged that the ordinance constituted spot zoning, was arbitrary and capricious, and was contrary to the purposes and intent of the Municipal Land Use Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55 D-1 et seq. The trial court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional. A new ordinance was passed. The appeals court reversed and held that the procedural defects had been corrected. The supreme court held that the new ordinance was identical to the old and remanded. On review, the court reversed and upheld the ordinance. The court held that by designating the area as public open space, defendant township intended to provide recreational facilities and access to the bay, and to preserve the aesthetic value of a bay view from the boulevard, and that, therefore, the challenged ordinance advanced one of the several purposes enumerated in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55 D-2. The ordinance did not constitute spot zoning because zoning the area to a lower density was in accordance with and furthered defendant's land use plan and advanced the community interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that declared that a zoning ordinance was invalid, in favor of plaintiff landowners. The court held that defendant township, by enacting the ordinance, was advancing a land use plan that was in the interest of the community.

In re Medicaid Long Term Care Servs. Bulletin 84-2


Nos. A-3120-83T2, A-2350-84T6 CONSOLIDATED


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


212 N.J. Super. 48; 513 A.2d 967; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1363


March 26, 1986, Argued  
July 15, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 18, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Department of Human Services, Division of Medical Assistance and Health Services.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nursing home sought review of a regulation adopted by the Department of Human Services, Division of Medical Assistance and Health Services (New Jersey) and the underlying bulletin, providing a revised policy for the calculation of reimbursable final per diem rates chargeable by long-term care facilities under the Medicaid program.


OVERVIEW: In its challenge to a regulation adopted by the Department of Human Services, Division of Medical Assistance and Health Services, appellant nursing home argued that the regulation was ultra vires, violated federal and state Medicaid reimbursement schemes and, by its retroactive application, offended due process. The regulation in question provided a revised policy for the calculation of reimbursable final per diem rates chargeable by long-term care facilities under the Medicaid program. The court held that the regulation provided for the setting of the per diem rate on the basis of cost reports submitted by the facility. Further, the appeal process permitted the correction of inaccurate cost reporting during a 15-month period following the setting of a rate. Therefore the regulation and its reflected policy did not offend the statutory scheme. The court was satisfied that a balancing of the public interest served by the regulation against the settled expectations of long term care facilities affected by its retroactive application favored the regulation and compelled the conclusion that its implementation did not infringe upon due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal on the basis that the regulation constituted a valid exercise of the commissioner's statutory discretion to administer the Medicaid program, was in harmony with the legislative history of the federal Medicaid statute, served the public interest, and represented a rational choice of the state agency charged with administering a program of limited resources.

Southland Corp. v. Edison


Nos. C-2825-86, L-5351-86PW


Superior Court of New Jersey, Law and Chancery Divisions, Middlesex County


217 N.J. Super. 158; 524 A.2d 1336; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1593



July 1, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 21, 1987.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs in the two consolidated actions, retail gasoline dealer and convenience food store operator, challenged on various grounds the constitutionality of a township ordinance that required plaintiffs' retail businesses to close between the hours of 12 a.m. and 6 a.m.


OVERVIEW: Based on a history of crime in the township, defendant township enacted an ordinance that prohibited gas stations and convenience stores from opening between the hours of 12 a.m. and 6 a.m., but permitting other retail establishments to remain open during those hours. Plaintiffs, an individual retail gasoline dealer and a convenience food stores operator, challenged the ordinance's validity. The court held that the ordinance was unenforceable as to plaintiff food store operator, because defendant failed to present evidence of a compelling public need in order to justify such a drastic measure. The court raised defendant's burden as to plaintiff food store because its impact was so prohibitory on that plaintiff. As to plaintiff retail gasoline dealer, the court held that the ordinance was overbroad, unreasonable and irrationally exceeded the public need.


OUTCOME: The court held that the ordinance was invalid as to one plaintiff because defendant township failed to prove a compelling public need to justify its impact on that plaintiff, and that, as to the other plaintiff, the ordinance was overbroad, unreasonable, and irrationally exceeded the public need.

Assocs. Commercial Corp. v. Wallia


No. A-3101-84T6


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


211 N.J. Super. 231; 511 A.2d 709; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1306


February 20, 1986, Submitted  
June 20, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 14, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant repair shop sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Camden County, which granted summary judgment on cross-motions in favor of plaintiff creditor involving the issue of priority between a perfected security interest under the Uniform Commercial Code and a garage-keeper's lien.


OVERVIEW: Defendant repair shop challenged a grant of summary judgment on cross-motions in favor of plaintiff creditor involving the issue of priority between a perfected security interest and a garage-keeper's lien on the repairs of a tractor. Defendants claimed that the garage-keeper's lien act, N. J. Stat. Ann. § 2A: 44-20-31, had previously been held unconstitutional in all respects, that it was entitled to an artisan's lien, and that plaintiff had been unjustly enriched at defendants' expense. The court held that the lien order of priorities embodied in § 2A: 44-21 was preserved and found no merit to defendant's contention that the act had been held unconstitutional in its entirety. Defendant contended that by making repairs to the tractor, it enhanced the vehicle's value and claimed an artisan's possessory lien. Because defendant conceded that the personal property was a motor vehicle, it could not claim an artisan's lien. Defendants could have anticipated that the vehicle was subject to a financing statement and taken steps to protect its position. Plaintiff was a bona fide extender of credit, which perfected its security interest. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant repair shop and in favor of plaintiff creditor involving the issue of priority between a perfected security interest and a garage-keeper's lien.The court held that the lien order of priorities embodied in the statute was preserved and found no merit to defendants' contention that the act had been held unconstitutional in its entirety and that plaintiff had perfected its security interest.

State v. Chappee


Nos. A-2442-84T4, A-3996-84T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


211 N.J. Super. 321; 511 A.2d 1197; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1328


June 9, 1986, Argued  
June 19, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 18, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Middlesex County, which convicted defendants of possession of a controlled substance with intent to distribute more than 3.5 grams of freebase cocaine and sentenced one to 20 years and the other defendant to seven years in a case brought by respondent, the state of New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged their convictions of possession of a controlled substance with intent to distribute more than 3.5 grams of freebase cocaine. Defendants contended that the trial court erred in its refusal to enforce the plea agreement. The court held that the pleas of guilty were not entered on the record before the state withdrew its offer and defendants were not prejudiced in asserting any defense by the state's change in position. Defendants argued for relief based on underrepresentation of women grand jury forepersons. The court held that there was no intentional discrimination against women and was unable to see the slightest prejudice to defendants by reason of this underrepresentation. Defendants asserted that they were detained and questioned and were not given Miranda warnings before they were requested to consent to open the trunk. Knowledge of the right to be assisted by counsel and to remain silent had little bearing on the voluntariness of a consent to a search. Further, there was no constitutional right to select an attorney who was not a member of the New Jersey bar. The court affirmed the judgments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of defendants convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to distribute in a case brought by respondent, the state of New Jersey. The court held that guilty pleas were not on the record before the state withdrew its offer, that defendants were not prejudiced by the lack of women on the jury, and that there was no constitutional right to select an out-of-state attorney.

Johns-Manville Sales Corp. v. N.J. Water Supply Auth.

May 13, 1986, Argued  
June 5, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 26, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Water Supply Authority.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant manufacturer sought review of a decision of respondent New Jersey Water Supply Authority, which imposed certain water use charges upon appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant manufacturer had been diverting water from a river along a tract of land owned by appellant for many years. The water was used and then returned to the river in virtually the same condition as when it was taken. Respondent New Jersey Water Supply Authority began imposing a user fee on appellant for the use of the water pursuant to N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7, § 11-2.2. On appeal, the court affirmed respondent's decision and held that appellant did not own the water flowing by its property. Instead, that water was owned by the public. Thus, respondent had the authority to impose the water use charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent New Jersey Water Supply Authority, which imposed certain water use charges on appellant manufacture because respondent was statutorily authorized to fix and collect charges for water and services provided by it.

 

1179 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Breakiron


No. A-2308-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


210 N.J. Super. 442; 510 A.2d 80; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1259


November 7, 1985, Argued  
May 22, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 5, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, which convicted him of murder, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3(a)(1); second degree kidnapping, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:13-1(b), burglary, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:18-2 and third-degree theft of an automobile, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-3(a). Main issue on appeal was whether the trial judge erred in refusing to submit to the jury the defense of diminished capacity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant strangled his girl friend. They had been living together for about four months and planned to get married. The jury rejected defendant's insanity defense and found him guilty of murder, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3(a)(1); second degree kidnapping, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:13-1(b), burglary, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:18-2 and third-degree theft of an automobile, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:20-3(a). Two psychiatrists testified, one for each side. The defense psychiatrist testified that defendant suffered from schizophrenia, a mental disease that the psychiatrist believed rendered defendant unable to formulate an intent to knowingly or willfully to kill the victim. The trial judge refused to charge the jury on diminished capacity as a defense because the judge believed that the defense no longer was available. The court held that the present statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:4-2, required the trial judge to determine whether the evidence of diminished capacity was of sufficient substance to be admissible. If the trial judge was so persuaded, the evidence would have been admissible and state would be required to overcome it at trial beyond a reasonable doubt. The court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court which convicted defendant of murder, robbery, kidnapping, and burglary was affirmed. Evidence of diminished capacity was not of sufficient capacity to be admissible.

Thompson v. N.J. State Parole Bd.


No. A-130-84T6


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


210 N.J. Super. 107; 509 A.2d 241; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1243


September 30, 1985, Argued  
May 7, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 21, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the New Jersey State Parole Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from respondent New Jersey State Parole Board, which denied appellant parole and imposed a future eligibility term of 12 years pursuant to regulations adopted under the Parole Act of 1979 (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-123.45 et seq., and which denied appellant disclosure of documents considered in appellant's parole file.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder in 1968 and became eligible for parole in 1984. The New Jersey State Parole Board (board) denied appellant disclosure of documents it considered in appellant's parole file and appellant was denied parol. Pursuant to regulations that had been adopted under the Parole Act of 1979 (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-123.45 et seq., the board imposed a future parole eligibility term. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed. The court found that imposing future parole eligibility pursuant to regulations adopted under the Act had not been ex post facto even though the Act was enacted 11 years after appellant's conviction. The court held the imposition of future parole eligibility had not been ex post facto because the regulations adopted under the Act had not been more onerous than those in effect at the time of appellant's offense. The court found that the nondisclosure of documents in appellant's parole file had not been improper because the documents had not played any substantial role in producing the adverse decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment denying appellant parole and imposing a future eligibility term because the New Jersey State Parole Board had not made an ex post facto application of the regulations adopted under the Parole Act of 1979 (Act). The court also affirmed a judgment denying appellant disclosure of documents considered in appellant's parole file because the withheld documents had not played a substantial role in the parol denial.

 

1181 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Atlantic City Mun. Utils. Auth. v. Hunt


No. A-2481-84T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


210 N.J. Super. 76; 509 A.2d 225; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1252; 17 ELR 20396


December 18, 1985, Submitted  
May 2, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff municipal utilities authority contested an order of the Superior Court (New Jersey), which granted defendant New Jersey Spill Compensation Fund administrator's motion for summary judgment on the parties' cross-motions, in plaintiff's action under the Spill Compensation and Control Act of 1976, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10-23.11 et seq., to recover cleanup and removal costs incurred due to environmental hazards created at a landfill.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff municipal utilities authority challenged the trial court's order in favor of defendant New Jersey Spill Compensation Fund administrator on the parties' cross-motions for summary judgment in plaintiff's action seeking a declaration that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10-23.11g(a) of the Spill Compensation and Control Act (Spill Act) of 1976, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10-23.11 et seq., entitled it to damages for cleaning up a pre-Spill Act discharge. Plaintiff contended that defendant was strictly liable, that it was entitled to landfill cleanup and removal costs, and that the trial court erred in finding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10-23.11g(a) was prospective except as to the Department of Environmental Protection's claims for cleanup and removal costs for discharges occurring prior to the effective date of the Spill Act. The court affirmed the trial court's order, holding that § 58:10-23.11g(a) was prospective and excluded recovery for damages resulting from pre-Spill Act discharges, because the high cost of cleanup and the fact that the Spill Act was an innovative statute made it likely the legislature intended a cautious approach rather than an all-inclusive one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order affirming defendant New Jersey Spill Compensation Fund administrator's decision denying plaintiff municipal utilities authority's claim for landfill cleanup costs pursuant to the Spill Compensation and Control Act (Spill Act), and held that the Spill Act's strict liability provision was prospective and did not apply to pre-Spill Act discharges except as to the Department of Environmental Protection.

 

1182 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Barone v. Dep't of Human Servs., Div. of Medical Assistance & Health Servs., Etc


Nos. A-2689-84T6, A-2837-84T6


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


210 N.J. Super. 276; 509 A.2d 786; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1250


March 4, 1986, Argued  
April 24, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 16, 1986.
Certification granted Barone v. Department of Human Services, 104 N.J. 461, 517 A.2d 446, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 2184 (1986)
Affirmed by Barone v. Department of Human Services, Div. of Medical Assistance & Health Services, etc., 107 N.J. 355, 526 A.2d 1055, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 324 (1987)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from final decision of the Department of Human Services.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant disabled persons challenged the decision of the New Jersey Department of Human Services, which denied their applications for benefits under the Pharmaceutical Assistance to the Aged and Disabled program, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4D-20 et seq., because they did not receive federal social security disability benefits and were under the age of 65.


OVERVIEW: Appellant disabled persons applied for Pharmaceutical Assistance to the Aged and Disabled (PAAD), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4D-20 et seq., but were denied benefits because they were under age 65 and did not receive federal social security benefits. On appeal, the court held that appellee Department of Human Services did not err in interpreting N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4D-21 to require receipt of social security benefits as a prerequisite to receipt of PAAD. The eligibility regulations were based on fiscal necessity and were consistent with governing legislation, thus N.J. Admin. Code tit. 10, § 69A-6.2(a), which set forth the prerequisite, was valid. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4D-21 did not violate the equal protection provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV or N.J. Const. art. I, para. 1, because the state's ability to rely on social security administrative determinations was fundamental to the integrity of the PAAD program and its financial ability to provide benefits. Therefore, the classification excluding the disabled needy under 65 not receiving social security was rational. Administrative convenience or expense was a justifiable and rational basis for the prerequisite.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions to deny appellant disabled persons' applications for Pharmaceutical Assistance to the Aged and Disabled (PAAD), and held that the regulations requiring receipt of federal social security benefits as a prerequisite for PAAD were constitutional. The classification affecting entitlement to PAAD was not suspect, and the administrative convenience was a justifiable and rational basis for the prerequisite.

 

1183 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Goetaski


No. A-2707-84T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


209 N.J. Super. 362; 507 A.2d 751; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1229


February 20, 1986, Argued  
April 18, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Atlantic County, which affirmed his conviction by the municipal court for driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol, and denied his motion to suppress the evidence produced by the stop, claiming an unconstitutional stop and seizure of his person under the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: A state trooper observed defendant slowly driving his vehicle on the northbound shoulder of a highway, late at night, with his left-turn indicator flashing. After observing defendant operating his vehicle in this manner for one-tenth of a mile, the trooper stopped the vehicle. When the trooper approached the car and talked with the driver, he made observations which resulted in the charge and conviction for driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50. Defendant sought to suppress the evidence produced by the stop, claiming an unconstitutional stop and seizure of his person under the state and federal constitutions. Defendant's motion was denied and he was found guilty in his initial trial in the municipal court and was again found guilty after a trial de novo in the law division. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of his motion to suppress because the facts were unusual enough for the time and place to warrant the closer scrutiny of a momentary investigative stop and inquiry. The court refused to substitute its judicial hindsight for what appeared to be a sound, nonpretextual exercise of curbstone judgment by the officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence produced by a stop which led to his conviction for driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol because the officer had reason to believe the circumstances were enough beyond the ordinary, though not necessarily criminally suspicious, that the vehicle stop was constitutionally permissible.

 

1184 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Riorano, Inc. v. Weymouth Township


A-5543-83T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


209 N.J. Super. 280; 507 A.2d 311; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1210


November 12, 1985, Submitted  
April 15, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 24, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant township sought review of a decision of the Tax Court (New Jersey), which concluded that the Pinelands Protection Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:18A-1 et seq., demonstrated a substantial depressing influence and ordered tax assessments lowered from $ 774,200 to $ 573,188 for 1981 and $ 450,362 for 1982, in plaintiff landowners' appeal of their tax assessment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowners appealed their tax assessments. The lower court concluded that the Pinelands Protection Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:18A-1 et seq., demonstrated a substantial depressing influence and ordered tax assessments lowered from $ 774,200 to $ 572,188 for 1981 and $ 450,362 in 1982. On appeal, the court affirmed. The inconsistent speculation about whether there was any realistic possibility of the development of plaintiffs' lands, and whether any prospects for development influenced their value was because there was no certified local master plan and so it was impossible to say how many homesites plaintiffs were allowed to develop, or if any, or under what restrictions. The reason for that was that defendant failed to satisfy its statutory obligation to produce a master plan conforming with comprehensive management plan, and plaintiffs had not applied to the Pinelands Commission for permission to develop. In the absence of such evidence, the lower court was allowed to find that developability was so speculative an element as to have no influence on value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court, which held that an environmental act depressed plaintiff landowners' property and ordered his tax assessments lowered because, in the absence of evidence of consistent speculation about whether there was any realist possibility of the development of plaintiffs' lands, the lower court was allowed to find that developability was so speculative an element as to have no influence on value.

Bd. of Educ. v. Cooperman


A-605-85T5, A-1378-85T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


209 N.J. Super. 174; 507 A.2d 253; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1207


January 7, 1986, Argued  
March 25, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 15, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Commissioner of Education, the State Board of Education and the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school boards appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Union County and from the order of defendant New Jersey Commissioner of Education, respectively, that directed plaintiffs to admit kindergarten-aged students to regular classroom attendance who had been diagnosed with the AIDS/ARC and HLTV-III antibody, and challenged defendant's guidelines for such admissions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant New Jersey Commissioner of Education promulgated rules requiring the admission of students with the AIDS/ARC and HLTV-III antibody into regular classroom attendance, with specific, limited exceptions, and specifically directed plaintiff school boards to place certain kindergarten-aged students into the regular classroom. Plaintiffs filed law suits challenging the orders and the guidelines, with one of the cases adjudicated in favor of defendant, from which that plaintiff appealed, and the other being granted a leave to appeal.
