OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant New Jersey Commissioner of Education's orders directing plaintiff school boards to admit students that had been diagnosed with AIDS and remanded for hearings, as plaintiffs were not provided an opportunity to be heard and to present evidence, and defendant's guidelines regarding admission of students with AIDS was null and void, as defendant failed to comply with the Administrative Procedure Act.

N.J. Election Law Enforcement Com v. Citizens to Make Mayor-Council Gov't Work


A-5081-84T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


208 N.J. Super. 583; 506 A.2d 773; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1169


February 25, 1986, Submitted  
March 13, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 1, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Final Decision of the New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens group sought review of the final decision of respondent, New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Commission, that held that appellant was subject to the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Reporting Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-1 et seq., requiring the filing of a final campaign report in its efforts to force a recall election of the mayor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant citizens group organized to secure signatures to force the recall election of the mayor. Respondent New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Commission held that appellant was a political committee within the meaning of the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Reporting Act (act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-1 et seq., and that it was subject to the reporting requirements of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-8- 16. The court held that appellant was subject to the act because the placement of the recall question on the ballot was part and parcel of the passage of the question. The court held that the collection of signatures and filing of a petition aided or promoted the passage of a public question. The court held that the petition process was as much a part of the overall electoral process as the voting itself. The court held that to campaign to get a public question on a ballot was to promote its passage. However, the court reversed the fine respondent assessed against appellant because the court's decision was prospective only because appellant may not have understood that the petition for recall was a public question.


OUTCOME: The court reversed respondent commission's decision that fined appellant citizens group for failure to file a final campaign report in its efforts to force a recall election of the mayor. The court held that appellant was subject to the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Reporting Act. However, it was not subject to the fine because the court's decision was prospective only.

State v. Fernandez


A-5846-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


209 N.J. Super. 37; 506 A.2d 1245; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1178


January 14, 1986, Submitted  
March 5, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 1, 1986.
Certification denied by State v. Fernandez, 109 N.J. 481, 537 A.2d 1275, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 505 (1987)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Somerset County, denying his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sex crimes and sentenced pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:164-6 of the Sex Offender Act (repealed), to a diagnostic and treatment center for indeterminate terms not to exceed 30 years. Five years later, defendant sought to be resentenced pursuant to the provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:1-1d(2) of the New Jersey Code of Criminal Justice (Code), claiming that he qualified for a sentence reduction. His application was denied. Defendant alleged that the prohibition against his earning commutation time for good behavior and work performed, which was contained in § 2A:164-6, was no longer applicable to him because the statute was expressly repealed and § 2C:1-1d(2) was meant to control his treatment. The court held that at the time of the imposition of defendant's sentence, there existed an express prohibition on the award of commutation credits to sex offenders, and awarding those credits later would have undermined the legislative purpose of the provision. The court affirmed and held that defendant's equal protection rights were not violated because he was not a member of the same class or similarly situated to persons serving sentences under the Code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief because defendant was sentenced under an act that prohibited the award of commutation credits to sex offenders, and he was not a member of the class of persons serving sentences under the New Jersey Code of Criminal Justice, which allowed the credits.

State v. Tischio


A-2804-84T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


208 N.J. Super. 343; 506 A.2d 14; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1146


January 28, 1986, Argued  
February 26, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 5, 1986.
Certification denied by State v. Tischio, 104 N.J. 420, 517 A.2d 416, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 2162 (1986)
Certification granted State v. Tischio, 105 N.J. 518, 523 A.2d 163, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 2204 (1986)
Affirmed by State v. Tischio, 107 N.J. 504, 527 A.2d 388, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 330 (1987)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Middlesex County (New Jersey), which affirmed his conviction by the municipal court of driving with a blood alcohol concentration of .10 percent or more in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50(a).


OVERVIEW: An hour after defendant was stopped for driving in an erratic manner, he was given a breathalyzer exam which revealed that he had a .11 percent blood alcohol level. Affirming defendant's conviction for driving with a blood alcohol concentration of .10 percent or more in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50(a), the court held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in admitting the breathalyzer inspection certificates because they were admissible as an exception to the hearsay rule and were properly authenticated. The court also held that the statute was constitutional and that the state proved the necessary elements of its case. The court reasoned that it was not necessary for the state to prove defendant's blood alcohol level at the time when he was driving because such an interpretation, although within the literal terms of the statute, produced anomalous results not intended by the legislature. The court found that the statute focused on the operation of a vehicle when there was sufficient alcohol in the driver's system to produce the proscribed reading so long as there was no further ingestion of alcohol between the time of operation and the time of testing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision affirming defendant's conviction for driving with a blood alcohol concentration of .10 percent or more because the state proved the necessary elements of its case by showing that defendant's blood alcohol concentration was .11 percent one hour after he operated the vehicle and that there had been no further ingestion of alcohol between the time of operation and the time of testing.

In re N.J.A.C. 11:1-20


Nos. A-932-85T1; Consolidated with A-1176-85T1

February 3, 1986, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the adoption of a regulation by the Commissioner of Insurance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the administrative adoption of N.J. Admin. Code tit. 11, §§ 1 et seq., by appellee Commissioner of Insurance (New Jersey), in an action seeking a judgment invalidating the regulation as arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, insurance industry organizations, filed complaints against appellee insurance commissioner, seeking judgments invalidating N.J. Admin. Code tit. 11, §§ 1 et seq., as arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable. The appeals were consolidated under, initially, an emergency basis and then a normal rule-making basis of the Administrative Procedure Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 52:14B-1 et seq. Adoption of the rule on a normal basis cured the minor procedural defects in the emergency adoption and thus justified upholding the rule ab initio. Administrative rules were accorded a presumption of reasonableness, and appellants did not meet their burden of demonstrating that the adopted regulation was arbitrary, capricious, unduly onerous, or otherwise unreasonable.

Seals v. Langston Co.


A-2551-84T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


206 N.J. Super. 408; 502 A.2d 1185; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1103


December 9, 1985, Argued  
January 13, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 28, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administratrix sought review of a summary judgment from the Superior Court, Camden County (New Jersey), entered in favor of respondent manufacturer on the ground that Louisiana's one-year statute of limitations applied to appellant's action for damages for injuries and death of a Louisiana resident caused in Louisiana by an allegedly defective machine manufactured in New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: Appellant administratrix's decedent was killed in Louisiana in an accident involving a machine made in New Jersey by respondent manufacturer. Appellant commenced suit in Louisiana against a party that did not make the machine. The Louisiana court entered summary judgment for the party on that basis. When appellant ascertained the true manufacturer, Louisiana's one-year statute of limitations barred suit in that state. Appellant commenced an action against respondent within the period permitted by New Jersey's two-year statute of limitations, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-2. The trial court granted respondent's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the action. The court affirmed the dismissal, holding that the trial court correctly determined that Louisiana's one-year statute of limitations governed the action. The court concluded that Louisiana's statute applied because its interest in the action outweighed New Jersey's interest. The parties were all present in or amenable to Louisiana's jurisdiction. The fact that respondent manufactured the allegedly faulty machine in New Jersey did not create an interest sufficient for application of New Jersey's statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of respondent manufacturer in appellant administratrix's action for damages and death of a Louisiana resident caused in Louisiana by an allegedly defective machine manufactured in New Jersey. The trial court correctly determined that Louisiana's one-year statute of limitations applied to the action because Louisiana's interest in the action outweighed New Jersey's interest.

State v. Rhoda


A-2140-82T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


206 N.J. Super. 584; 503 A.2d 364; 1986 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1094


November 25, 1985, Submitted  
January 6, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 22, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Somerset County (New Jersey), which, in connection with defendant's sentence for a series of thefts, increased a prior order of restitution after the prior order was reversed on appeal. Defendant argued that increase of the order constituted double jeopardy, and violated his plea bargain.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to a series of thefts and in sentencing defendant, the trial court ordered restitution. After the court reversed and remanded the restitution order, the trial court increased the order in implementing the remand instructions, and defendant again appealed, arguing that increase of the order constituted double jeopardy, and violated his plea bargain. The court affirmed and ruled that double jeopardy principles did not apply to restitution because restitution was not technically punishment for a crime. The court ruled that, although restitution had aspects of rehabilitation and deterrence, which were also aspects of punishment, it was predominantly nonpenal in nature, and thus there was no constitutional infringement by an increase in restitution after appeal. The court also ruled that the plea agreement did not address the issue of restitution, nor was it required to be addressed by a plea agreement, although the better practice would have been for the trial court to have addressed the matter in the colloquy at the time the plea was accepted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order requiring defendant to pay restitution in his sentencing for a series of thefts. The court ruled that the increase of restitution did not constitute an unconstitutional double jeopardy because restitution was not technically punishment of a crime. The court also ruled that the restitution did not abridge the terms of defendant's plea agreement.

 

1192 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. A-3771-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


206 N.J. Super. 341; 502 A.2d 1149; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1592


November 19, 1985, Submitted  
December 19, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 21, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant was convicted of felony-murder, he sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Hudson County (New Jersey), sentencing him to a 30-year minimum incarceration without parole eligibility as mandated by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3b.


OVERVIEW: This appeal involved the issue of whether the 30-year minimum sentence without parole eligibility mandated by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3b for felony murder convictions was constitutional. Appellant was convicted of felony-murder for stabbing a woman to death during a robbery. He was sentenced to a minimum term of 30 years during which he would not be eligible for parole. On review, appellant argued that the statute establishing the minimum sentence violated the federal and state constitutions' prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. The court disagreed. According to the court, when applying the tests for cruel and unusual punishment, which have been judicially created, to the sentencing provision of the New Jersey statute, the proper inquiry was whether the 30-year mandatory minimum sentence for murder went beyond what was necessary to accomplish any legitimate penal aim, or if it was a reasonable expedient to achieve the public purpose that could be deduced from the legislation. Here, the court affirmed the sentence imposed because it concluded that the 30-year requirement met these tests and found that the statute was therefore constitutional.


OUTCOME: Appellant's 30-year minimum sentence for felony-murder as required by New Jersey statute was affirmed because the court concluded that the statute did not violate either the state or federal constitution in that the punishment was a reasonable expedient to achieve the legitimate penal purpose.

N.J. Election Law Enforcement Com v. Brown


A-2521-84T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


206 N.J. Super. 206; 502 A.2d 59; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1583


November 18, 1985, Argued  
December 12, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 3, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school board members challenged the decision of the New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Commission, which adopted the findings of the administrative law judge that front page, laudatory, noncritical profiles of appellants aided their reelection efforts and constituted campaign contributions. A fine was imposed on appellants.


OVERVIEW: Appellant school board members running for reelection were interviewed by an independent newsletter. The front page article provided laudatory and noncritical profiles of appellants and nothing about the other six school board members. The administrative law judge (ALJ) concluded that the front page coverage aided appellants' reelection efforts and unmistakably urged their reelections upon the eligible electorate. As such, they were campaign contributions, under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-11. The New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Commission (ELEC) adopted the ALJ's findings and imposed $ 50 fines against appellants for failure to report campaign contributions exceeding $ 100 in value, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-16(e). The court affirmed, holding that a campaign contribution reporting obligation arose under the circumstance of appellants' participation in the development of their laudatory, noncritical front page article, coupled with the timing of the publication during the school board election campaign.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Commission which imposed a fine on appellant school board members because laudatory, noncritical profiles of them aided their reelection efforts and constituted campaign contributions. The court held that a contribution reporting obligation arose when appellants participated in the development of those profiles, which were published during a school board election campaign.

State in Interest of G.W.


A-5814-84T5; A-5358-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


206 N.J. Super. 50; 501 A.2d 1012; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1566


October 23, 1985, Argued  
December 5, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 20, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Sussex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juveniles sought review of the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Sussex County, which waived jurisdiction and referred them for trial as adults pursuant to N. J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:4A-26. Appellants, who were charged with murder, robbery, burglary of two homes, and aggravated sexual assault, claimed that the lower court erred in waiving jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juveniles were charged with conduct that if committed by adults would constitute murder, robbery, burglary of two victim's home, and aggravated sexual assault. The lower court held a detention hearing at which it determined that there was probable cause to believe that appellants committed the alleged conduct. The juvenile court referred appellants to the law division for trial as adults because they did not show that it was likely that they would be rehabilitated by age 19 under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:4A-26. Appellants challenged this ruling and the court affirmed. One appellant argued that § 2A:4A-26 unconstitutionally required him to disprove facts that supported waiver, because the facts were also the elements of the offense. The court disagreed, holding that the statutes upon which that appellant relied in support of his claim applied to the criminal, but not the juvenile code. The court rejected the argument that the trial court erred in denying appellants an evidentiary hearing before it waived jurisdiction because the trial court reviewed the record of the detention hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order referring appellant juveniles for trial as adults for conduct which, if committed by an adult, would constitute murder, robbery, burglary of two homes, and aggravated sexual assault. The statute that authorized waiver of jurisdiction was not unconstitutional, and the lower court gave appellants a sufficient opportunity to present evidence before it waived jurisdiction.

Ann. § 2C:33-2(b), if he were an adult. Appellant allegedly addressed a police officer with profane language, the only purpose of which was to offend the officer, in effect, to exact verbal vengeance for his arrest. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction, holding that prosecutions of speech, based solely on the fact that the speech offended the sensibilities of the listener, were unconstitutional.

1196 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Portock


A-5733-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


205 N.J. Super. 499; 501 A.2d 551; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1552


October 23, 1985, Argued  
November 20, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 11, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a decision by the Superior Court of Atlantic County (New Jersey), which dismissed indictments against defendants because the prosecutor's opening statements were insufficient.


OVERVIEW: An indictment charged defendants with conspiracy, unlawful interception of an oral communication of another, and complicity. A jury was sworn, and the prosecutor and defense counsel gave opening statements. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the indictment because the prosecutor's opening was insufficient. The court granted defendants' motion, and the state appealed. The reviewing court found that a prosecutor was required to make an opening statement in a criminal action but that there were no requirements as to what the opening should state. The court noted that criminal cases should not be decided prematurely because a dismissal on the opening was not appealable and would preclude retrial on double jeopardy grounds. The state contended that because the judge ruled on matters of law only, retrial was not prohibited and that, even if the defendants technically were acquitted because the jury was not discharged, no retrial was required. The court held that the dismissal of the indictments acquitted defendants of the charges and that the jury had been impaneled and sworn. Therefore, double jeopardy had attached, and the appeal was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The state's appeal was dismissed because the dismissal of defendants' indictments acquitted defendants of the charges after impaneling of the jury, resulting in attachment of double jeopardy protection.

 

1197 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Hilton Int'l Co. v. Ginsburg


A-2774-84T6


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


207 N.J. Super. 1; 503 A.2d 879; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1614


October 22, 1985, Argued  
November 20, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant individual appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which struck defendant's statute of limitations defense and granted summary judgment to plaintiff hotel based on plaintiff's claim that a Puerto Rico judgment was entitled to full faith and credit under U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant individual appealed the striking of his statute of limitations defense and the summary judgment granted in favor of plaintiff hotel based on plaintiff's claim that a Puerto Rico judgment was entitled to full faith and credit. The court reversed and dismissed plaintiff's complaint. The court found that defendant's limitations defense was properly stricken because N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:82-4.3, the limitations statute, violated the Full Faith and Credit Clause of U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1. Next, the court found that the Puerto Rico judgment was defective and not entitled to full faith and credit and that no New Jersey judgment should have been based upon it. Full faith and credit was available only to judgments based upon notice that was reasonably calculated to have apprised defendant of the action's pendency and that afforded defendant an opportunity to present a defense. Defendant's notice was defective because it did not include an English translation. Moreover, plaintiff's counsel had default judgment entered despite having a copy of defendant's answer and knowing that defendant planned to oppose the claim, and courts could vacate judgments procured by mistake or fraud.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and dismissed plaintiff hotel's complaint. Although the lower court properly struck defendant individual's limitations defense as unconstitutional, the trial court erred in giving a Puerto Rico judgment full faith and credit where notice of the action lacked an English translation and did not reasonably apprise defendant of the action's pendency and afford him an opportunity to present a defense.

Prb Enters. v. S. Brunswick Planning Bd.


A-432-84T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


205 N.J. Super. 225; 500 A.2d 732; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1523


October 9, 1985, Argued  
November 8, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 20, 1985.
Certification granted PRB Enterprises, Inc. v. South Brunswick Planning Bd., 103 N.J. 488, 511 A.2d 663, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 1152 (1986)
Affirmed by PRB Enterprises, Inc. v. South Brunswick Planning Bd., 105 N.J. 1, 518 A.2d 1099, 1987 N.J. LEXIS 264 (1987)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board appealed after the trial court (New Jersey) reversed its denial of preliminary and final site plan approval to build a convenience store.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff company sought site plan approval for a convenience store. Defendant board denied preliminary and final approval because the store was not "low traffic generating," as required by the preamble to the ordinance. The trial court reversed and granted final site plan approval. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the preamble could neither limit nor extend the meaning of a statute that was clear on its face, and that the term "low traffic generating" lacked interpretative standards. The court held that the power to deny a site plan because of traffic was an exercise of the zoning power vested in the municipal governing body, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-2, 62. The court held that the convenience store was a permitted use, which required preliminary site plan approval. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-46b. The court affirmed the trial court's order insofar as it granted preliminary site plan approval, but reversed and remanded to the trial court for imposition of reasonable conditions (such as parking, loading, and traffic restrictions, including the pro rata share of any street improvements) insofar as the order granted final site plan approval.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court order that reversed defendant board's order, which denied plaintiff's company's petition for preliminary and final site plan approval of a convenience store. The court held that the store was a permitted use and that preliminary site plan approval was required, but remanded the action for imposition of reasonable conditions insofar as the order granted final site plan approval.

 

1199 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Promulgation of N.J.A.C. 13:35-6.14


A-3919-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


205 N.J. Super. 492; 501 A.2d 547; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1553


September 19, 1985, Argued  
October 17, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 11, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Promulgation of a Regulation by New Jersey State Board of Medical Examiners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, The American Physical Therapy Association, New Jersey Chapter, appealed from the promulgation of a regulation, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13, § 35-6.14, by defendant, New Jersey State Board of Medical Examiners. Plaintiff contended that the regulation was ultra vires since the authority to regulate the actions of medical assistants performing physical therapy functions rested solely with plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the promulgation of N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13, § 35-6.14 by defendant New Jersey State Board of Medical Examiners, plaintiff, The American Physical Therapy Association, New Jersey Chapter, contended that because the definition of physical therapy in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:9-37.14a had previously been held constitutional, the regulation of the actions of medical assistants performing functions which would fit the definitions of physical therapy was under its exclusive jurisdiction. The court disagreed and affirmed the promulgation of the regulation. The court held that the regulation in question clearly governed an aspect of the practice of medicine, i.e., the delegation of the use of simple modalities of physical therapy as part of medical treatment within the physician's office. This aspect of medicine was similar to, but yet different, from the unsupervised application of physical therapy by a licensed physical therapist exercising professional judgment. Further, defendant was empowered pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:9-2 to provide standards for the practice of medicine. Therefore, defendant had jurisdiction to promulgate the challenged regulation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the action of defendant, New Jersey Board of Medical Examiners, in adopting N.J. Admin. Code. tit. 13, § 35-6.14. The court held that although the regulation addressed certain activities that fit the definition of physical therapy, it also clearly governed an aspect of the practice of medicine, and therefore, plaintiff, The American Physical Therapy Association, New Jersey Chapter, did not have exclusive jurisdiction.

 

1200 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Grasso v. Borough Council of Glassboro


A-5364-83T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


205 N.J. Super. 18; 500 A.2d 10; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1504


September 10, 1985, Argued  
October 16, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 7, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Gloucester County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Law Division, Gloucester County (New Jersey), affirming defendants', mayor and city council's, dismissal of plaintiff as their acting chief of police based upon disciplinary charges and plaintiff's alleged interference with an ongoing criminal investigation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, who was the acting chief of police, was dismissed by defendants, the mayor and city council, after disciplinary charges were brought against him. Plaintiff was found guilty of interfering with an ongoing criminal investigation. The trial court affirmed plaintiff's dismissal. The court reversed, holding that the amendment to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:14-150 did not limit de novo hearings to the record before the disciplinary board, but permitted a party to supplement the record with additional testimony at a de novo hearing. Therefore, the trial court erred in precluding plaintiff from presenting additional testimony at his hearing. Furthermore, defendants had no authority under a city ordinance to conduct the disciplinary hearing at which plaintiff was dismissed. Such authority was vested in the director or in the disciplinary board selected from among the members of the police force.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of plaintiff as the acting chief of police was reversed because the trial court erred in precluding the presentation of additional testimony at the trial court level hearing. Furthermore, the authority to conduct the disciplinary hearing in the first place was not vested in defendant mayor and city council, but in the police disciplinary board.
